de la hainche	I'm not sure what you are asking. The term "de la hainche" does not appear in the text provided. Could you please clarify your request or provide more context?
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When humid vapors descend to the joint of the hip, and for this reason it moves out of its place, and one sign is that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and the location of the separation is visible, then you should cauterize the patient on the hip bone with a cautery similar to a circle, and mark before the separation around the joint as it turns, so that the hip bone is within the circle; and let the cauteries be such as those used for stomaching.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if these cauteries are not present, make three cauteries of large olives, and let the cauteries be as deep as all hearts; and heal it until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	for the pain of the hip.
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the joint of the hip, and it is due to cold and moisture, and the patient has been treated for what we have said in the division but the treatment does not work, and the illness is old: then you should purge the patient of heavy humors with fetid pills or other good similar ones.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	 Afterward, he performs cautery; and the types of cautery are according to two methods: namely, hot irons and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	 The fire cautery is of many methods, one of which is as follows: you cauterize on the boil of the swelling three triangular irons in this shape, and make them of good depth and large, and let there be between each iron a space the width of a finger, and let the irons be olive-shaped; sometimes a single iron is placed in the middle on top of the swelling's chief, for which reason there are four in this shape.
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you wish, cauterize with the circular cautery that we mentioned earlier for the dislocation of the edema; but do it in such a way that the circle encompasses the entire swelling, and all the flesh of the area is burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	 And this is the method used in sciatica, when the pain stays only in the swelling and does not reach either the thigh or the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	 And if it reaches the thigh and the leg, make two fire cauteries where the patient says the pain is located, and four cauteries above the ankle on the inner side; let the cauteries be knife-like, and let the thickened part of the flesh be burned; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to the toes or near them, cauterize it where they feel the pain three or four times with the cautery called "points.
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if necessary, more may be done; and if the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, then a sharp-edged or circular cautery should be applied, and take great care in all your cauterizations that you do not leave the cautery on for too long so as to burn the nerves and major arteries, and that you do not cause greater harm and contraction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	 And I myself have seen several people who made a cautery on the ankle of the foot, and they let it go for so long that the leg swelled up completely, as did the foot, and the entire foot became pierced and rotten.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	 After a stomach operation which led to his death.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	 And if the pain is in two adjacent parts, perform cautery on one and then the other, in the following manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	 And the physicians said in the cautery for an abscess, this is the method - make such a iron and let it be as thick at the tip as a little finger of a hand, or just a bit less, and let there be interlacing between them with the space of a nut's width from one to the other; and let the interlacings be turned in two parts, and let them be like knots, and let there be one well-made iron rod; and this is its form.
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Heat it until it is completely red and drips sparks, then place it on the boil of the inflamed patient, and turn it on the healthy side; and cauterize once with one cautery, and leave it for three days; then make a poultice of butter, and leave the wound open for a long time; after that, cure it with ointment until it heals.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Al-Zahrawi (Albucasis) says that we use little of this cautery because of the fear of its appearance, and I myself have seen few who use it; but nonetheless, this is one of the good cauteries, which can endure it, and where it is applied.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	 The cautery of burning medicine is such that you make an interlaced instrument in which the edge of the opening descends, and it should be made of brass or iron on one side, and be long, and at its height have two knobs, and let there be between each the thickness of a thumb; and let them be overturned both below and above, and let them come together in this form.
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	 After place the box of the groin on the sick patient lying on a healthy, clean side, and then press firmly with your hand on the box of the groin; after pour between the two circles of the awl hot water that has been heated by fire one pot, and let it stay for an hour in length, and allow the patient to endure the heat and burning of it.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 For it causes a burning sensation as from fire; and when the burning sensation has passed, lift your hand with the instrument and gently raise the groin away from the awl, and leave it in this manner for three days, and apply butter until the blackened area from the burn is removed; and let it be left alone for three days until pus drains out; and this would be the final treatment after the cure of poultices until it has healed.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	 And if the pain has extended to the thigh or leg, make an instrument that matches what you have done in the hip enlargement; and this is the method of hot cauterization, which I have written in the treatise on the correction of medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	 Take alkaline and quicklime, equal amounts of one as the other, and grind them together, and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	 which has a small hole in it so that the tip of a razor can enter; and place another pot, well soldered, over it; and put sulfur and lime and soft cautery on top, until there are two fingers' width of powder above the pots when you have thoroughly coated your hand with it; and leave it like this until the mixture cools down and becomes solid in the soldered pot, then take all the mixture and cast it back onto the lime and sulfur as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	 And then it will be very weak and is fed with medical work and cauteries of other limbs because it does the same work as fire, and there are other medicines with which one cauterizes inflammation, such as hedgehog fat and gum, and lime with soap, all mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	 And Galen tells us of a cure through which a man was cured of the pain of inflammation and sciatic pain, and he praised it highly, saying that no other treatment was done, and that he was cured in one go when this treatment was administered, and he bathed as is taught hereafter.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	 And he says in this way that you take fresh and dry litharge (lead monoxide), grind it well with a little bit of fat, and apply it to the inflammation and on the thigh and calf where the pain resides, and bind it; and leave it for three hours and until the patient no longer feels the burning sensation.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	 And then make him enter the bath until his body is somewhat heated, and make him enter the bed, and the pain will go away completely and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	 And know that no one should use such a fire cautery unless it is after the evacuation of humors.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	 And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat's grease, it helps greatly; and the cautery should be done in this manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	 Take wool and soak it in old oil, and place it on the depression which is between the thumb of the foot and the other one called foscile.[Note: The translation of "foscile" is not certain, as it may refer to a specific part of the foot that is not commonly referred to in modern anatomy. It is unclear what exact location is meant by this term in the original text.]
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	 Afterwards, take dry goat's dung, heat it on fire until it becomes coals, and place it on wool, leaving it until it becomes ashes; and repeat this process, not stopping until you think that it will reach the swelling, and that the pain has ceased; and this method of cautery is called "cautery of goat.
de la dolor dou dos	of the back pain
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, either from falling, or from being struck, or from excessive evacuation, or from an expanded cold substance, no form of cautery is effective for these cases, except for that which results from the infusion of a cold substance.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	After the patient has been purged with fetid pills or other similar substances, three lines should be signed on the back, where the pain is located, using ink; and in each line there should be five cauteries or more, according to the strength and quantity that the patient can endure; and let the cauterizations be done using the type of cautery known as "poins"; and if you wish, perform three or four cauterizations using the clavile moien method, in this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This illness often comes to young children, and the signs of its onset are that they have stiffness in their limbs when they get up, and fear; and you will find in the spine of the back, near the base, an appearance which rises above the other vertebrae.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and wish to cure it, cauterize it using the cautery of this kind, in this form:
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	 Such that the cautery reaches every part of the spine equally.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	 And if you wish, cauterize around the spine with the cautery, making two or three lines and keeping them close to each other.[« Et si tu veux, ainsi cautérise autour de la colonne vertébrale avec le cautère en faisant deux ou trois lignes, et qu’elles soient rapprochées les unes des autres. »>
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	 Afterwards, keep the area clean and healthy until it is healed, as we have said; and be careful not to apply fire cautery to a gouty swelling in a nerve span.
de la dolor des jointes	of joint pain
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When joint pain comes from humors that are spread throughout every member of the body, and when it occurs in the feet (which people commonly call "gout"), and when it results from a cold cause and cannot be cured by medicines, it should be treated with cauterization in this manner: make many cautery marks around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	 And if it is necessary to apply cautery to the sole of the foot, use the entire "point"-claimed cautery on the face.
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	 And if the pain extends to the knees and other joints, which happens frequently, apply three or four cauteries with an olive-shaped tip to each knee on both sides; and if more is needed, do so, but be careful not to hold the cautery for too long that the flesh burns too deeply.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	 And if the pains descend down to the knee and back, administer the cautery as we have said in its chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	 And if the pains are in the hands, make incisions around the wrist two lines deep; and if there is no more pain, make incisions on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come down to the wrists or shoulders, cauterize each part, and provide good care to the patient and give them medicine.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	 For if you take good care of them and purge the phlegm, they will be healed with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the syphilis sore
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When an abscess comes to a head and the bowels descend to the hips and it is recent, then when you see that it needs to be cured, they must not eat that day; and they should use things that lighten the belly so that feces descend from their stomach; after, make them sit on their back between your hands, and command them to hold their breath until the abscess has receded, and massage it with your fingers, and apply pressure beneath the abscess up to the bone of the hip, and in such a way that it forms half of a circle above the body; then heat the cautery of which this is the shape: [The text here refers to a figure or illustration which would have accompanied the text but is not present in this version. The text continues with instructions on how to use the heated cautery.]
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	 until it is white and excretes pus.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	 Then return the bowels to their place; and the minister places his hand so that they do not return backward; and works well the thighs for the patient, and puts a cushion and a servant beneath the thighs, and another on the stomach who holds the hands; then place the cautery on the sign with your entire hand, and hold it straight and steady until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, start again until you come to the bone; and carefully watch that the bowels do not protrude when you apply the cautery; so as not to burn; and so that through this the patient does not die, or other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	 And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your efforts are in vain.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	 And it is necessary that the cauteries for children be fine, according to the measure of eggs, and also large for larger people, according to their measure; after three days cure the place of the caution with butter until the burn is removed; after cure other applications until it is healed, and let the patient lie down for 40 days until the wound is well healed; and it is necessary that his bandages be left on long enough, so that the boils do not swell when he takes a walk in chambers.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	 And after 40 days, when he wishes to get up, prepare a well-made belt for him and let him wear it for another 40 days; and have good rest, that he works little and guards against excessive consumption of drink and food, and high voices; and when he follows this teaching, he will be fully healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	 And I will say hereafter the cure of cutting in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of intestinal perforation or rupture
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	 When ruptures come in other bellies and are recognized, and you see that they do not grow anymore, perform the fire cautery of the returning cautery according to its quantity, and let a third of the intestines be burned; after that, cure according to what we have said; and some of the ancients have said that it should be cauterized with the three-angled cautery in this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	 but first mark the location of the rupture and make a line above it according to its width, and another below, and place your hand in the middle of the entire cautery claw.[additional text](Note: The translation is meant to be an interpretation of the Old French text provided and should not be taken as definitive or professional medical advice. The use of medieval medical practices such as cauterization can be dangerous and should only be performed by trained medical professionals in a modern medical setting.)
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	 But the first cautery is lighter and more subtle.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of ancient pain in some limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	 When pain comes to any limb, either from falling or being struck, and this pain lasts for a long time, and medical treatment is unsuccessful, then it is necessary to cauterize with the "pointed" cautery, and let the cautery be according to the length of the member, its smallness, weakness, and strength, as well as its location in terms of twists and pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	 If it heals from the first cautery, that is good; but if not, begin another cautery on top of it, for it is often the case that it must change to the member that is near it, therefore you must continue with the cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	of leprosy.
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	 The eyelids are sometimes helped by cautery with great aid, and likewise the diseases that come from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	 If you wish to cauterize, take care if the disease is at its beginning, and if it has been cured according to what we have said in the division, and if it does not subside or remain, and you doubt that the corruption will spread throughout the patient; then perform V cauteries on the head: one at the forehead, and the other towards the front at the end of the hairline; and II on the two temples, and one behind on the occiput; and leave your hand in such a way that the cautery reaches the bone, and so much that the scabs come out, allowing the vapors of the thick humors to escape; and cauterize on the affected area according to what it looks like.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the malady is spread everywhere and it is clearly lost, then you should cauterize it with the cauteries that we have mentioned in the head, and one cautery on the nose, and two cauteries on the spine of the neck, and three cauteries on the spine of the back, and one large one on the haunch and another next to it, and two on the shoulders; and two on the hips, and two on the tendons of the arms, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and be careful not to burn the nerves that are at the back of the heels; and sometimes make a cautery on the bone of the thumb, and one another on the bone of the stomach, and one another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	 And know that the more I do with fire cautery, the more help I provide, and the more it benefits; and know that the patient does not feel pain from the cautery as a healthy person does, because the body is already entirely corrupt.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	 And it is necessary that the fire cautery be large or small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you will find in the ways of iron.[Note: I'm assuming "manieres des fers" refers to different types or shapes of irons used for cauterization. ]
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	 After the treatment, dust the area with a mixture of barley flour and honey, along with other cures, until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When swelling occurs in a limb and is treated with medicines, oils, and poultices but does not heal, then cauterization should be performed on the limb according to its size; and let the cautery penetrate somewhat into the thickness of the flesh; then cure it with ointments until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	 And sometimes, a fire cautery is done on the hand, foot, and back, at the exit of the nerve that moves the member, and in this way, swelling is removed; but no one should meddle with it if they are not knowledgeable about the members and the exits of the moving nerves of the body.
de albaras	of ulcers/sores
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" has woken up, and the means of medicine are worth nothing, then cauterize it with a cautery somewhat deeply, according to the thickness of the flesh, until the whiteness is removed and its color changed; then cure it with flour of vetch and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and the blood of a swallow and a lark, each of one part; and mix everything together, and bind it with a cloth, and let it air in place until it heals.
li cure de chancre par cautere	the treatment of cancer (chancre) by cauterization
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	 When a chancre first appears and you want to stop it, cauterize it with a fire cautery that forms a circle, all around the chancre.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	 And yet, wise men say that a fire cautery should also be done in the middle of the chancre; but this does not seem good to me, because I fear that it may become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have seen it happen before; and it is more appropriate for it to be cauterized around, using the "circular" cautery, as we have said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot mature or grow. This refers to a condition where a swelling does not develop into a full-blown abscess and cannot be resolved through natural means, requiring medical intervention.
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	 When someone has an illness called "adubelati", and it delays in dying due to its superfluity or the water of the patient when they are infirm (that is, too old) and have little blood, or due to time; and you wish to hasten its death: then cauterize around with many small cauteries by pricking; leave it like that afterwards.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	 Because it will hasten in dying.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you wish to pierce it with the entire cautery, heat the cautery until it is like this form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	 And put your hand in the middle of this illness called "adubelati" until the cautery has pierced the core, and make the cauteries such that the patient feels them from outside in such a way that the course of the decay is alleviated.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 After the care until it is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	curing with fire through iron (i.e., using a hot iron)
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	 Another kind of illness exists which is called "corrodens", and it is nothing but a consumption of the limb, for it consumes the limbs just as fire consumes dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	 If you see this illness in a place that can tolerate cautery with fire, then heat the cauterizing iron to a moderate and large degree, according to where the illness is; after that, cauterize all around until you reach all of the corruption, and let nothing of it remain, so that all that is corrupt is removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	 And then let it be for three days and apply on the cauterized areas ground barley with oil until the burns from the fire are removed, along with all of the corruption.[/If you see this illness in a place that can tolerate cautery with fire, then heat the cauterizing iron to a moderate and large degree, according to where the illness is; after that, cauterize all around until you reach all of the corruption, and let nothing of it remain, so that all that is corrupt is removed.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	 After the treatment of wound-generating pus.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	 And if after three days you see that healthy flesh has not grown, it is good; and if not, then reapply the cautery to the remaining areas of corrupt flesh.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	 And this abscess has sometimes been cured with medical powder instead of fire cautery; but nonetheless, fire cautery is of greater help. I have already mentioned the cure for medical powder in the previous section: take it as needed.[](Note: The translation of "prend la quant tu en as mestier" could also be "take when you need it.")
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of athlete's foot that comes to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	 It often happens that in the feet there arises a disease called "clos" according to our understanding, and it is a large abscess that wounds the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	 And the cauteries for this disease are of two kinds.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	 That is to say, cautery by fire and cautery by hot water.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	 The cautery by fire is: heat the cautery like a rooster's spur, and make it from good iron, of a size that can encompass the nail from all sides, and have fine edges; then place it very hot on the nail, and turn your hand all around the nail until you reach the base of the nail; and leave it in this manner for three days until it begins to putrefy; then apply a plaster made of crushed mallows with oil, and let the plaster remain overnight, and the nail will fall out and be uprooted from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then heal the wound with ointment until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	 And if they are turned inward by the body, and this happens often in hands and feet, then you should apply hot water cautery; and it is done in this way: take an iron or steel cannula, or a pen of vaults, and place the nail and althelul on top, that is to say powdered herbs for warts; and place the cannula so that it surrounds completely, then add some hot water, and hold your hand firmly, pressing your hand around so that the edge of the cannula comes to the base of the nail, and can find a deep path through the hot water to the root; and let the patient endure the biting of the hot water for an hour; then leave it as is, and it will come out completely with its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	 Do one after the other, as you burn all those that are on the body, then cure the abscesses that produce flesh.
li cure dou trembler	the treatment of trembling/shaking
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	If someone trembles from coldness of nerves or quartan fever or otherwise, then you should make 4 cauteries or 4 of them on the spine at the base of the neck, one cautery between each vertebra; and one on the hip, and one on the stomach at the olive-shaped cautery; this will stop the trembling and hasten the recovery from the cold sickness.
des pustules puans	"foul-smelling pustules" or "putrid pustules"
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	 Sometimes it happens that the body appears with hollows, or stinking pustules, which come from thick corrupted matters.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	 It is necessary, at the first appearance of these, to apply a cautery on each pustule: a thin rod of myrtle wood, with its tip heated in fire, or a long root of aristolochia, or a round shaped cautery.[br]Note: I am not adding any comments or contextual information as per your instructions. The translations are based solely on the given Old French text.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	 And sometimes they cauterize at the beginning when they appear in this manner, and they cannot grow further, but the excess is broken down and healed; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.[br]Note: I am not adding any comments or contextual information as per your instructions. quant li artere est copee	when an artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Often, there is a large flow of blood from the cut artery to the wound, or to the incision of an abscess, or to the cauterization of the limb, and similar things; and it is a very difficult thing to stop the bleeding.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And yet, when this happens to someone, quickly place your index finger on the wound of the vein and press very hard so that the blood is calmed under your finger and no more comes out; then heat various olive-shaped cauters, both small and large, until they are all red; then apply one, whether large or small, according to the wound and the place where the artery is located, and place the cauter on that vein where you have your finger, and hold it there until the bleeding has stopped.[translated by Taylor R.](<https://community.duolingo.com/comment/43267959$comment_given_id=100%3Apost%3Fid%3D43267959>)
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it starts to bleed again when you remove your finger from the vein, and the cauter is extinguished, quickly take another one from those in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not stop doing this one after the other until the bleeding has stopped; and be careful not to burn the nerve that is next to it, and make sure no other harm comes to the patient; and know that when blood flows from an artery, it cannot be stopped easily, especially if the artery is large, unless it is done in one of the four ways we have mentioned: with a cauter, by extracting it when it has not been treated, by tightly binding it with a bandage, or by using medicines that have the power to stop bleeding; and let it be bound and constricted appropriately.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will treat tight restraint with tightly wrapped cloth or by placing hot things on it, or similar things, will not benefit much from it.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if it happens to someone who does not have any medical supplies with them, they should place their index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and apply firm pressure until it is stopped above the wound and the vein; and they must not move it, but wet it frequently with very cold water until the blood coagulates, thickens, and stops flowing; and make preparations for what they need in terms of cautery and medicine.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of surgical treatments.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all diseases that require fire cautery or heated medical instruments, and we have discussed their causes, tools, and forms; and I have arranged this chapter from head to foot, and in this chapter, I will follow the same path so that one can more easily find what they are looking for.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so, as I begin this, it is appropriate, dear friend, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of the cauteries, and therefore greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	 And I advise you not to undertake foolishness.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	 For many kinds of people come for cures.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	 such people come who are so afflicted by their illness that they would easily die due to the severity and greatness of its harm; and one should fear for these individuals.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	 And there are some who regain their senses and say: "wait, I am healed"; yet the illness is scornful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	 It is not at all appropriate for you to agree with those who come to you with such behavior, but rather put more effort into your honor than your greed, and do not rashly open up for those about whom you are uncertain and can gain nothing, instead use caution and prudence. Also make use of prognosis and indication in the treatment of your patients so that their health may be restored. This will help you establish a good reputation, and bring you glory and praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dear son, may the Lord give you understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to inspire from the holy inspiration of his hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	I have divided this chapter into sections for you, as it is before the chapter on cauteries that I have explained to you from head to foot, so that you may more easily find what you need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	a full or swollen head (lit. head full of water)
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this illness often occurs in children during childbirth, and it happens when the birth canal applies too much force to the child's head; and sometimes it is caused by unknown reasons.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I never saw this disease except in children, and in all that I have seen, death hastened; and for this reason, it seems better to me to abandon the work in such cures.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child where the head was full of water, and the skull thickened each day so much that it could not support it; and the moisture increased so much that he died, and this moisture is gathered under the bone at the siphac, between the brain and the bone; and the operation is such if the moisture is between the brain and the bone, and the abscess is small, that you make an incision in the middle of the head a wide opening; and let it be as long as .ii. fingers, so that the moisture runs out; and here is the form of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more abundant and the abscess is larger, then make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and the signs that you see are the corners of the mouth open on each side, and the water jumps out when you press it from the inside with your hand, and this does not respond, then you must make three incisions in the middle of the head in this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	 And after the incision, remove all the pus.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	 Afterwards, bind the cuts with cloth and powder, and apply wine and oil, leaving it like that until the fifth day; then loosen it, and treat the wound with bandages and ointments, and also keep the head bound, and give the patient dry food with little moisture until the limb is strengthened and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is that you look where the swelling of the abscess is prominent and where the collection of water is; for sometimes it is in front, sometimes behind, sometimes to the right, and sometimes to the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Therefore, incise there where the abscess is prominent and the collection of water is, and shape the wound according to your ability; and make sure that you do not cut the artery; and if a flow of blood comes, so that the patient dies from bleeding and evacuation of pus.

Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it happens to someone a disease called "catarrh" in the eyes or in the lungs, and the illness is chronic, and medical treatment does not help at all, then the last resort is the cautery with that which they will burn two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	 Therefore, when you cover the eyes, let the patient bend his head; then rub the area around the eye with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then have the patient press his neck against the entire cloth; then look where the veins bulge, and the areas on both sides of the ears are swollen, and if they are not aligned; then make marks at the meeting point, then cut both sides with a sharp knife one-third of the way, so that the incision reaches the bone, and this should be done across the width of the head.

de emigrainne	Here is the translation:

Here is the translation:
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Here is the translation:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	 then gently flay the skin until you reach the artery, then pull it up with hemostats, and separate it well from the membranes beneath it in each part; and if the artery is fine, then turn it with the tip of the hemostat, then let blood flow from that part according to the quantity of two fingers.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	 For if it is not cut, the blood will not leave entirely.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw blood from the six holes until three; and if the artery is large, then it should be tied in two places with a strong double thread of silk, to prevent necrosis before the wound is sutured and bleeding occurs; then cut away the excess that is between the two ties at that very hour, and then, if you wish, cauterize the wound with a scalpel cautery up to the bone until the holes are burned through; and this is the best practice, if the patient does not have a fever and has a hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For fire cautery helps to end moisture: for this reason it is of greater help with moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	In which case, for the extraction of arteries, it is necessary to fill the wound with old cotton and place well-made bandages on top; and when they are loosened, cure with dry medicines that cause flesh to grow, and with bandages until it is healed; and if blood flows from the artery as long as you work on it, then quickly cover it with cautery or fill the wound with vitriol and press on it firmly until the bleeding stops; and if you do not have this on hand, place your finger over the wound until the blood clots, and keep pouring cold water over it until the bleeding stops, pressing as needed; and a more gentle and easier method for extracting an artery is to cauterize the vein with this two-sided cutting cautery, but make sure that the edges are thick to maintain their heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too thin, it holds its heat less.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And there should be a finger's breadth of space between the two knives, and when you have marked the two places, place the heated iron upon them until it reaches the bone, and cut the vein in two places; and they should be far apart because this fire cautery is not solid all throughout; and that is the form of the cautery.
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears flowing from the eyes come from the veins that are above the temple of the head and medical treatment does not help, and you see the face of the patient turn red, and feel a pulsation on the forehead like a tremor; and if the eyelids are tight and moist so that the paper has fallen off, and the paper has been heated up and scorched by the heat of the tears, then this remedy is needed.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	 And the ancients called it "cure contused", and you should do the following for the patient who has this illness: let him have long hair on his forehead, then make three equal incisions on his forehead according to its length; and one of the incisions should be in the middle of the forehead, going down to the eyebrows, and the other two should be above the eyebrows; and be careful not to cut the arteries which are located above the eyebrows; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the two mandibles, and let each wound be the width of three fingers joined together; and prepare a piece of sponge and plenty of rags for wiping the blood, then insert the suppository as follows: [the text refers to a medical recipe for making a specific type of medical suppository called "spatumile agut", but it is not possible to provide a complete translation without the context provided by the original medieval medical treatise.]
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision that is above the temple to the second incision; and scrape off all the flesh that is between the two cuts right down to the suture on the bone, then make another cut from the middle incision to the other second one, and then remove this styptic.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	insert into the first cut the instrument called "cultellar", which is very sharp on one side and blunt on the other side, with this shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure. Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous to where it is visible near the heart, and then do the same in the middle split until the other side; and then bleed equally, and press the area so that blood is extracted; then place a piece of old cotton in each split, and put wet bandages on them with wine and oil and vinegar, and make sure no abscess forms; and on the third day, loosen the tie, and apply a lot of cool water, then cure it with basilicon ointment and rose oil, and other cures used to treat wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the swelling of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When someone is accustomed to getting a catarrh frequently, and you see the eyes sunken and small, with weakened vision and inflamed eyelids; and the hair falls out, and there is deep pain in the head, and the patient sneezes; then know from these symptoms that those matters and those catarrhs do not come out of one vein alone, and the proper cure for this is as follows.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	 And instruct the patient to bend their forehead, then make a large slit between the eyebrows, and another one an inch wide.
