Begin at the slit of the left temple and extend the incision to the right temple, cutting down to the bone; keep your hand away from the temple nerves that move when eating; once the bone is exposed, wipe away all blood with a sponge, then separate the two lips of the slit and place a piece of old cotton and linen cloth, then bind bandages soaked in wine and oil over it, being careful not to cause a hot abscess; when removed, rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then treat with drying agents that promote the growth of flesh.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this way, take two parts of wheat flower and four parts of colophony, and make it into an ointment; then apply it to these wounds to promote the growth of flesh throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	The blockage of the ears.
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls into the ears is one of the four things: either grains, or creatures, or mineral stones such as iron; or seeds, such as lice, beans, peas; or fluids such as water and ashes and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	 When it falls into the ear a stone or other object that does not join with the ear, nor grows in the ear, then place the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	 If you see the stone, distill a few drops of violet oil or sesame oil, then introduce extraction; and make them sneeze with a powder, and stop up their nostrils when the sneezing comes, and place pieces of cloth or wool around the ear; and stretch the ear upward.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	 This cure often brings forth the stone; and if it does not come forth, introduce extraction with delicate tweezers, of which this is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out with the pincers, that is good; if not, then facilitate extraction using a fine hook of thin wire; and if it does not come out that way, then make a probe of tin and insert the head of the probe into the hole of the ear forcefully, and stop what is around the probe with soft wax so that the wind cannot enter with the probe; then pull it out strongly, for many times it comes out as we have said; and if it does not come out in this way, then take birdlime, which is used to catch birds, and place some on an instrument that is suitable for this purpose, and put a piece of cotton around; then press the birdlime onto the stone or whatever it may be, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not come out with all of these things that we have mentioned, then hurry to pierce the ear so that abscess and scab forms; and the manner of this piercing is that you first make an incision on the patient's head and draw blood according to their strength, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small incision at the base of the ear in the fatty area or where it hangs; and let the incision be like a crescent moon, coming to the stone, then remove it as best you can, and quickly suck on it with your mouth; and continue this treatment until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a grain that is infected and swells, perform an extraction; and if it cannot come out, apply a thin spatula in this shape:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	 and make an incision in that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	 But do not make the mistake of thinking that the gland is moist due to ear moisture, until you have made many slices; then carefully extract it with forceps, as we have said, so that the extraction is eased.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	 Therefore, in the water that falls into the ear, the patient should use sneezing of prepared substances first and widen the ear with soft cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	 And lie with the affected ear upward where the water is.[](note: I am a helpful AI and my purpose is to assist you. You can continue to give me sentences from your text and I will translate them for you, one by one.)
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	 If it comes out by itself, that's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	 If it does not come out by itself, take many small and light pebbles, and warm them slightly by the fire; and place one of the pebbles in the patient's ear, and jump up on one foot from the other side, and strike another pebble on the stone that is in the ear; and do not stop striking with one pebble after another until all the water comes out, and it will come out completely; and if you wish, take a reed and insert one end into the ear, and light the other end with fire until the inner part of the reed is burned; then repeat the same process with another piece of reed until all the water comes out, as we have said with the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of an animal, if it is of small size, such as a louse and similar things, cure it as we have said in division; but if it is of large size that can be felt, then perform extraction with tweezers; and this is the easiest thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms in the ears, when you treat it as we have said in the division and treatment of distillations, and the cure does not help at all, then you should look at the ear in the sun: if you see any worms, then pull them out with fine forceps, and if you don't see any, then take a probe of the kind described here:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	 And should be tight below and loose above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	 And insert the thinnest end of the instrument into the ear according to the degree of the patient's pain, then suck strongly until all the wax is removed; do this frequently until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	 And if they do not obey to come out, then stop up around the instrument with cotton as I have said on the stone; and if they do not come out as we have said, then administer the distillations that the ancients have proven in cases of worms, and you will find them in the treatment of distillations; and distill your oils and medicines into the ear with this instrument, of which this is the form as you see.[Note: I assumed "vers" means "worms" based on context]
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And let it be made of silver or brass, narrow below with a small hole, and wide above for distillation; and have a well-made brass instrument to press the distillation in, and if you wish, take a scraper and wrap cotton around the tip; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever you choose of your medicines into the probe, and keep the probe in the ear; then insert the scraper with all the cotton, and press your hand gently until the oil is distilled or flows from the ear; and let the patient feel it inside, and let the distillation be a small pot heated by fire so that it can be distilled into the ear; and make sure it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be as effective.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	The blockage of the ears.
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	Any child is born who has no hole in their ears; and the same thing happens to adults due to blockage from wound or pus inside the ear, and this blockage sometimes goes deep into the ear, so that it cannot be seen; and sometimes there is a small pock near the hole, and one can see it well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	The one that goes deep and cannot be seen is of difficult healing in many cases, and for the one that can be seen, it is necessary to expose the patient's ear to the sun; and look inside: if you see the blockage clearly, work on it with this instrument, which is its shape.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let it be sharp and blunt at the front and back, so that it does not injure the ear; if the blockage is from pus or flesh in the ear, hold it with delicate tweezers and gently scrape it out until all the flesh is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	 And if pus is deep in the ear, take a thin, sharp razor, heat it slightly over fire, then place it in the ear canal.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	 If you notice pus causing discomfort to the patient's hearing, make a small incision, but be careful not to damage the ear nerves; then insert a wick of appropriate size into the incision, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this for some days until the wound is healed, or take a tent and soak it in rose water, and powder made of crushed vitriol; and if you see the ear swollen, then you should remove that tent and apply another tent soaked in cerote made from roset oil and wax, until the swelling is gone; then continue to care for it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, then soak a sponge and cloth in cold water, and place it on the ear, and use other cures that stop the bleeding which are in the treatment of distillations.

de la gresle	The term "de la grésle" is a medieval term that can refer to hail or a type of disease. Without more context, it's difficult to provide an accurate translation. However, in the following phrases, "grésle" may be translated as "hail":
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	 Often, small grain-like substances appear on paper from the patient's eyes, having the form and hardness of sand; this condition is called "grains" (or grauin in Old French). It is an accumulation of thick moisture in the upper and lower eyelid paper. Here is the treatment: check if the grains are moving from one side to another, which is easy to notice; then make an incision along its path, gently scrape the area, use forceps to grasp it and remove it.[
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	 if you cannot cover it without puncturing the paper a little, it does not harm the patient; and if the wound is large, suture it with a stitch and cure it until it is healed; and if it is small, do not force it, for the ointment will soon restore it and help heal the flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the grandine descends inside the ear toward the upper part, turn the paper and extend the grandine with tweezers, and remove it while pressing from one side and the other; and if the paper is moved away by the incision, this does not matter; and when the grandine has been removed, irrigate the eye with salty water and cure the wound until it heals.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	 Exinach is an ointment that is applied to paper sheets and this happens more in children than in any other people, and it greatly irritates their eyes, and they get discharge in the mornings, and they cannot look at the sunlight because their tears rush to their eyes; and for this reason, they often lie on their backs with their faces up and sleep, and their papers are wet under their eyelids, causing swelling and giving the appearance of exinach that is visible in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	 And when you press the joint with your hands and feel the exirnach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the method of this procedure is as follows: the patient places their head on your lap, and then take a linen cloth and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity of exinach present in each part, then place it on top; and press with your hands from both sides so that the exinach comes together in the center; then make an incision in the middle of the moisture with a sharp scalpel-like instrument, and let it not be any larger than the wound made when opening a vein; and cut through the leather until you reach the exinach; and in multiple ways, the exinach comes out of the incision, in the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Then extract it all in one piece with the cloth between your fingers outwardly, and turn your hand to left and right until it is dispersed; and make sure not to press on the incision, so that you do not reach the whole scalpel until you touch the eye and wound it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the exit wound does not appear at the beginning of the incision, slightly increase the incision length until it appears; then extract it as we have said, then wet bandages in oil and water, and place them on the wound, and bind with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	 And if there are such men who trample soil and place it on top to corrupt the moisture that has remained.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then cure it until it is healed.

Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When paper-like hairs grow that are not natural and have grown old, they harm the eyes and cause various illnesses such as excessive tearing and softening of the eyes and cataracts, to the point of causing eye destruction. There are four ways to treat this: through cauterization with fire, or through medicine according to what is described in the chapter on cauterization, and it is done either by incision and suture or by blisters, depending on what I will say.

It is necessary that you place the patient's head in your lap, then turn the paper of the eye to your left hand; if it is turned, it is good; if not, insert a needle with a single thread; and let this be beside the margin of the paper where the hairs grow next to these hairs, and pull a thread above the entire paper, and turn it to the razor; then make an incision beneath the paper, beneath the adjusted hairs, as wide as the spatula, from the large tear duct down to the small one; then pull out a thread, and place underneath the paper a small cotton and linen tent, then sign with a figure of an inch, such as a myrtle leaf, and nevertheless it is necessary that the figure corresponds to the height that you wish to raise the paper which is divided to all.

et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	 And if there are those who need to cut a large quantity of paper according to how the paper has softened; then apply ointment to the entire spatula along the two lines that you have marked, starting from the big notch down to the small one; and make one of the cuts close to the natural hairs, as thick as a root, then insert the probe into one of the two angles of the wound, then scrape it all; and if not, then ignore it and leave the stitches and threads for three or four days; then cure the wound without drying or constricting materials, as the paper will swell upon closing of the wound and bring them together, but the stitch is harmful (as the ancients have said), and this is a fearless procedure; and there is another way: to sign the paper with a figure similar to the leaf of myrtle, with three incisions as shown here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then bend [or force] what sticks out above the small bones equally, following the shape that is here:

Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of gangrene is as follows: and it consists of folding the paper and making an incision according to what I have said, and then making two incisions with skill, and two thin threads as long as the paper and as wide as the space between the eyes; and bend the two corners of two parts where you hold the threads; then bring the two thin threads together gently on top of the part of the paper above the eye, and pull the two threads firmly from both sides; and leave it like that for several days, and the skin that has been pulled will die and turn black and rot, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	 If it delays, strike it with force, then cure it until it is healed; and when the wound is closed, and the paper is removed, and the hairs will no longer prickle; and this is the shape of the two sinews that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The procedure is as follows: take a fine needle and thread a soft, fine silk thread through it; then bring the edges of the wound together and tie the thread gently, and let the length of the threads be one palm long; then place another fine thread of silk next to it and tie the ends of the threads; then put the patient's head in your lap; and do this in a sunny place so that the procedure is well-lit, for it is a delicate and small task; then insert the needle through the entire length of the needle into the root of the hair adjacent to the wound, and quickly push it through the skin until it comes out above the natural eyebrow hairs; then pull out the hairs up to the tip of the needle and insert the pulled-out hairs into the needle, whether there is one or two or three or more hairs; then remove your hand so that all the hairs come out through the entire length of the needle along with the natural eyebrow hairs.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the suture is removed and the hairs do not come out with it, then pull the suture downwards below the thread that you have placed until the suture comes out of the opening above and you can see it with your eye; then pull both the suture and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days until the hairs become embedded in their place and new growth appears; and if the hairs are small, then attach one long hair from the natural eyebrows and lift it up with that or let it hang loose until it is lengthened, then remove it.

de l’ungle de l’oil	of the eyelid or corner of the eye
