Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	 It is necessary, firstly, that you look to see if the eye, where the swelling is, is outside [its socket], and there is no other illness but the swelling; then the eye should be treated in this way: instruct the patient to place their head in your lap, then gently lift the eyelids with your fingers, delicately doubled in this form.
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two fingers arranged gradually in one row in this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	then when you have carefully constricted those veins, and wiped away the blood hour after hour, until you see the swollen veins recede from the eye; and take care not to poke the eye with the ends of the cauterizing tools, and perform this task at midday before the sun, and be very diligent in your work so that you do not injure the veins; and once you have done this, distill into the eye a mixture of green and red bile to break down any remaining pus.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are unable to do all of this in that hour, make a poultice for the eye with soothing ingredients to alleviate the pain of the eyes, and leave it on for several days until the pain subsides and you are certain there is no danger of abscess; then resume according to the previously described method until it has healed; this is the method of constricting:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The masters call this type of fistula "arissati"; when you treat it with cautery and hot medicine as I have previously mentioned, but it is not healed, there is a trick to it: you must make an incision on the abscess, at the point where it should burst, and drain all the pus that is in it, until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed, and you see corruption and blackness, take all the instruments which are in the form described here; and it is called "rough head", and make it of iron one cubit long, and point it like a file as in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	Place the "rough head" on top of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your hands and press down firmly until you feel that the corruption is removed; do this several times, then restore the place with drying medicaments.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	 If the wound is closed and pus forms, and the flesh of the eye is closed, and it remains so for forty days, without becoming inflamed or developing an abscess, and no other ill happens, know that it is healed; if not, there is no other means but to bring the fistula to the opening of the nose in this way: reveal the bone a second time with iron, and with sharp medicines, and when it has been revealed, take a three-pronged fork of iron in this shape, and the head of the fork should be of three angles, and the handle should be made thin up to the tip as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	 then place it on the bone next to the tear duct, and move your hand away from the eye pupil, then turn the entire style until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through the sensation of breath if they hold their hand over their nose; and then restore the place with dry medicines, as I have taught you, and when the flesh grows and hardens in the area, then the material goes to the nose; making it a lighter matter for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the eye socket/orbit dislocation
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eye is open wide all around and there is no trouble or reduction in vision, then bind the patient; next cauterize, then apply leeches or cups without striking to draw blood, then place a mixture of alum, aloe, incense, and sarcocollex on the eyelid; then bandage the eye and cover it with bandages and soft cloths; take care to use enough soft cloths, doubled in four layers, and apply them gradually according to how much is needed for the eye; next bandage firmly with a hard bandage, and reapply the cups without striking to draw blood; then remove the cups and leave the eye bandaged day and night, and if the mixture softens, tighten the bandage again; then remove the bandage after a day and a night, and if you see that the eye is healing, it is good; if not, reapply the mixture, bandages, and leeches until it heals.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	of retinal detachment
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When there is a disruption in the retina, it becomes visible and appears as if there are grains of resin on the paper; this is frightening to see. If you view such a detachment, the procedure is to insert a needle into the root of the lower part all the way up to the upper part, then insert another needle with double thread in the corner of the eyelid. Pierce it and leave the first needle as it was placed; next cut off the end of the doubled thread and use it to tie around the edge of the retina, pulling it tight, then remove the needle and place a soft, wet cloth soaked in egg on the eye. Leave it until the threads stick to the retina, then treat the eye with comforting remedies until the wound heals. Sometimes, the wound is restrained by a circle of cloth around the edge of the eye until it has healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eye appears swollen, pierce it with a thin spatula that comes from within the eye, and let the watery humor run out, and let the eye descend and go in again; then pull it out until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the swelling of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	 This disease called "alcunnati" is nothing but a bubble that forms in the eye, appearing like descending water, and it is not water; and the manner of its appearance work is as follows: make the patient sit on an appropriate chair, straight up, then hold their head with both your hands, and move it back and forth until you see the bubble rise above to your eyes; then have it fixed and let the light not descend or be obstructed, and let the patient see things as they used to; and if it does not descend, know that it is water, and if the descent of the bubble is not formed as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 if you make the patient sit between your hands, then take the thin spatula and pierce through the horny tissue up to the continuation of the conjunctiva with the horny tissue and the ring; until the boil comes out; and when it has come out, distill warm water mixed with honey, or water or fenugreek that has been boiled and mixed with honey, then cure it with another cure until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the waters (or fluids) of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	 We have similarities of the waters in the division, and that which is necessary to pierce; so work according to the health (condition).
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	 It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from the light for the sun, and cover the healthy eye and constrict it very strongly; then place the patch on the eye on your left hand if the eye is left, or on your right hand if the eye is right; then take in your right hand, if the eye is left, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand if the eye is right; then place the tip of the instrument next to the ring by the thickness of a thread in that whiteness of the eye at the part of the lesser tear duct, then push the instrument called "almagda" forcefully, and turn your hand until it pierces into the whiteness of the eye, and feel that the almagda reaches the empty space; and the measure of the way of the almagda should be at the bottom of the measure of the space which is from the pupil to the end of the darkness; and this is the ring of the eye; and you will see the bone in that patch due to the clarity of the horny tissue, and then place the instrument until it reaches where the water is, then press it down under one path after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	 if the water recedes now, the patient will see in front of him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	 After a short rest, if the water rises again along the second path, apply force with the instrument, and when it is embedded and no longer rises, gently extract the stone while turning your hand around; then put a little bit of gem-like salt water in it, and raise the eye from this.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	 Then place over the eye wadding or wet wool soaked in rose oil and egg yolk, and bind it with the healthy eye.[ (Note: "abun d'uef" means egg yolk)]
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	 We, and those who are of our time, put on a compress with egg yolk.[ (Note: "comin broiet" refers to a compress)][ETA: I have corrected my translation of "comin broiet". Thank you to the user who pointed out my mistake.]
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for there are some men who have very hard eyes, then it is necessary that you take the instrument which is called "alberit", whose shape is as follows:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	 And then only pierce the ligament, and do not go too deep, but make it subtle, then put in almagda as we have said; and at the completion of the work prepare a pleasant sleep for the patient, in which they sleep on their back in a dark place; and be devoid of all movements, and partake light foods, and do not move his head to the right or left, and be bound according to his disposition until the third day; then unbind him in the same dark room, and test his vision, and let him see some things, and then replace the binding until the seventh day; and it is not at all suitable to do this during the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary to lighten this, because the water rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	 if pustules appear, let the eye be unbound before the seventh day, and apply a compress of that which soothes the pustule; and when it has calmed, let the vision be unbound and place a dressing on its side to cover for some days, and let it always remain in that darkened room.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	 And then leave the house frequently and often, and return to your duties; and know that no disciple should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And a man came to us who was from Yrach, who told us that in their country they make almagda perciet, which one can suck the water (juice) from, but nonetheless I have never seen any such thing in our land, nor do I read of it in books of ancient knowledge; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of the forms of almagda, so that those who do not know it may see (them); and they should be made of pure tin:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And let the tops of them be of this same delicacy, and the rear parts in three sharp points.[translating "agues" as "sharp points"]
de la char sor le neis	of flesh from the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	 Sometimes various types of swellings or blisters are born, some of which resemble scorpions with many feet; and there are such that have hardened skin of fox-colored hue, and soft skin of good color.[](Note: I'm assuming the term "fuxe" refers to a reddish-brown or foxy color.)
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	 Then in the case of this dislocation which is gentle, and not inflamed, it is necessary that you seat the patient between your hands towards the sun; and clear out his nostrils, and apply a small piece of lard to those parts, and pull it out; then collect with a delicate narrow spatula what you are able to hold on one side, until you know that the part is completely free from obstruction.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains any part that cannot be cut, open it with all one instrument very delicately and lightly, so that nothing remains; and if pus forms or an abscess arises, treat it as appropriate; and if they are malignant abscesses, hurry and cauterize them until the blood stops and all the flesh growths are removed, then pour vinegar or sterilized water into the nose.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	 If the nose clears and moisture reaches the palate, know that it is healed; and if the moisture does not penetrate as it should, know that there is a growth in the bone above, which the instruments cannot cut: then it is necessary to insert into it a fairly thick linen thread, and let it be tied with loose knots at intervals of about an inch or less; and place the filament in the patient's nostril up to its capacity, and pull it gently until it comes through the nose into the mouth; and children often do this in school, and it is an easy thing for those who want to do it; then hold the part that comes out of the nose with one hand, and the other part that comes out of the mouth with the other hand, and feel along the thread to determine what is inside.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	 Perform this procedure so that you know the wound has corrupted the flesh, then pull out the sutures, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and place it back on the nose as before; perform this for three days or more, until the ointment corrupts all remaining flesh; and then place a strip of willow on the nose for several days until it heals, and if drying medicines are needed, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, with which oils and medicines are distilled into the nose.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be of silver or brass, resembling an open lamp, such as a candle, and the wick similarly; and if you wish, make a closed candle, and let the instrument be full to purge the head; and have a handle on the head to hold it when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of flesh from the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Often arises in the head of the nose a disease called "telul", and it grows and becomes large at times, to the point where it is visible; and therefore, you must cut it at the beginning and remove it all, then place the cautery or hot medicine on the wound; and if you delay cutting it until it has grown, see if it is hard, of purple color, with poor sensation: do not touch it with iron because it is an abscess that has festered, because when it is cut even once, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is soft to the touch, not of purple color, and you see that you can cut all of it, empty the patient and cut the wound without fear, and cure it with drying and constricting things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose has been cut and sewn[References:
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	 Know that when solutions of continuation come to one of these cartilaginous works, it profits little, except in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then, when this happens to someone, look if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then bring the two edges together in a stitch, then cure it until it heals; and if the edges are separated on one side and the other, then you must cauterize all the parts of their edge until they heal, then bring the two edges together in a stitch, and bind it, and put powder of dragon's blood, and ground incense on top of the powders, and place a piece of strong plaster or another adhesive plaster on top, and leave it until it sticks to it, then cure it with ointment until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of suturing is such that you approximate the wound: either with needles, as we have said in the suture of the belly; or with thread, as I have made known to you.
des apostemes des levres	abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	To some men, hard abscesses like grains of pepper appear within the lips, smaller and larger; then you must turn the lips, and make an incision on each node, and take it with forceps and cut each part; then apply a poultice of powdered vitriol after the incision until the blood is stopped; and then apply goose grease, and cure the wound with dry things until it heals.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often, a hardened flesh is born on the gums, which the ancients called "albulus"; you should hold it with tongs and cut at its root, letting the pus or blood flow; then put vitriol powder or other restraining and desiccative powders on the wound; and if this flesh comes back after the incision, which often happens, cut it again and cauterize it: it will not come back after cauterization; and these are the shapes of the instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of abscesses or inflammations. The term "sordes" in medieval medical texts often refers to purulent, infected matter or discharges that accumulate in the body and need to be drained or cleaned out. So "des sordens" could refer to the treatment or removal of such abscesses or inflamed areas.
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes, hard and rough crusts form on the top of teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, which are ugly and harsh; and sometimes the teeth become black, yellow, or green, such that corruption reaches the gum, and the teeth become foul-smelling; you must make the patient sit between your hands, with their head in your lap, and scrape off any visible tartar, crusts, or stains from the teeth until nothing remains; and do the same for black, green, yellow, and other stains until they are cleaned; and if all of the buildup is removed during the first cleaning, that is good; if not, resume cleaning on the second and third days until everything is removed; and know that teeth require various shapes of instruments to clean them, depending on what the task requires, because scrapers used to clean between teeth have different forms than those used to clean the surfaces of teeth; and make sure you have these shapes and others prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary, when you cure the tooth of its pain, that you delay pulling it as long as you can, because one should not do this hastily; for it is a very serious matter up to the point where there is no excuse for damaging it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	 Then, when the patient is about to be drawn, you should make sure that the tooth loosening dent is ready.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	 Often, the pain deceives the patient, and they think it is in a good tooth, and they have that tooth pulled; yet the pain does not go away, until the harmful extraction is done, as we have already seen with these surgeons; and when you are certain of the loose tooth, you must cauterize around the tooth with a strong stylet to protect the gum from all sides; then extract it between your fingers or with fine tongs at first pull and pull until it is fully extracted, then securely fasten the tongs; and have the patient's head in your lap, holding it firmly so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	 After extract the tooth without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, then take one of these instruments and gently push it in from both sides, and move it as you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	 And if the tooth is pierced and eaten away, then you should fill it with cloth where the holes are; and hold it delicately with tongs, so as not to break it when holding; and one must work very carefully around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	 And take care not to break it, and leave a part of it, for if you do not, greater pains will return to the patient because of the malignity of the root.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	 And take heed that you do not act as some ignorant surgeons do, who in their haste and recklessness sometimes break the leg, and bring about none of the things we have described; but instead, through their carelessness, sometimes cause great illness to develop due to the retained roots, or because they broke the leg, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is extracted, wash the wound with wine or vinegar and salt; and if pus forms there, which often happens, apply vitriol; and if that does not work, cauterize the area.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments with which one moves the teeth first should be long and have thick handles, so that they do not bend when you pull the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should have thick shanks so that they do not bend when pulled, and they should be made of good iron, and serrated to hold teeth in place.
de la racine des dens	on the roots of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	 When the root remains after extraction, you should place cotton soaked in butter on the wound for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	 as long as the place is softened, then put in the tongs called "algefri," which resemble a bird's beak; and they should be made inside like a file, and this is its shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all of these tongs, then you must cut open the flesh all around the root and place in it the instrument called "althali," that is, a scalpel, of which this is the shape:[ST1] It is not clear what is meant by "c’est a savoir palainche" in the original text. I translated it as "that is, a scalpel," but it could also mean "namely, a scalpel" or something similar.
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the roots come out through this, that is good; if not, use all the instruments, of which forms are described later.
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And one can help themselves with this instrument that has two handles, of which this is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other iron instruments that are in front of the teeth's root, and of this instrument that looks like large pliers, of which this is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let these instruments be strong so that they do not break, and know that there are many dental instruments; and also other instruments that are not mentioned here; and the wise master subtly finds his own instrument, according to what his work and the disease show him, because there are such diseases for which the ancients did not teach any instrument due to their diversity; and one does not break the cart or other bones, where it will rot, but instead searches among the instruments that are needed, as I have told you, and helps with gestures, of which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be thick and able to hold the bone so that it does not splinter, but can instead hold and remove it; and then restore the place with medicines appropriate for this, and if there is rotting in the bone, and it is small, then use all of this instrument for it.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not in accordance with the body's natural form, and its shape is ugly, and the same is true for young women, you should determine if the tooth is new after the tooth, and it is not in the right place, and it cannot be straightened or filed: then file it; but if it is crooked compared to the other tooth, take this tool, the shape of which is shown here, similar to a small beak, and made of sharp iron:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And hold the instrument close and keep it in your hands for several days due to the tooth's hardness, and so that you do not move the other teeth, and if it appears that it can be filed down, file it with a file like the one shown here in form:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is similar to the file used to make needles; and carefully and lightly file down the tooth, holding it still until it is loose; then use a plane at the end for smoothing, and if the tooth is too sharp and cuts the tongue, file down the roughness until it is even, so that it does not cut the tongue or distort speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth loosens.
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	 When the front teeth loosen, either from being struck or falling out, and the patient cannot bite down on what they eat without spitting it out, and you have treated them with constricting medicines but to no avail; then they must be constricted with a gold wire, for silver wires turn green and rot, but gold never changes; and let the wire be of medium thickness, not too thick or too thin, according to the space between the teeth; and if you wish to align the teeth, take the thread and place it double between the two healthy teeth, then put the loose teeth on top of the wire, whether there is one or more than one, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side; then begin covering it up to the point where you started, and subtly and tightly pull your hand until it does not move; and let the thread be tied at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	 Then bind the jaw with a thread using pliers, and align it, and place it between the healthy tooth and the loose tooth, and position it so that it does not cut the tongue; and keep it tight as long as it can stay, and if it loosens, or the threads break, then tie it with another thread; if it stays and serves in this way throughout its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the shape of aligning two healthy teeth and two loose teeth, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth falls out, it is replaced in its place, as we have said, as fresh as possible; and let no one who is not wise and skilled interfere; and sometimes the shape of a tooth is made from animal bone, and it is placed in the empty socket and constricted as we have said, and it remains and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cut the tie of the tongue.
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	 Sometimes there is a ligament below the tongue that is natural or occurs due to an accident of a healed wound; and the procedure is as follows: you open the mouth of the patient, hold their head in your hand, and lift their tongue; then cut the nervous ligament widely, so that the tongue is loosened from its attachment, and if there is toughness or knot, it is due to a healed wound, then insert the hook and cut wide that ligament; and make sure not to injure the artery that is beneath; and when you have finished, apply a little red rose water or warm water, or cold water, then place a linen tent under the tongue; and tell the patient to hold it in their mouth every night, so that the ligament does not heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	 And if there is bleeding, put vitriol powder on the wound; and if the blood does not stop, cauterize it with a slow-burning cautery, which is good for that; then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it of a bluish-black or hard color, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, for it is a chancre; and if it is declining towards blenchor, and there is moisture, then place the "oncine" (a medical instrument) and make an incision with a thin spatula, and release it from one side and the other; and if the blood comes to meet your work, then apply vinegar powder until it stops bleeding, then return to your work until you draw everything out; then lift it up with ease and support, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses in the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	 Sometimes abscesses come inside the throat called "godath", and they are properly called the "two almonds". And when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, be careful: if it is hard abscesses of small size and greenish color, do not touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	 And if they are red and the root is large, do not touch them with iron, also for the risk of bleeding; but leave it alone until it is ripe, and then you will remove it, or it will break by itself; and if it is of whitish color and the roots are fine, prepare the instrument to cover it, but first check whether the hard abscess has calmed down and is appeased.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	 Then make the patient sit down in front of the sun, and let his head be in your lap, and have him open his mouth and the servant place the instrument between his hands, and press his tongue down below with all the instrument, which is its form; and it should be made of thin silver or brass as with knives.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	And when you press the tongue down with all this instrument and see the abscess, then take the "oncine" (a medical instrument) and insert it into the almond (growth), and draw it out as much as you can; and draw some of the pus with it, then cover it with the instrument, which has the form of forceps; and yet the cheeks are curved inward towards each other and are very sharp, and it is made of iron or steel.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have this tool at hand, take tongs instead, of which this is the shape:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And let one side be sharp and the other blunt; and once you have bent one of the almond-shaped parts, bend the other in the same manner; and after the incision, gargle the patient with warm water and vinegar; and if there is an evacuation of blood, gargle the patient with water or the skins of pomegranates cooked, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding stops; then treat it until it has healed; and sometimes other abscesses appear in the throat besides the two almond-shaped parts, so cut them in the same way as the two almond-shaped parts.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	 And I treated a woman for an abscess that was inside her throat, that is to say, a small abscess; and she had tightly closed her entire throat so that the woman could not exhale through the passage that was blocked, and she could not eat or drink, and she would have died if she had lasted another day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	 And the abscess was so swollen that it had pushed out two corners through the two nostrils.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	 I hastened then and quickly inserted one probe into one of the nostrils, then pulled it out and extracted a large piece of bone; then I put another probe in the other nostril, and closed her mouth and pressed her tongue; after that, I inserted the probe into these abscesses and cut off a part of it, and only a little blood came out; and thus, the passageway in the woman's throat was cleared, and she began to drink water and then wine, and I continued to cut away at this abscess for a long time; and the abscess grew again and filled up the space that I had emptied, so that it became very large; then I blocked it and cauterized it from the inside of her throat: thus, it ceased to grow; and I left those parts, not knowing what God did with her afterwards.
de l’uve	of the eye (uvea)
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	 When the rupture descends to the eye, and it is swollen and elongated, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is below, large and round, it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	 When it is healed as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help at all, and you see that the large abscess has calmed down, and it is fine and not long; and it is blood-red or the color of a dry twig or black, then you must avoid making an incision into it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	 For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And have the patient have a hair on their head, or place the medicine in it, such as the teeth of a spoon, and place the instrument full of medicine on the eye; and let the patient lie on their side, so that the saliva and mucus flow from their mouth with the medicine inside, so that it does not descend to the throat and cause harm; then keep your hand on all the medicine and press it on the eye, for the duration of half an hour, until you see it absorbed and the irritation of the medicine has calmed down; and if necessary, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument full of cotton into the wound above, until the cotton hardens on the eye; and do this often, until the cautery is complete, then let it dry and fall off after three or five days. Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or cauterization; if it is treated with fumigation in this manner, take pennyroyal and hyssop and oregano and rue and chamomile and elderberry and similar herbs, and combine them all or some of them in one pot, and place a spout on it; and let the pot be well glued with strong earth, and in the middle of the pot there should be an instrument like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut. Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer. de la sansue de la gorge	of the throat sinus
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	 And if you see the vein, then draw it out with a small hook, or with delicate pliers that are suitable for this purpose.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument with which to treat the vein, when it can be seen, is similar to curved pliers so as to easily enter the throat; and it should resemble the beak of a bird of prey, and have roughness like sandpaper, so that what it takes, it cannot release; and see here its shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter on abscesses.
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	 Many similarities of abscess exist, according to what memory comes after from one and the other in this book, and they are different in perforation and size; and it is in two ways: one is in its very form, and those that it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	 And the second manner is for the places where they are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	 For the abscess of the head is different from that of the belly, and the abscess of the fleshy part is different from that which comes in joints, and each one must be judged in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	 And there are abscesses that should not be pierced until the boil is mature according to its development; and there are such ones that it is necessary to pierce when they have grown, and they do not die according to their development, such as abscesses that are near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	 For when abscesses appear near joints, and are left until they rot around, perhaps the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, causing constriction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	 Or if the abscess is near a major limb, and you delay the incision until it has died, it will harm the principal member; or if it is near the anus, then pierce it as soon as it dies; and one must not pierce an abscess that has grown without digestion being completed, except for those near the anus, so that it does not rot inwardly, become elongated, and form a fistula; and cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the hour of piercing the abscess when it is dead according to its completion, and this is when the pain has subsided, and the cessation of fever, and the decrease of pain and redness, and the softening and swelling of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and you must make the incision in the lowest part of the abscess, where it is most prominent; and let the incision be long enough for the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints, and near nerves and arteries, and on all sides where there is no curvature.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	 In those that bend, according to the member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	 And when an abscess is in a fleshy place, it is better to leave the incision until it has solidified after complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	 For if you pierce it before this, the body of the pus will be prolonged and full of much filth; and perhaps the lips and depths of it will harden.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	 And if there is any abscess that is pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the limb requires.[](https://fr.glosbe.com/fr/en/et%20si)
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	 And it is necessary that you make small incisions for small abscesses and large incisions for large ones, and many slits according to the likeness of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where the core must be cut out and covered; when it has become like a cloth and is dead, it should be done as with boils: and if there are such that are split into three angles, and if there are such that are cut like the leaf of myrtle, so for abscesses of glands; and if there are such where a round incision is made, and other cuts and similar coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	 Those who have no visible swelling, such as a soft superficial abscess, it is necessary to fully pierce it; and when the abscess is large and has collected a lot of pus, do not pull out all the pus in that hour, but instead remove only a portion; then stuff the abscess until the next day, then remove something again; do this multiple times, gradually increasing the amount each time, until all the pus comes out; do this especially if the patient has weak strength, such as women, young children, or elderly decrepit men.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	 For the spirit (i.e. pus) may suddenly burst forth with the evacuation of pus, which may accidentally cause the death of the patient, and you would not realize it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Avoid this chapter with great care, and when you have lanced your abscess, wash the wound, and see if the abscess's wound is small; and if it is a clean cut, then apply strips of linen or old cotton; and if it is large abscesses, and there are many holes, then you must put in each one a strip so that they come up against each other; and if you have cut off a piece of skin from the abscess and left it hanging, then you must fill it with old cotton or linen rag without moisture, and bind it for three days; then remove it, and treat it with ointment until it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	 And if bleeding occurs during your work, bring cold fresh water and wet a cloth, and apply it to the wound several times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the bleeding persists, apply a treatment and the powders that I mentioned in light hands in this book, and if it is during winter, and the place where the abscess is is very sensitive, then you should put up tents and wet cloths in hot wine and oil; and if it is in the summer, and the place is fleshy, then you should put wet cloths in water and oil, or in wine and cold oil, until the third day, as we have said; and then unbind the abscess and dry and treat it, as appropriate, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this is what must be universally known in the treatment of abscesses: I have told you how to proceed with the treatment of abscesses, and here is the chapter.
