Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	 Where small abscesses of the head come, and are shaped like blisters, as the hock of a chicken, and there are many similar ones.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	 Some of them are fatty and similar to boils, where there is moisture like pus; and some are hard and stony when cut into, and there is no doubt that the artery opposes it.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	 And the procedure for cutting is that you should test every instrument called "entromissoire", of which there are several kinds, to see what it contains.[Comment: The word "entromissoire" may refer to a probe used in surgery, and "li forme vient ci aprés" implies that more information about the different types of probes will be provided later in the text.]
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	 Because if it contains moisture, you should split it lengthwise.[Comment: The word "moistor" likely refers to pus or other fluids that may be present in the body and need to be drained.]
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	 And when the moisture is evacuated, thoroughly skin it without leaving any of the skin that contains the moisture, for it will return if anything is left; then soak a cotton swab in Egyptian ointment, if available; if not, in water and salt, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and those staying overnight will take care of it.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And then repeat the process with a new cotton swab, as before, on the second and third day, until you are certain that no moisture remains overnight; then treat the wound with appropriate ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	 And if the abscess contains foul matter, cut it in length as follows: insert your lancet and throw your linen on it, then skin it all around and focus your care on removing the pus; and if an artery opposes you, do what I told you before.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	 And likewise do for the abscess if it is hard, and for cutting and curing as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	 And cutting into a hard and moist abscess is easier, for they contain little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	 And if there are some abscesses in the head or neck that have no moisture, and these are the kind of abscesses I cut into on the head of an old woman; and I found the abscess to be as hard as a rough and white stone, unable to break; and if one had struck it with anything, it would have caused as much damage as being struck by a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	 In other abscesses appearing on the head, except those that appear on children's heads and at the roots of ears, the incision should always be made as low as possible so that pus can easily drain out; and cure them as necessary.[NOTE: I am a helpful, respectful, and honest assistant. I will continue to assist you in translating this text to the best of my ability.]
des scrophules	"Scrofula" is a medical term used to describe a group of diseases characterized by the presence of swollen lymph nodes, typically in the neck. The term comes from the Latin word "scrofa," which means "she-pig," likely because the affected lymph nodes can resemble the swollen glands of a pig. Scrofula is also known as "the king's evil" because it was once believed that the touch of a king or queen could cure the disease. This belief dates back to the time of King Edward the Confessor in England and was continued by subsequent monarchs. However, this practice has been abandoned and there is no scientific evidence to support the idea that royal touch can cure scrofula. Scrofula is usually treated with antibiotics, but surgical removal of the affected lymph nodes may be necessary in some cases.
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	 Many times, these abscesses occur on the neck, and below the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes they appear elsewhere on the body, and they are large, and are interconnected with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	 And each scrofula is specifically within its own cavity, just like the glands and abscesses of the head, as we have said; and the likenesses of these scrofulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	 There are some that contain moisture, and there are wicked ones that do not want to obey health.[Translation note: I assumed "santeit" is a typo for "santé", which means health in French.]
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	 Then in the one that you see with good disposition when touched, and it resembles the color of the body, and moves from every side and is not swollen in the nerves of the neck or in the artery or vein, and is not deep; then you should cut it open from above, and remove the skin from every part, and extend the two lips of the flesh to the oncines, if you need, as we have said in abscesses of the head; and press and drain the pus repeatedly, and be careful that you do not cut the nerve or vein, and let the scalpel not be too sharp or cutting, so that the hand does not slip, and do not penetrate too deeply, so that you do not cut something that you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	 And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not let you work, put in the wound vitriol powder, or any powders that stop bleeding, and bind the wound; and leave it until the abscess has calmed down, and the wound has softened and begun to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	 And when the bleeding has stopped, return to your work until you have completed it; then examine with your skilled hand if any small scrofulous sores remain, cut them and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	 And if there is a large vein at the root of the scrofulous sore, it is not appropriate to cut the sore at its root, but instead bind it with strong double thread and let it fall off by itself without harm; then apply the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then bandage it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	 And if you cut out the entire scrofula, it is necessary that you bring together the two edges of the wound and sew it up, since there is no remaining excess due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	 It is necessary that you attend to cutting the root of it and pulling it out, and sew it up as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 For those scrofulas that have an excess, pierce them where they appear to be mature; and pierce them as previously mentioned, in dependence, then apply bandages with a compress and similar things so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, cure it with a compress of healing herbs until it is healed.

Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke of the operation (or cutting) of the throat; but I never saw anyone in our land who performed it, and this is the writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	To those who have squinting, it is necessary that the slit of the throat called "epiglotte" be cleared; and this is not done with help, because all the veins and the windpipe of the patient are blocked by those who have a hot abscess in the mouth, or in the throat or in the two amygdales.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the sickness is in the channel of the windpipe, it is necessary to cover the epiglotte to avoid suffocation which comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	 Therefore, when we wish to split the epiglottis, it should be split below three or four circles, making a small slit across, between the two circles or according to the length of the slit in the syphac, not in the cartilage; and these places are suitable for splitting the epiglottis where there is no flesh, and the vessels are long and empty.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	 And if the master is afraid, he should stretch the skin of the throat as far as possible, then split the windpipe until it reaches the trachea ring; and avoid cutting any blood vessels, if you see anything; and then cut the syphac as we have said; and this is demonstrated by the section of the tracheal ring that jumps out through the broken hole, and by the loss of voice; and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed where there is doubt about strangulation, bring together the two lips of the windpipe wound and sew it all the way up to the cartilage; then administer medicines that promote tissue growth until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Al-Zahrawi (Albucasis) says that this should not be done until the throat is completely stuffed up and the patient is judged to be at death's door with respiratory distress.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	 Then cut the epiglottis so that the patient cannot swallow, and they breathe through the wound, and thus they are kept from death; and for this reason, the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the evil of the illness has passed, and it passes in three or four days. And then they command to sew up the wound and cure it, until it is healed; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	 I saw that a young lady took a knife and plunged it into her throat, cutting part of the tendons in the windpipe; and I was called to cure her, and found her as if she were dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that had issued from it, and knew well that it had not received any venesection or surgical attention except for the throat, and the wind was escaping through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	 I hurried and sewed up the wound, and cured it until it was healed; and nothing happened to the young lady except that she lost her voice and regained her composure; for this reason, I say that in cutting the epiglottis, there should be no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the thick throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	 These abscesses are called "goiter hernias," and are large abscesses in the color of a lump, and are very common in women; and are according to two ways: natural and accidental; where the natural one has no remedy.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 And the accidental [goiters] are according to two manners, one of which is similar to fat, and the other manner is similar to an abscess that comes from an artery; and there is fear, and one should not operate by cutting outside of it unless in the case of a small one, and prove and search the entirety of the inserted [goiter]: if you find it like our fat, and it does not bleed from any vein, then cut it as one cuts fat, and pull out all its covering, if there is any; and search well early, and cure it as required, until it heals perfectly.
des nous	of the nails.[*](Note(s): The translation "of the nails" is based on the assumption that "nous" in this context refers to fingernails or toenails. However, it is possible that "nous" could have other meanings depending on the context in which it appears. In general, "nous" can refer to either the plural form of "nous" (meaning "we") or to a reflexive pronoun (such as "himself," "herself," or "itself"). However, in this case, neither meaning seems plausible. Therefore, it is reasonable to assume that "nous" refers to nails.)
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	 Many ways are there, which I will tell all the similarities; and now it is appropriate that I say all the difference which is between nature and dislocation.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that issue is heat and fever persisting until the boiling has passed and the decay is complete; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	 With nature, there is no heat or fever or pain, and it contains pus, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins as a small lump and becomes large; and there are two similarities, either fatty or moist, and very colored, just as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of dislocation, that you first test and inquire about all the instruments which are called "entromissors," according to the form which will appear in the chapter which follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	 And the manner of inquiry for abscesses in the body is that you take the moistest place that you find in the abscess, and turn your fingers back and forth, so that you know that the instrument has penetrated the core, according to the size of the abscess; then extract the intrusive object, and be careful that it does not break apart.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	 If moisture runs and corrupts, whatever color it has, then lance it as I have said for other abscesses; and if after the incision moisture does not come out, know that it is fat, then lance it in a cross shape, and take it with forceps, and lightly scrape it from each side and ward the skin where it lies so that you draw it out whole with the pus; and if you cannot draw it out whole, then draw it out piece by piece so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	 For if anything remains, the pus will return many times; and if some remains, and the blood bothers you, then apply corrosive powder to the wound, bind it up, and place something warm and soothing for an abscess on it, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed; and if the pus is large, then cut the two edges of the wound, and treat what festers in the flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the boiling blood is against you or something else, hasten and use the liquid of broken vitriol, and let it stay for two or three days until the wound putrefies and the ebullition of the blood settles; then apply a new covering to what remains.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	 See here the forms of introductory instruments, and they are of three types: large, medium, and small; and there are three squares called "albaret", and one that is called "breb", and there are also three types: large, medium, and small, to encircle abscesses of fistula; and they are similar to the needles used to sew up wounds, and are made of citrine bronze, or iron, or silver, and the new ones are more valued, and are better proven for encircling the hollows of fistula; and there are three types: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the openings.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	 The shapes of the kidneys are of many similarities, as you can see here: large, medium, and small ones; and there are kidneys that have two indentations of three types; and there are kidneys that have three indentations, and they are also of three types; and there are kidneys that have two indentations, and some have only one indentation, and they are of three types; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	 The tips of these (kidneys) that are cut are sharp, and there are some that only cut on one side, so as to flay the flesh without cutting the vein or nerve; and the needles that are inserted are placed in handles, so that the patient does not feel them when opening abscesses; and they are of three types: large, small, and medium, as you can see; and one never uses them except in fleshy places, such as legs, arms, breasts, and armpits, and similar locations; and sometimes one makes another instrument, resembling the scabs of ulcers, of this shape, to stop bleeding.

des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses in the armpits.
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come under the armpits are types of hard scrofulous swellings or they have cores, and some of them contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	 Then those who contain moisture should have their hair cut in this manner, from line b to line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the abscess has been drained, fill the wound with clean cotton and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton and apply a suitable ointment to it until it heals.[*](footnote: The word "ceu" is not a standard English word. And if the abscess is similar to scrofulas, lance it as we have said for scrofulas, and if the wound becomes pus-filled again, apply a hot iron as we have mentioned before.[*](footnote: The word "devant" in Old French means "before," referring to an earlier part of the text.)
de la routure de l’artere	from the rupture of the artery.
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	 When an artery is injured and the skin above it is stuck down, swelling often occurs, and the same happens when a vein becomes engorged and swells; one can recognize this as being due to the artery if the swelling is long and deep; and when you feel it with your hands, it feels tight; and when it is due to a vein, the surface appears uneven; and it is foolish to cut into this swelling, especially when it is located beneath the nails, under the joints or near the neck and in many other places, and is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then it is necessary to avoid the cure of iron, and also to avoid touching the head, and in one who is swollen from an artery burst above the skin; then make an incision at the edges, and neatly separate the artery from the surrounding tissue, until it is exposed; then place a needle underneath it, and pierce it to the other side, and constrict the artery with a double thread in two places, as I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples; then insert an instrument into the space between the two ligatures until the blood within comes out, and let the abscess be released; then make the incision small enough so that it heals quickly, until the ligature falls off; then cure it with a suitable ointment until it is healed; and if the abscess is due to the incision of the vein, then stain your hand with what you can of the abscess over all the skin, then insert the needle underneath the place you are holding, and pierce it, and let there be one double thread, so that you pull it from the other side; then bind the abscess as I have told you, with the ligature of one of the two ends of the double thread; and if you fear that the threads may come loose, then insert another needle underneath all the abscess to the incision of the first needle, and constrict the threads in four places; then cut off the excess of the abscess until what remains is bound; then cut away the excess skin and leave what is bound; then place a wet cloth soaked in wine and oil on it, then apply dressings and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as an abscess can occur in the artery and vein, an abscess can also happen in the nerves when they are wounded or from excessive labor and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	 And this happens more frequently in the shoulders and hips, and in all places where there are joints, especially when there is an abscess; its color resembles the color of the skin, and it is in various dispositions without pain; but when squeezed firmly, the patient feels pain, and it is not deep within the body, but beneath the skin; and it can move in all directions, neither forward nor backward, nor downward nor upward; and a joint should not be covered with iron, for it may cause contraction; and if it is in the head or forehead, it makes the skin swell up.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the abscess is small, hold it with forceps and cut into its root; and if it is large, suspend it with a string and peel it, then remove it and stitch the wound closed, and care for it until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	of large, dangling breaks/fractures
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	 Sometimes there appear in the belly and not elsewhere "thelul", and it is a disease called "funge" due to its resemblance to them, and it has fine roots and large excrements; and some are small and others very large; and I saw a man who had two such fungi in his belly, which were more similar to fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had thin roots, and were jagged, and moisture was constantly running from them.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	 I weighed them and found that one weighed eighteen ounces, and the other six; and in performing the incision, look to see if the patient is moist, and the color of the "artelul" (excrement) is white and moist with fine roots; then use a large spatula, and have the cautery prepared with fire in your presence.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	 For when cutting, there often comes a great loss of blood, and if the blood flow overcomes you, then hurry to use the cauterizer; and if you see the patient frightened and fearful of the incision of iron, then take a well-made flax thread, and tie the artery as we have said, and leave it for two days; and then tighten it and never cease tightening the flax thread until it cuts the artery, and this will happen without pain; and if the roots are thick, then there is fear of cutting the same due to the belly, but you can easily cut half of it, then cauterize it so that it does not grow back; then cure the wound, and take care not to cut the vein which is of a fleshy color and poor sensation and has a milky appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an inflamed abscess, and I will come to the treatment of the chancre later.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the abscess bursts open.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	 If the appearance of the swelling comes from a cautery of a wound or a crack in the syphilitic sore, and is located on the abdomen and in some cases in the buttocks, as it happens in other ruptures, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what is before, or from flatulence; and if it is due to the rupture of the syphilitic sore and the issue of the intestine, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the flesh, and is a light thing without pain, and has a diverse opening.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the issue of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when pressed with one's fingers, it protrudes and then returns, and perhaps it becomes constricted, and greatly enlarges at the entrance of the bath and after heavy work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	 And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing, and appears clearly when you press it with your hand, and do not constrain it; and if it is due to blood, then the abscess is large and hard, and fixed according to a quantity; and if it is due to flatulence, it is soft to the touch, and the operation consists of looking to see if the appearance is due to the blood of the artery, or of the vein, or flatulence.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	 So you must let the wound heal.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	 For there is doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter on abscesses, because of the artery and vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	 And if the appearance is due to an intestine or a boil, you must instruct the patient to fast and lie flat, then girdle their belly tightly; have them lie in your hands, then go around the place you marked for the entire duration of the incision, then extend half of the abscess above with a large probe; then bind it tightly with strong thread or a cord of strong silk, leaving enough slack for swelling; then perform the incision on the extended half of the abscess, and insert your index finger, searching for the intestine; if you find it caught in the ligature, release it and push the intestine back into the abdomen; if you find the boil, take hold of it with the probe and remove any excess; if an artery or vein is opposed to your incision, carefully move around it and then return to your work, taking two needles and inserting them crosswise where you made the incision; then pull the abscess taut in four places on the needles, and if you see pus, remove the needles and leave the wound open until it dries out, allowing the dead tissue to fall away; or cut it away when it has become thin and rotten; clean the wound as necessary, and bandage the abscess as we have described; then extract any blood or pus you find, clean the wound as needed, and suture the wound.
dou chancre	of the chancre
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the similarities of chancre, and how one should work on it with medicines, and how to avoid the cure of iron; and we say that the chancre swells in the groin, and requires great caution in its treatment. And the ancients said that when a chancre is in a place where it can be scraped, such as a chancre that is on the breasts, or on the thigh, and similar places, one must completely remove it when it first appears. And when it becomes large and old, one should not approach it at all, for I have never cured any; nor has anyone ever cured any before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the operation, when it is in a place where it can be removed, as we have said, is that you purge the patient of black bile once; then make them sweat if they have obvious bloating; then prepare the patient for the procedure with one good location for performing the operation; then cast your leeches or chancre and all the hairs from around it, and remove everything without leaving anything behind; and let the blood flow freely, and wipe clean the area with your hand or some other object, and if the bleeding caused by the incision of the artery or vein is contrary to you, cauterize until the bleeding stops; then cure the wound with another cure until it heals.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	 We have previously spoken in the division about the similarities of dropsy, and how the gathering of water is made, and the signs of each type, and the cure that is done by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: only a blister; and one should not touch with iron in these two types: namely tympanites and hydrops ascites, for it is a deadly thing; therefore when you treat this type of dropsy with medicine, which is called "blisters," and the cure does not help, look if the patient is weak, or if he has another illness besides dropsy, such as pleurisy and loosening of the bowels and similar things; then do not touch it with iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient of strong virtue, and he has no other illness but dropsy only, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you should proceed in this way: lift the patient up straight on your hands, and have the assistant press the belly by pushing the water to the lowest part of the abdomen, then take the pointed spatula in this shape:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	 And let it be cut in two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	 And let it be pointed, yet not so sharp that it can reach the intestines when inserted and not harm them; then check if the dropsy has spread towards the intestines: if so, you must make an incision above the swelling three fingers wide directly under the arm; and if the dropsy is due to liver disease, let the incision be on the left side of the swelling, and if it's due to spleen, let it be on the right, and it is not necessary for the patient to lie on the incision so that excess fluids do not flow to the weaker side; then pierce through all the skin with the instrument, insert it, and lift your hand in a space of half a finger width between the skin and the abscess as when lancing to the depth of a fingernail or thereabouts; then pierce the abscess until the instrument reaches the visible spot, which is the watery place, then pull it out, and insert this instrument (the form of which is described earlier).
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	 And it is similar to a thin silver hinge, and is made of light bronze or iron, and has a small hole in its lower part; and on one side, there are three holes; and two on the other side, and one on the other; and the shoulders are cut like a feather quill, and this is the shape of the incision that writers make when sharpening their quills.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	 At the top is the reservoir, so that when the instrument comes to the water, it sinks down now on the instrument; then empty out half or a third of it, for if you empty more than necessary at that hour, the patient may die from the resolution of their spirit through the weapon, or they fall unconscious, or they approach death; but empty it according to its strength and according to what the dispositions of the patient's strength indicate and their pulse; then pull the instrument and hold back the water, and it is now held back by the stopper that plugs the hole which I spoke of earlier, which you pierce in this manner; then replace the instrument the next day if you see the patient tolerating it, and draw out a small amount of water; do this for several days, and be careful not to overfill it so that there is only a little water left.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	 And if you doubt the patient, and leave too much water, then cure it with sepulture or hot sand, and by sweating or bathing in the sun, and dye it with drink; and cure it with drying medicines until it is healed, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of water, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stopping of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	 Not at any time does a child born have no opening in the foreskin, or the opening is small, or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	 It is necessary for him to have pierced immediately with a very fine probe according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	 then place or insert a thin piece of sponge in the urethra, and bind and hold it for three or four days, and when he wants to urinate, remove the stopper and let him urinate, and then replace it; and perhaps it is not necessary, because the urine that comes out does not allow it to stay closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	 If his urethra is narrow, then he should be treated with a sponge stopper, as we have said, and it will widen.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	 Those whose urethra is not in its proper place are injured, because some are born with the urethral opening at the tip of the penis, for which reason they cannot urinate unless they lift their penis upwards; and they cannot ejaculate because the matter cannot reach the exit, and this is a bad illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the method of the procedure is that the patient lies down on his back, then stretches out the head of the penis and holds it in the shape of a pen's nib, so that the opening is in the middle as it should be; and be careful of bleeding which often occurs, and if it happens, stop it with a styptic and cure the wound until it heals.
des pustules de la verge	of pustules on the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often these ulcers appear on the penis, and it is an ugly appearance of flesh; and there are malignant and non-malignant ones; so you must take them with a subtle lancet, and cut and clean all of them, then put a cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment on it; then cure it with Diafinicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	 And if the abscess is harmful, of putrid color and foul-smelling, then you should apply a fire cautery to it.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	 After you have lanced it, and if the abscess is on the shaft of the penis, with part of it under the skin and part outside, then you must remove the one that is inside first; and when it has drained, heal the outside part.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Because when you heal it all at once, the head of the penis is not assured that it will not be pierced, and blackness and corruption will come to the penis and anus; then cut away all that is blackened and corrupted, then bind with a poultice of honey and flour made from the bark of pomegranate rinds and vinegar, then heal with other healings until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	 And if there is an outpouring of blood, then moderate the moon causer according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	 The causer has two functions combined: namely, when there is an outpouring of blood and when there is corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, then you must insert a piece of willow cane into the penis, and let the patient urinate through it; and when the hairs are dry at the tip of the penis, which happens to those who have not been circumcised, or due to a wound or abscess, then you must scrape it with a small knife until the ligament is loosened and the head of the penis is released from all sides; and if this is difficult to do, then you must scrape it with a scalpel at some point on the tip of the penis and the skin; then gently separate them and place a thin linen cloth soaked in cold water between them, so that it does not become wet again.
de la circoncision	Here is the revised translation with "de la circoncision" added:
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not the same as the loosening of continuity like other wounds; nonetheless, when we perform this work willingly and particularly for children, it is necessary that we do the best work and the easiest one for health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not use circumcision for their children since it was not part of their law, and we only have what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	Because I have seen that most masters and surgeons who performed circumcision around one thumb's width and with force, using a novacule, avoided the area because there are two layers there, and perhaps they cut the one above and leave the one below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or they cover it up, and the pain is doubled, and with the cleansing of the wound from the thumb's width, there is no certainty in the cleaning of the wound; and during the cleansing of the nail, perhaps the iron slips and ruins the work, and many times it happens that they do not need to clean it and I have seen this.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	In the cleansing performed with force along the entire length of the incision, I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forces (surgical knives) cut precisely both above and below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 For when you press your hand, cut evenly in the shape of an "I" all the time; but let the thread be well tight around the skin; and let the first task be to make the child, if they pay attention, think that you are only tying the thread around the member and not hurting them; then make them happy in every way you can; then place it straight between your hands, and apply pressure between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see, nor any of the instruments; then place your hand on the member and blow or cough, and pull it up until the foreskin of the member is exposed; then clean it well of the dirt that has accumulated, then bind the area with a double thread, then bind it under the scrotum to another ligature; and hold it for two days by the second ligature at the thumb and index finger, and cut between the two ligatures; then quickly lift the scrotum and pull the foreskin; then let the pus flow out, for this is beneficial; and put powder on it and on the powder a piece of cloth glued with a half of an egg white cooked and tempered with rose water, infused with good and fresh rose oil, and leave it on until the next day, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forceps for cleaning is as follows: the two heads should be sharp and even, and should be of equal size to the little finger.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in cleaning is when the core within runs out at the incision; then you must stretch it to your fingernail so that the place forms an abscess; and cut it evenly, and if you cannot hold it with your finger, then hold it with pliers, and then cut it.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they pass three days, and what is beneath the groin is swollen, leave it until the abscess has calmed down, and gently flay it; cut as you can move it, and be careful near the part of the groin, it will not harm him at all.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal the wound of things that have grown together with powder, as we have said in the treatise on powders, and if you cut beyond measure with a knife and it goes too high, it will not harm; heal it then, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	of urinary retention
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	 The holding back of urine is due to a blockage from a stone, congealed blood, pus, flesh rot, or similar things, which we have mentioned in the division; and if the urine is not released and you see that the retention is due to a stone located in the neck of the bladder, then the patient should bend on their knees, place their feet on their back, stretch their belly over the back, and restrain the patient's abdomen as much as they can; and then the neck of the bladder is constrained for the expression of the stone above, so that the urine is released; and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you should administer extraction with all the instrument called "siringue", of which this is the form: and be made of thin and light silver, like the feathers of a bird; and let the cane be one palm and a half in length, and be fine at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	 And the manner of urine retention is as follows: take a double thread, and tie one end to the head of a wool or cotton rag, and insert the head of the thread into the syringe; and cut off the excess wool and push it up to the head of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and egg yolk, and have the patient sit on a seat, and anoint the bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and warm water; then gently insert the syringe into the penis, until it reaches the base of the penis, then fold the penis over the bulge; then push the syringe forward to the bladder, and have the patient feel it reach the empty space, and this is not done in this order except that the conduit through which it passes is twisted; then pull the thread out along with all the wool rag, and allow the urine to flow; and repeat the process until the bladder is emptied, and relieve the patient.
des maladies de la vessie	diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When ulcers or blood come into the bladder, or if pus has accumulated, and you wish to distill water and medicine into it, then use an instrument called a "clepsydra," which is shaped as follows:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	 It is closed, and has three openings: two on one side, and one on the other, as you can see; and the location for inserting the medicine container should be such that it effectively stops up the opening, allowing one to draw out moisture and push in when necessary; and when you see fit to administer your medicines into the bladder, place the tip of the container in the moisture and pull gently on the attached string; by pulling the string, you will pull the moisture into the container, and then strongly replace the string; the moisture will enter, and come to the bladder immediately, so that the patient will feel it; this is the subtle form of the enema used to cleanse the bladder. Here it is:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	 And it is made of silver or brass, and the head (noisemaker?) is higher up; and below is the bladder or the location where it falls; then take a sheep's bladder and put in it the moisture which you want to use to cleanse the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts with a strong double thread, and heat one corner of the moisture over the fire; then insert the head of the enema into the penis, then strain your hand on the bladder until all the moisture has entered, so that the patient feels that the moisture has reached the bladder; and if you don't have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle out of it, and pierce it evenly around; then insert a strong string through these holes, then gather the circle like a bundle, and put inside it what you want of oil and moisture and water, and tie it in the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, to press with your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	"from the stone" (in this context, likely referring to a kidney or bladder stone that is being treated with the enema)
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have previously said in the division the kinds of stones, and the extraction together with their medicines; and I have said the difference between the stone stuck in the kidneys, and all the signs, and in what kind of stone one should work by cutting; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell it to you plainly and concisely.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is stuck in the bladder happens more often in children, and this is a sign that the water jumps from the bladder similarly to water in its subtlety; and it appears sandy, and the patient urinates with difficulty, and urinates frequently, and then becomes rigid; and there are many of these jumps; and the foundation is light in children until they reach 4 years old, and it is very grievous in the elderly, and it is moderate in those who are between youth and old age; and the treatment is easier for those who have large stones, than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	 And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary to first purify the patient with an enema, to draw out all the filth that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	 For it sometimes hinders the search for the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	 Then take the patient by the feet and raise them up, moving him downwards so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder and sometimes comes out; then have him sit between your prepared hands, with his hands under his thighs, so that the bladder is entirely tipped downwards; then search for and touch it inside; if you feel the stone in its place, hurry now to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	 And if it does not fall at the touch, moisten your index finger with oil from your left hand, if the patient is a child, or your middle finger, if the patient is a mature adolescent; and insert it into its foundation, and search for the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, pull it by the collar of the bladder; then press with your finger, and push it out where you want to make the incision.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the assistant to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to lift the hips with his right hand and remove the skin beneath the hips on the side where the incision is made; then insert the spatula, which has the following shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	 And make the incision between what is between the hips and the anus, not in the middle but to the left side of the anus; and let it be straight above the stone, and your fingers should always be on the foundation, and let the cut of the incision be wide in front, and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, and not too large; perhaps the pressure from the finger that is in the foundation will make it jump out without difficulty; and know that there are some stones with angles and sharp edges: they are difficult to come out; and there are some that are swollen, similar to a gland, and round, whose exit is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	 Then at that place where there are angles and edges, make the incision larger; and if it does not jump out, you should pull with pincers that are like a file at the top, to extract the stone so that it doesn't shatter; or you put a thin curved instrument at the top; and if you cannot deceive it in this way, widen the opening a little, and if the flesh is thick, constrict it with vitriol; and if there is more than one stone, first place the largest one at the neck of the bladder, then cut on top, then pull it out, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	 And if it is very large, it needs to be sawed, and a larger wound needs to be made.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	 For two things happen to the patient: either they die, or urine repeatedly comes from the wound that cannot be healed; but nonetheless, strive to pull it out, or break it with pincers, as much as you can pull it out in pieces; and when you have completed your work, apply the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and bind it, and place above it a damp cloth soaked in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to appease the hot abscess; then turn the patient on their side, and do not loosen the binding until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you unbind it, rinse the area well with oil and water, then clean it with a diaphoretic ointment and a basilicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	 And if abscesses and corrosions come in the wound and congealed blood in the bladder, and urine is retained in such a way that it comes out with difficulty: then insert your finger into the wound and draw out the blood, for if it remains there, it will corrupt the bladder and cause it to rot; then rinse the wound with water and vinegar and salt, and help him in all ways that you know, until it is healed; and it is necessary that every hour that you care for him, that you bind his two thighs together, and apply the medicines to the place.
