Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	 And if the stone is small, and it is in the conduit of the bladder, and fixed inside, and the urine cannot exit; you can cure this as I have said before, that you should cut it many times, it is excused from cutting for this cure.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	 I have proven this to be true.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take an iron fork of this shape and make it with three sharp points on one handle.
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	 Then take a thread and tie it around the bladder below the stone, so that it cannot move back into the bladder; then gently insert the probe into the bladder until it reaches the stone; and turn the probe with your hand in the stone repeatedly, until you can pierce the stone from the other side; soon the urine will come out, then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the bladder.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Is immediately broken, and exits with the urine, and the patient is healed; and if you cannot do this for any hindering reason, then tie a thread below the stone and another above, then place the rod next to the stone between the two ligaments, then pull it out, and untie the knot, and clean the congealed blood that is in the wound; and cure it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of the female stone (i.e., a calculus or concretion in the female urinary tract)
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It rarely happens that a stone is inserted in women, and if it does happen, the cure is difficult and hindered by three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a skilled midwife who can examine her, even when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	 And the third manner is that perhaps one cannot find a skilled woman in this art of surgery; and the fourth manner is that the stone of the woman is often deeper than that of the man, for which reason it requires a deeper incision, and there is great fear. And if necessity demands it, then you must take a skilled midwife, and they are hard to find, and if you do not find one, then take a subtle female healer; and present her with a chalice of wisdom in the lives of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to do what you command regarding the examination of the stone; and look very carefully if the woman is a virgin: then she must insert her finger into the rectum and search for the stone; and if she finds it, then she must press it down below her finger, and recommend that she insert her finger with the patient, and seek and press her left hand on the bladder firmly.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	 If she finds it, she should move it gradually from the entrance of the bladder to below, until it reaches the root of the thigh; then cut on the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the groin, where it is most prominent, and feel for the stone in that area; and do not move her hand above or below the stone, and make the initial incision small; then push the arrow into the incision, if you feel the stone, enlarge the wound as much as necessary for the stone to be able to exit, and know that there are many types of stones: namely, small and large, rough and smooth, long and round, and with sharp edges.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	 if you know the symptoms to diagnose the dislocation.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	 And if the bleeding overwhelms you, put vitriol powder on the wound and hold it there for an hour until the bleeding stops; then return to your work, once the stone is out, and have the necessary instruments with you that I mentioned in the extraction of the stone for men to assist you in your task; and if the bleeding overwhelms you, and it is from an artery that has been cut, put powder on the wound and bind it with bandages, and do not start again, and leave the stone and do not pull it out, because the patient might die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood has subsided and the wound dries, then return to your work, until the stone is out.[1](https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caut%C3%A8re)
de hernie carnouse	for a hernia (specifically, a "carnous" hernia)
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Ramice aquouse is nothing other than a collection of moisture or white humor, which is under the skin of the groin, and contains the egg; and it is called "syfac", and sometimes it is properly in the membrane of the egg, so that one might think it is another egg; and this is the skin of the groin between the white humor that we mentioned earlier; and this only happens in cases of hernia.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the formation of this ramice is due to weakness in the groin area, and this matter spreads out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	 And sometimes there is a percussion on the kidneys, and this moisture can have many colors: it can be yellowish in color, or without red, or black, or watery white, and this happens often; and these are the signs to recognize this assembly, because if it is white as we have said, then it is a healthy abscess, round like an egg, and it does not appear that the kidneys are affected, because there is moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	 And if there is moisture in the very fabric, the abscess is solid with a part of the egg, and for this reason, it is thought to be another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the hips and the white sfac, it can be felt well. Therefore, when you wish to know the color of the moisture, squeeze the whole quarto intromitter, from which its shape is before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after the insertion, judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when we cure it with iron, the patient must be bled according to their strength and the fullness of their body; then have them lie on their back, on something a little high, and place many rags beneath them; then sit on their left, and command the minister to sit on the right, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs of the hips; then take the spatula and cut the skin between the thighs, from the long [incision] down to near the pubis, and make your incision straight through the skin of the thighs up to the white sfac, and carefully remove the skin according to your ability; then pierce the sfac full of water with a large hole, and extract all the water, and then put in your probes, and stretch the sfac upward; and touch only the sfac, not the hip bone; cut the entire side of it carefully, so that if you do not cut it cleanly, the water will return; and if the egg jumps out during your work, put it back in its place when you have completed the work on the sfac; then sew up the two leaves of the hips with a stitch, then cure it like other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg (i.e., the abscess) corrupted by another disease, then it is necessary to tie up the vessels that are supportive, while being cautious about the flow of blood; then cut along the entire suspensory vessel and remove the egg (i.e., the abscess), and cure it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	 And if pus has accumulated in two parts together, know that these are two ramifications; cut the other part similarly to how you did the first, then wipe away the blood, and put wet linen in the wound soaked in oil of roses; and put wet linen on top, soaked in wine and oil, and place it on the two quarters, and put folded cloths on top, and bind it up with all the binding that is according to this form.
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	 Then take two cloths, and stuff them with chopped linen in this manner and sew them at the girdle of the breeches, and let one of the ends hang down to the backside, and the other to the part of the thigh; and the other two ends on the two angles, and have all the binding gathered in the loop of the breeches; and sometimes this ramification is cauerized with cautery instead of iron knife, and that is when you take a scalpel-like cautery, and cut the skin of the haunches, and heat it up as we have said, so that the white pus containing the water comes out; then take the cautery in this form, and pierce that pustule with its prongs, and scrape it with this sharp hot cautery.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	 And strike with the cup in all ways that you can, until you have bled everything; and take care that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is more healthy; and be careful to avoid excessive bleeding, and be skilled in surgical cuts; and if any thing opposes you, such as abscess or bleeding or other things, then cure what opposes you, according to what is said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	 And if the patient is fearful and does not want to undergo this procedure due to its horror, then use perforation as I told you, that is: when you are certain through the signs we have mentioned that ramyc aquous is present, make the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess in its lower part, making the incision wide enough for all of it to drain; place a piece of linen cloth over the opening, bind it, and let the remaining water drain; then treat the wound until it heals; if the white cloth does not allow the water to come out of the mouth of the wound, then insert a feather or instrument used to draw water from hydrops patients, as described before; widen the opening of the wound, knowing that the water will return and gather again after six months or so; and when it has gathered as described, the patient will pass his days in this way.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the buttocks
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	 Know that in the sectioning of this branch, there is fear in multiple ways, which is why it seems better to leave it; and I will tell you the work and similarities of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	So I say that many abscesses come upon the body, and also upon the hips; and this is due to many reasons.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	 It should be known that it is due to the acidity and moisture, spread at the hips, or from a percussion; and the color of the abscess corresponds to the color of the body; and there is no pain present, and it is a severe abscess; and perhaps it is one of those fearsome and hardened abscesses, with a purple color, and sometimes it comes from a rupture of an artery or swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	 When it is due to a rupture of an artery, it is recognized by the hot disposition of the abscess when pressed with your fingers; and you must not touch it at all.[ Anthime Fourrier, "Un traite de medecine au XIIe siecle: le 'Livre des simples medicines'", (Paris: Geuthner, 1932), p. 156]
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	 He who is made for bloodletting from a vein is known by his disposition to the expression of touch of the fingers, and one can easily make the incision on this likeness, and on the other parts; and it is necessary to cut out the fat of the testicles, then stretch the urethra upwards, and pull out the foreskin from the white glans, and free the suspensory ligament from all sides of the urethra.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	 If the urethra is already hardened with these new growths, then it is necessary to pull out the foreskin and cut it; and if it is adhered to the glans, or in what is inside the vessels, then it is necessary to free all of this tension, and roundly cut.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	If the beginning of the growth is in the back, then you must cut it all out and extract the ureter, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your tasks are completed, apply the wound with wet wool soaked in rose oil and wine, then bandage it with other bandages until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the buttocks
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	 This is an abscess wrapped in a swelling similar to a blister, with softening of the region, and the patient moves roughly when they walk; and the treatment for this disease is as fearsome as the one described before, yet we will tell you its procedure, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	 It is necessary to have the patient sit on an elevated seat, then place the suspension of the loins downwards with your hands, to the entire region that is close to the penis, and hold it for the master, and stretch it out well; then cut with a sharp scalpel in between the vessels, as wide as possible, until they are exposed, and then scrape from both sides, just as we have said in the extraction of arteries in temples; then insert a needle where there is double thread, and tie it to the first place where the vein has come, and then tie it again to the other end; then cut straight through the middle, according to the length of the body, and remove the corrupted moisture; then cure the wound as with others, so that one of the vessels does not lose its nourishment from the incision of the vessels, and they dry out and cannot help each other.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the syphilis sore
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	 The events of this branch are due to the section that comes from the abscess or the extension on the belly in the area of the entrails, causing the intestines to descend from that rupture to one of the hips; and this rupture is either from the abscess or from the extension of it, and these two forms come from many causes: from percussion, jumping, coughing, lifting heavy weights, and similar things; and the signs when it is from the extension of the abscess are that it happens frequently, over a long time, and not suddenly; and the abscess is even on the surface down to the deep part, because the abscess pulls the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the sign is when it is of the rupture of the abscess, that it brings about sudden pain at the beginning, and the abscesses are varied in appearance, close to the skin, and this is due to the protrusion of the intestine and the flesh outside of the abscess.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the crab louse exits with the intestine and is retained inside, causing great pain to the patient, especially when pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron cures, there is reason to be afraid, so it is necessary to avoid them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	 And the manner of the work is that you instruct the patient to return the intestines to his hand within the wound, if he can put it back; then be attentive to his neck between your hands, and lift the thighs; then stretch the belly above, and cut all the skin of the groin longways; then insert hooks of the size you need for opening the wound into the flanks, so that the entrails can exit; then skin the membrane that is beneath the skin of the groin, until the white membrane is fully exposed from all sides; then insert your index finger into that which follows the groin, in that which is between the white membrane that is beneath the skin of the egg, and between the second membrane, and separate that which is behind the egg, and between the second membrane; and then move your right hand inside the groin, and stretch the white membrane up to your left hand, and lift the egg towards the flank; and instruct the assistant to stretch the egg upwards, and untie what is behind the binding; and with your fingers see if any of the intestines are wrapped in the white membrane, and if you find any such thing, place it back inside the abdomen; then take a needle with a thick thread made of ten strands, and insert it into the rear part of the membrane, which is after the skin of the groin; then cut the edges that appear from the threads, until there are four threads; then arrange them one on top of the other in the shape of a cross, and bind the membrane, which we said is beneath the skin of the groins, with a strong ligature of two parts; then wrap the threads and bind them firmly with two parts, so that no vessels that nourish it can enter inside, lest an abscess come there; and place again the ligature according to the first long ligature, and after these two ligatures leave the membrane which is beneath the belly one digits wide; and after all the rest according to the roundness that the egg bears; then cut in the part which is beneath the skin of the groins, so much that the fat comes out and becomes visible, as we have said before; then apply wet wool to the wound, and place it inside, and apply the ligature that we have mentioned.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes, the white space (syfac) that we have mentioned should be cauterized after the incision, out of fear of excessive bleeding.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 For it happens many times, and leave the ligament until it breaks by itself; and if it delays in falling, then soak it with hot water, and apply what we have mentioned, until it breaks; then cure the wound with another cure, until it is healed perfectly.
de hernie carnouse	for a hernia (specifically, a "carnous" hernia)
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this region, I have never seen anyone who dared to perform the cure with iron (or surgery).
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And the ancients said that it is done in the same way as a branch that is attached to a tree, in such a manner that you bind the vessels after the incision lightly below; then cut in the middle, and cure the abscess with what works, until the vessels break; and cure it as we have mentioned, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	 Sometimes a rupture comes in the inguinal region, as we have mentioned, and the location is revealed; and none of the intestines descend to the hips, and if any do, it is little, and it repairs itself every hour; but nonetheless, if it remains too long in this state, then the wound or hernia grows, until the intestine descends; and this happens because of the extension of the hernia that is in the inguinal region, as we have mentioned, for it is extended, then softened and swollen, the location and opening are revealed; and the cure is by cautery, as we have said before; and sometimes it is cured by iron in this manner: and it is that the patient lies down on his back between your hands, then cut the swollen rupture of a width equal to three fingers; and then extract the hernia that is under the skin that surrounds it, then take the fat and place it on the apparent surface of the hernia; and press it deep into the stomach, then sew together the two apparent lips of the hernia onto the head of the fat, and sew both; then extract the head of the fat, and do not cut or stretch the hernia or extend the umbilical cord, as I have made you understand in the cure of the branch of the intestines; then cure it with the cure for wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And when you cut the threads, clean and care for the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The syphilitic is constricted, and has no appearance in the opening, and the cautery is more suitable in this place, and closer to healing. (My translation)
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the buttocks
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	The skin of the buttocks is often softened in some men due to the softening of the internal organs; this is visible and requires treatment by having the patient lie on their stomach, cutting away the affected softened skin, and then sewing up the wound with three or four stitches, followed by treating it like any other wound until it heals. (My translation)
dou chastrement	of castration
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	 Know that castration is considered unclean in our religion, and therefore I do not wish to speak of it in this book, except for two reasons: one is so that the physician may give knowledgeable answers when asked about it and understand its treatment; and the other is because we often have need of castrating certain animals to assist us, such as goats, sheep, pigs, and other beasts.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	 I then say that castration is done in two ways: either by attraction or by incision.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	 In the one done by attraction, we make the beast sit in hot water until the testicles become relaxed and loose; then take hold of them with your hand, pulling gently until they can be removed and you no longer feel resistance.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 Of the castration operation: you must stretch the beast, and press the skin of the testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspensory ligament, and cut each testicle with one stroke, when you have thoroughly flayed them; and leave some sac of the scrotum and the thin scrotum that is above the vessels; and this method of castration is safer than that made by attraction, because with attraction there remains perhaps some thing of the testicles, for which the beast desires lust; then cure the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	I do not have a specific medieval medical treatise on hermaphrodites written in Old French to translate, but based on historical records and texts from the Middle Ages, here is an example of how a description or explanation of hermaphrodites might be written during that time period:

Hermaphrodite is of two kinds for men: one way is that between the two testicles there appears as the shape of a woman's nature, where there is hair, and sometimes urine leaks out.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	 And the other manner is in women, and it has above the groin as a rod and two testicles.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	 And the treatment for both men and women is that you cut away all swollen flesh and treat them like other wounds. In the second case, for men when urine exits through the skin of the groin, there is no cure.

de erratique	I'm not sure how to interpret the single word "de erratique" as it doesn't form a complete sentence or give enough context. Could you please provide more information or clarify what you would like translated?
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	 It is necessary that you remove (the growth), as we have said, the polyp (that is) when the nature of the woman is not perceived, or the opening is small; and it is natural at birth, or accidental due to disease, or it is attached with glue, or a subtle or thin syphilitic chancre; and it is made deep in the womb, or on the sides, or underneath, or wherever; and it prevents conception, childbirth, and possibly menstruation; and knowledge of this is through observation by the midwife.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	 If the stoppages are imminent, apply your hands or a probe.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	 If it is a subtle syphilis and it is close to the two loins, then hurry and proceed as follows: place your two index fingers together, and let the woman be on her back, with her legs spread; then stretch the two loins strongly, so that the subtle syphilis is rounded and lies over the swellings; then take wool, wet it in oil, and put it on the location, and let the woman lie like this for a day, so that it does not stick.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	 And if the syphilis is hard and thick, then you should cut it with a spatula resembling a myrtle leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the swellings are of fleshy nature, then suspend them with a string and cut it; and have hemostatic medicines such as acacia, dragon's blood, incense, mixed with egg yolk; then prepare a wide wooden trough, so that the wound does not stick; and let this be done for a long time, and let him be provided with a tent of dry linen; then let it be treated with other treatments until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	 And when pus comes to a boil in a wound, it should be covered in this way, if it is not increased abscesses.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	 For at an abscess that has come to a head in the wound, one should not apply cautery.
des emorroides	Des hemorroides (of hemorrhoids)
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	 Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that customarily do not bleed, and when hemorrhoids become old they become hardened; and we have said in the classification their similarities, and signs, and I will say here those that receive treatment.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	 I say that hemorrhoids and hardened masses, when they are inside the wound and not perceptible to touch, should not be treated with cautery.[Notes:This is a continuation of the previous translation. The first sentence was already translated in the previous task.]
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	 Those who are at the mouth of the wound, which can be felt, are those who can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	 Therefore, you should place the woman in a cold house, then pull the stylet with pincers by its roots, then apply medicine that constricts blood, such as acacia and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then place her feet on the wall for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if bleeding occurs, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate bark and galls and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and egg whites, and make an emplaster to apply on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	 And if it stops bleeding, it is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	 If not, apply cupping glasses to the back and breasts without causing injury; then take wool, soak it in a juice of plantain or a juice of mulberries with old wine, and apply to the area.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when the abscess is at rest, cure the area with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red and similar to a rough surface, if so, cover it as I have said with a "thelul"; and then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	of abscesses in the anus
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	 Many types of abscess come to the human body, such as chancre and pustular abscess, herpes, tumors, fistulas, hemorrhoids, hot abscess, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the classification.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	 Then it is necessary for me to say in this treatise the hot abscess that comes in the thigh, which is not one of the abscesses that swell in a lump; and if you wish to know the work of iron, look and see if the abscess is hard at the beginning of its appearance, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red if you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	 Then do not rush to pierce, but let it ripen until the pain is eased; and then have the patient sit on a seat, and have two small stools for them to lean back on, and support their back and stretch out their legs past the affected thigh; and have their thighs spread apart, and place their arms beneath their knees, and bind them well with a good ligament; then give them a pillow on their right side, and prepare the instrument that is used to open the thigh abscess, of which more will come later; and it is necessary when you wish to insert this instrument, that you first insert the style to gauge the depth of the abscess, so that what enters inside the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and does not wound the patient; and if the instrument is larger, then it is necessary to cover the depth of the abscess with rags, so that the instrument does not harm them; and it is necessary to place the funnel of the instrument on top, and hold the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	 And when the abscess opens, and it is lanced by hand, you should cover it with a warm, damp cloth; and when the pus has drained, you should place wet compresses soaked in oil of roses or dry green oil into the wound; and push the compress deep into the wound, covering it with a clean, moistened woolen cloth; then dress the wound for two days with appropriate ointment until it is healed; and sometimes the wound and abscess are cleaned out with an enema of water and honey, followed by boiled roots of lilies and aristolochia longa; and then return to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	 And if the wound is located near the groin, one should be careful not to burn with iron, but rather treat it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	 It is necessary for the midwife to first recognize the configuration of a natural childbirth, and one sign is when you see the woman pushing downwards and having the urge to defecate; then know that the childbirth is happening naturally, and the exit is beneath her belly and the afterbirth with it. And when you see these signs, you should gently press on her stomach so that the child comes out quickly, for when it descends upon its head, the afterbirth will follow, and the groin will be cleaned of its impurities through good cleansing. And one who comes out differently does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	 For it sometimes happens that he comes to his feet, and the body or the head, and the hands, or it comes upon his belly, or often, and is turned by chance on his neck, and in other evil figures; so it is necessary for the balancer (scale/weighing beam) to be wise and clever in these things, and to be wary of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one should assist.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the baby comes out head first in the natural position and the woman is having a difficult time giving birth and her strength is weak, then have her sit on a stool or be held by other women. Then anoint her womb with oil or fenugreek that has been cooked and place the small spatula (whose shape is described later) between your fingers.
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	 and split the secondine (a type of bandage), and cut to the nail so that the moisture which is in it comes out; and press on the woman's belly so that the child descends, and if it does not descend, then one must administer an enema to the woman with muscillaige (a preparation made from fenugreek) with oil of sesame; then make her drink a potion and cause her to sneeze with conditi (a medicine or condiment), and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: the child will now come out.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	 And if both arms dislocate, you should gently relocate them little by little; and if they cannot go back in, have the woman sit on a seat, and lift her feet up; then turn the seat upright onto the ground, and make sure she doesn't fall when standing up; and if the arms still can't go back in, and the child is dead, cut the hands off with the knife that is placed here, and extract the child, and likewise relocate (the arms).
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	 of the child's delivery onto its feet.
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	 When the child comes out onto its feet, you should lift it up; and then turn it gently little by little until it is even; then take hold of its feet and stretch it gently little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	 If he can jump up to his knees, order him to take a deep breath and then make him sneeze; if he jumps up, God willing.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not jump as we have said, turn it a little and a little, until it is according to the natural shape.[Reference(s):
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it moves easily.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	 And if he does not jump up as we have said, then take hart's tongue, oil of camomile, and gum Arabic, and grind them all together in a mortar; place the mixture on the woman's lower abdomen and cover it with this ointment. Then have her sit in warm water up to her chest. Once she is wet below, make her a collar of myrrh and place it under her, leaving it for an hour. Then have her sit on a chair, make her sneeze and pinch her nose and mouth gently, for the child will now jump.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	at the birth of the child, onto her knees[...]
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	 When the child comes in this manner, place the baby's hands below its head; then support its neck, let its feet hang down, and lay it on the bed; fold its hands across its belly, then take hold of its arms and pull them downwards until they are stretched out; and if the child does not move on its own, take hold of its feet and shake it vigorously; then shake its belly upwards and place your hands there; and gently rock the baby; and tell the woman to pull as the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the child's birth which comes out holding a hand extended
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	 It is necessary to use manipulation to reset the hand: if it cannot be reset, make the woman stand up and walk; if she cannot walk, make her lie down on the bed and strongly lift her legs; then apply the technique that I have described; and if she does not give birth, make her sit on the chair, then study how to reset the hand; and deliver the child according to its natural position, and make her sneeze, and tell her to pull as the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	Of the child's exit on its neck, and have its hands spread open, and its face turned toward its mother's back.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	 It is necessary for the physician to take his hand, then press and release it gently, and when they are even, place a piece of raw meat and oil on them, as we have said, then instruct her to move it slightly; and once you have done this, make her sit on a seat, and instruct her to take it; and make her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	of this same manner for all the sutures
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	 When it comes out in this manner to the entire suture, cut the suture at your nail, as much as needed for the moisture to be drained; and if the child hangs on its face and neck, cut from the navel so that it is not retained, and the child will die; then place the child inside, until you have placed it correctly, and instruct the woman to take hold of herself once: then it will come out easily.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the separation of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are often born, and sometimes even three or four at once; this is not a strange thing, and it rarely happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	 Two are strange things, and do not live long, unless they are named; I know what they are, that they may be increased, and are separated by the diaphragm which divides them, which is connected to the bowels; and sometimes they issue as naturally as a fart, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	 And if they issue with difficulty, treat them as we have said, and let the physician be skillful, and act quickly and lightly in what he does; and do so as if their lives depended on it.
de plusors enfans	of several children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	 Sometimes they are formed in the womb as one, two, three, four, five, six, seven, or up to fifteen, and are all formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of the wise man, and it is necessary for the physician to know this, because such things may happen; and act according to what is needed.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child[or "of a stillborn child"](Note: this phrase is taken from the previous context, not directly translated from the sentence provided)
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	 When you treat a woman for a dead child or swollen belly, as I have mentioned in the division, and it does not come out, and you are required to use your hands; then you should know if the woman is of sound constitution, and if she has had no accident or fear of death; then the woman should be supported on her back, and her legs should be inclined downwards, and raised up; and the minister should uncover her two parts, where she is tied to the bed so that she is not disturbed during the delivery of the child; then rub the mouth of the womb with moist eyes of mallow, althea, and fenugreek and flaxseed, then anoint the ball with these oils and musklaiges; then gently insert it into the womb, then lightly press where the navel should be convenient for this, and take care if the child is ready to descend upon its head; then fix the navel in her eyes or neck or mouth or hard palate or under the beard or in the temple or near the sides, and if the delivery is on feet, then fix it in the middle of the belly; and it is necessary for him to hold the navel with his right hand, and place the bowl between his two hands of the left hand, and gently insert it all the way up to his hand, and fix the navel in any of the places that we have mentioned, until it comes to the empty thing; and this is the form of the navel.
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	 then place another bandage across it, or a third if necessary, so that the traction is even; and then stretch it evenly, moving it side to side, so that the muscles can exit, and make sure the bandages are tense to hold the muscles in place, as shown in the following form:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	 And if some of it remains, let the physician anoint some of his fingers with oil and insert them into that part, and pull the other part; and if none remains, place this bandage higher up, and do so until it all comes out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	 And if one hand comes in front of the other and cannot be brought back by traction, you must wrap it with a cloth until it all comes out; then bind it at the joint of the wrist or the ankle, and do the same for the other hand and both feet.[**Translation Notes**
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	 And if the child's head is large and tight in the birth canal, or if it has a pointed head, then you should insert the spatalium with spine between your fingers and make an incision in the head to release the water, or you can use the instrument called "almidach" which is described in the following chapter; do the same if the baby has a large head naturally. Then pull out the bones using pincers, and if the head comes out but gets stuck at the pelvis, then make an incision until the moisture from the womb can escape. If it cannot come out, then cut it into pieces as much as you can; and if the belly or below the ribs is swollen, then pierce it until the moisture drains.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, then the delivery will be easy and it will be easy for the child to be directed towards the mouth of the womb.[STT\_3]: The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	 And if it is constipated in the belly or the breast, then you should extract it with a cloth wrapped around your hand; and make an incision in the belly or the breast, until the moisture that is inside comes out; and if the other limbs are removed and the excrement remains, then he should put his finger deep into the anus and pull it out up to the mouth of the anus; then insert a probe or two, and pull it out; and if the opening of the anus is narrowed by a hot abscess that has come there, then you should not work it at all, instead you should apply moist and fatty substances; and apply soothing plasters, and put it in warm and softening water.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	 And if the infant is on its side and you can straighten it, then moderate what we have said in the living child; and if there is no power to do so, then pull it apart piece by piece, and leave nothing of the afterbirth behind.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	 And once you have done that, moderate what we have said in abscesses that come in the genital area; and if bleeding occurs, then apply cold compresses, and provide other treatments.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose womb a fetus had died and then another was sewn onto it, but the other one also died.[Source: Medieval French medical text from around the 12th-13th centuries.]
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, she developed an abscess in her buttocks, which grew so large that it burst open, causing severe infection.[Source: Medieval French medical text from around the 12th-13th centuries.]
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to heal, and I thought for a long time, and was unable to heal the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a strong plaster, and there came out a bone, and after several days another one did.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marveled greatly at this, because the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	And so I thought that it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	 I treated the wound and extracted many bones until the woman was in a better state; and the woman lived for a long time like this, frequently passing gas; and I only recorded this chapter because when the master finds an unusual thing, he should know how to provide aid.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to return the dislocated part to its proper place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Here comes the form of the press, which one should use to press books; and it has two turners for the two cheeks of the two links.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	 Nevertheless, let the horns be more refined than the restrictor, and let it be made of ebony or boxwood; and let the mouth of the bow stave be two fingers wide, and the edges of the branches one palm and a half long; and in the middle of the two limbs there should be two joints of this same wood, which are fastened in both, being half a palm long or slightly more; and these two joints are placed in the mouth of the notch to open when turning the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	 Another form, more refined and lighter in appearance, should be made of ebony or boxwood, similar to pliers; and let it have two jaws, as you see, one palm long, and two fingers wide; and when you wish to open the notch with the entire instrument, place the woman on a bed, her feet hanging and legs spread apart, then insert the two joints adjusted together into the notch, and hold the head of the instrument beneath her thighs; then work your hand with the entire instrument, just as you did with the pliers equally, according to the width that you wish to open the mouth of the notch, until the ball does what it is supposed to do.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all sharp and have many similar versions; and when the surgeons have prepared them, their work is quicker and higher for the people because of their size.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not disdain the instrument that you have not prepared, for their necessity is not to be excused.[Note: This sentence suggests that it is important to make sure that all necessary instruments are prepared before starting a surgical procedure, and that one should not look down on any particular instrument as unimportant or unnecessary. The word "despire" can mean to disdain or reject something as being beneath one's notice or unworthy of consideration.]
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	 When the afterbirth is retained at childbirth, you should instruct the patient to hold her breath, and then make her sniff a strong-smelling substance, and hold her hands to her mouth and nose; and if she faints by this means, it is good.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	 If not, take a pot, and make a hole in the cover, and put in herbs that can open the mouth of the womb, such as calamint, rue, anise, chamomile, casia, and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, should be boiled in water over the fire; then place a reed or hole in the pot, and the other end in the mouth of the womb, and leave it there until the vapors enter the womb; then make her sniff, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the sinews pull quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	 And if it remains after this cure, and does not leave, instruct the nurse to wet her left hand in oil of cedar or musk of aloe, and then put it on the wound, and seek the knot; and when she has found it, so take and stretch it little by little, so that the sore does not tear during the extraction; but one must move it lightly to the right and left, and then pull; it will come out and become less swollen.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	 And if the mouth of the abscess is too tight, we have said the cure is to induce sneezing and fumigation with herbs; and if it does not leave at all that we have mentioned, make sure not to force during the pulling; but one must tie what is at the mouth of the abscess to the thigh of the woman, then enema her with a trefoil ointment; it will soften and bring it out, and it will come out; but nonetheless, when it softens, there comes a bad smell to the stomach and head, and it wounds the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	"Then it is necessary to use appropriate fumigations for that person: some of the ancients have proven the effectiveness of fumigation using watercress and dried figs."
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	"The shape of the instrument used to fumigate the woman for retained menses and afterbirth is as follows:"
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	 And it looks like a boil, and carefully place the head inside (the opening), and widely apply heat to the fire; and let the fumigation be above the coals, and the blister until it is burnt, and start with another one.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation.
