Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Many children are born who do not have a perforated anus, but instead have it stopped up with a thin membrane: therefore, the midwife must pierce that membrane to the right side, and not with a sharp instrument, and make sure the lacing does not touch it; then place wet wool soaked in wine and oil on top, then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you fear that it will swell, place a piece of wood into the wound, and leave it in for several days, and remove it when the child wants to go to bed.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes these stoppages come from a sudden wound or abscess; in this case, the wound must be covered and treated as we have said with a piece of wood.[Reference(s):
de la fistule dou fondement	of an anal fistula
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	 Fistulas that come from under the anus are swelling and grow near the anus, or in the space of two parts, whether it is one fistula or several; and when this swelling is old, it works, and still has moisture, white pus or thin pus, and sometimes these fistulas are persistent; and they are recognized by the fact that there is a discharge or flatulence when the patient makes a bowel movement, and perhaps in jumping, a worm comes out.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that reach to the bladder, and to the middle of the penis; and they reach to the joint of the thigh, and to the groin.[`screen`]
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	 And thus is recognized the fistula in the anus, and not: and it is that you insert your index finger into the anus, and insert a thin needle of bronze or iron into the fistula when there is no tortuosity.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	 And if there is tortuosity, insert a thin probe of plastic or horsehair until you feel it with your finger; and if you do not feel it, and no egestion or ventosities or fluid come out, as we have said: know that it has not pierced; so hurry to treat it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula has penetrated to the bladder or the conduit of urine, if the urine leaks out and cannot be healed by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	 If the probe has reached the joint of the thigh, then the probe has reached its place; if there is no tortuosity and no pain in the surrounding area, it is that it has already healed, and medicine or ointment is of no use; and in these fistulas, there is no cure except through hard work, and vanity from foolish physicians who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	 In the one who is not Persian and not ancient, there is hope of health through surgery, as I have tested, and it is that the patient lies in your hands on their back; and lift the legs up to the thighs, and have the thighs inclined towards the belly; then insert a tent stake of iron, or of wood if there is curvature, until you know where the stake comes out.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	 If the patient feels it around the rectum, then you should insert your index finger, and if you feel that the stake has pierced it; and expose the area where you feel between your finger the syphac or flesh, then know that it is Persian; and do not trouble yourself as it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	 Always keep in mind that some can be cured, but it happens rarely; and the help that one can provide is to heat the subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula, as previously stated; and insert it very hot into the fistula until it reaches the bottom; and do this twice or three times, until you are certain that the charred parts, which resemble a bird's feather, have burned away; and then cure it with wet bandages smeared with butter, until the char comes out; then cure it with a spreading ointment that heals and joins flesh.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 If it is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	 If it cannot be healed in any other way, and if there is a swelling, and it does not reach the finger that is at the bottom, and between your finger and the swelling there is a thick covering of flesh or abscess, and you see the fistula following the covering of the swelling; then begin by cutting from the beginning of the fistula, and push the swelling forward before the tent, and then apply the cautery until it reaches the end of the tent; and the swelling will be released and will fall; then burn away the charred parts that resemble a bird's feather, leaving nothing behind.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the blood flow is too strong and cuts between you and the procedure, cauterize it with fire or medicinal powder.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	 For the fire cautery brings about two good things: namely, the burning of gathered charcoal, and the stopping of blood and the drying of moisture; then the healing of damp tents smeared with butter or crushed herbs, until the place where the burned charcoal is placed becomes numb and the charcoal falls into the numbness; then heal the wound of hard, clotting ointments and let the medicines be dry.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is healed, it is cleaned and does not return again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes to the depth of the fundament, and is separated from the body, then insert your finger into it and examine (the condition).
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	 If you feel the tent (i.e., swelling), and between two there is cloth or syrup or charcoal, or it is close to piercing, let there be no hesitation, but rather trust and hope in the administration of one of three methods: either cauterize it as we have said, or cut it down to the root, or if you can, place tents and heal it as before; and do not go too deep, so that you do not cut the tissue that holds the foundation, and cause unwanted excretions there; then heal, as we have said; perhaps it will be healed, or you remove that covering and clean it after it has been cut next to the foundation, either with a tent or with another pointed instrument; then clean the faulty flesh that is in the wound, as much as you can; then strive to restore the wound and keep the fistula on the side of the foundation: it will be easier for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	 And sometimes fistulas occur in this manner: and it is when you insert the probe into the fistula, and it is next to the base near the skin above, then take a probe pierced at the tip in this form:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And insert a twisted wire through it, and insert the probe entirely along the wire into the fistula until it reaches the base.[4](#footnote_4_0)
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	 If it (the probe) is pierced in the margin of the base inside, then pull the thread from this perforation, as you insert your finger into the base; and pull the head of the thread, and bring the two sides together, and hold them close to each other, and leave it for one day or two; and tighten it occasionally, until the threads cut through the flesh between them, and drain; then cure the wound until it is healed and clean.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, make it pierce in all ways that you can, if it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Because it is not at all appropriate to cover the incision when it is so deep and then cure it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	 The shape of the spatalon spine that is used to make the fistula is very sharp on one side and cutting; and on the other side not, so that one does not cut what one should not cut, as you can see here:
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	 Piles (emorroids) are of two kinds: either they are inside the rectum, like grains of resin, and these can be small or large, and they often bleed, and there can be one or more, and they are located near the rectum and at the opening of the rectum; but those that are external have little moisture, and still sometimes there is a little yellow water or a little blood, and they have the color of flesh. And the treatment for those who have them inside the rectum is that you instruct the patient to strain when going to the bathroom, so that the rectum protrudes, and the threads can be seen; then hurry, and cut with pincers or hold it with your nail, then cut at its roots. And if the hooks cannot hold them because of their moisture, take them with a piece of cloth or cotton or from a piece of camelot; and pull them out with your hands, then cut them, and sprinkle some hot powders on them that are in place of cauterization; or cauterize them as it is said in the chapter on cautery, and cure them with other cures until they are healed. And if the rectum cannot come out, give the patient a harsh enema to clean what is in the rectum, so that it can come out openly. When the patient feels the urge, and when the threads are out of the rectum, then the cure is easy. And take them with your nail or with pincers, and cut them, then cure them as we have said until they are healed and be afraid of incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 You should prepare the suture in this manner: take a twisted thread and put it on a needle, then pull the thread over and make the needle pierce from the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread below the needle, and let it be of suitable size; pull the thread tight, then knot the thread, and remove the needle, and do the same with all the others, and leave one to draw out any excess blood; then place a damp cloth soaked in rose oil or cerote on the wound bed, and place it on the wound bed, and instruct the patient to rest; and let him rest until he urinates, and when they have passed, cure them with ointment and other care, until it is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	(the drying of pus or foundation)
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	It often happens that there is drying of pus in the intestines, due to constipation and the old age of the disease for which no medication is effective.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 It is necessary that you place the edge of a spatula or your nail on the skin above [the wound], preventing it from getting moist; then heal it until it is solid as it should be; and if it cannot solidify, repeat the shaving more forcefully than before, so that it heals well and becomes scabbed; then heal it until it is healed.
dou fremit	in a trembling state.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	 A formica is a small, harmful creature that enters the body and goes very deep; sometimes it is found by the doctor, and its presence is felt like a tremor, and it spreads throughout the body, but more so in the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	 The treatment is to take a quill from a goose feather, or a strong vulture feather, and place it on the tremor, so that the circle encompasses the tremor completely; then move your hand along the entire quill while scraping all around the tremor, pushing it in deep, and extracting the tremor from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you wish, do this with a reed of silver or iron, in the same manner, being fine underneath and dragging above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Not too deeply, in order to hold it with your fingers and press down on it; And if you wish, cauterize the frozen area as described in the chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the shape of the enema syringe
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Never is an enema made with silver or brass, or melted iron or lead; and never are these instruments small or large, depending on who they are prepared for.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore, those who are prepared for use in children's care and those who are weak and suffering are small (in size).
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the small and large enema syringe is as follows, where the stomach is bound in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	 And there is a dislocation where the belly is bound, as you see, and the feces are pierced inside; and has two openings on one side, and one on the other; and let the belly be where the medicines of an animal bladder or parchment are put in, and let it be pierced all around with small holes, and have one inch of space between each hole, then insert a strong thread twisted in X or spiral around, and bind the belly as if it were a sack; and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument in front with a strong thread, then enema; and this is the form of the circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	 And let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the head of the enema with oil or egg yolk, or similar thing, then insert it gently; then the minister presses it with both hands together until it is fully inside, then extract the enema, and raise the patient's legs in the air, and if the medicine wants to come out, let it come out as much as it can; and if he sleeps through the night, it will be a greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you give an enema to a patient with a disorder of the belly, and the medicine quickly comes out, then re-administer it until it is clear that they are better.[I'll continue with the next sentence:]
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	 And if there are piles or a abscess on the fundament, let the enema be as thin as for a child; and this is the shape of the thin enema where the leather is constricted:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have previously spoken in the division about wound treatment; now we will tell you of hand and medical treatments, according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and by what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	 The things by which wounds are made are by striking of a stone, cutting with a sword and knife, or a lance or stick or arrow, or similar things; or they are made according to the parts of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or the head, or the chest, or the stomach, or the liver, and similar limbs; and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and I will begin with simple wounds of the head, for the memory will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	 I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, take care if it is from a strike of a stone or similar things, and the skin is torn open and the wound is large, and you suspect a hot abscess: then have it immediately cauterized with the cephalic [part] itself if it comes out slightly bloody from the wound, and let the incision be on the opposite side of the injured part; and make the patient empty themselves of wine and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if he does not want to be cauterized, reduce his food and let him drink no wine, nor eat meat or any solid foods; and place on the wound, if hot abscesses come there, cotton soaked in rose oil only, or in stiptic wine; and if there is no hot abscess, place on the fresh wound, if it is still bleeding and has not been exposed to air, a powder that I will mention shortly; and if the wound has been opened by fire, place some poultices until it heals.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like that of a sword cut or similar, and the lips cannot come together by stitches, then bring them together with sutures, just as I will say for wounds of the belly.[Note: The phrase "de la costure" at the end refers to the practice of sewing or suturing. I have translated it as "sutures" here.]
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	 If the wound is exposed to the bone, and is gaping and only holds together by a small amount, then cut it; next, cure the wound with medicine, and replace hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat hearty foods, such as meat and roasted bread, also poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	 And if you find rotten flesh on the skin, and it is not attached to the bone, then cut away all the decayed flesh and discard it, then cure the wound; and if there is an artery in the wound or a vein, that cannot be stopped with medicine, then tie off the artery, and if you find it loose, then bind it with a thread; and if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the cure is easy: and that is to apply this powder which solidifies once the wound has moved (i.e., been cleaned).
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 And the manner of the powder is as follows: take one part of incense; dragon's blood two parts; and living lime three parts, and grind the powder finely, and apply it to the wound, and bind it firmly, until it dries out and joins with all its blood; and then bandage it well, and leave it unbound if it does not swell; for the medicine is not removed until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	Sometimes, quicklime is used alone if incense and dragon's blood are not available, but only after the wound has been cleaned by the practitioner.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the wound has festered due to pus, then do not apply this powder at all; but instead use digestive ointments or a poultice of barley flour made with water and honey until it discharges pus; then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	 And if the fracture of bones comes with the wound, and it is small, then pull it out with delicate forceps; and I will tell you later about the fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound in the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and one in the head, except if a nerve or artery of the neck is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	 If it is the nerve, there is no other device but to leave the wound alone and not put anything constricting, for it harms nerves and makes them retract; and do not apply anything cold to the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their connection is with the brain, which is the highest member; but let the medicine be warm, such as lime washed in soft water, and mixed with rose oil, and also lye boiled in soft water, and other similar stones in this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, suture and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	 And if the wounds are deep and wide and full of pus, pierce it lower down; and if an artery is cut and there is a flow of blood, tie it off, and bind it up, and cauterize it if necessary; and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the windpipe, and the passage is kept open so that food can pass, then sew up the windpipe to the neck bone, but do not touch the throat; leave it as is for some days, then cure it with discarded dressings until it heals; and if the wound has left an impression on the bone, seek it out; and if there are pieces of bone, pull them all out if you can, and those that you cannot remove, leave until the wound rots, and becomes loose and healed; and if the wound is fresh, powder onto it the powder that I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is a fistula, cure it in this way as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the spear or knife wound
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	 If it is a spear or knife blow, and the wound is deep, look if corruption comes out of the wound while the patient urinates: know then that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, do not put powder in it at once, nor bind it tight because the blood does not coagulate and returns to the heart, killing the patient quickly. Instead, put on a drawing ointment, and bind it twice a day; and if you don't have ointment, put old cotton in the wound to absorb moisture, and make the patient lie on the wound for 3 or 4 days; this way, no spasms, bad heart tremors, nor strangury will come; and when you see good signs, know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	 Treat then the abscess and other injuries, until it is healed; and if it cannot be healed, know that there is a fistula; treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	 And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and it is simple, whether on the belly side or the back, treat what is in front; if it is large, with stitches; and if it is small, with powder; and if it is close to the bone, and pieces have been chopped off, then clean the wound, and remove the fragments if they are separated; and if they are not separated, then let the wound rot, this will make the extractions lighter; and for other wounds in other limbs, judgement should be as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	"the rupture of the stomach" or "stomach rupture" would be a possible translation for "dou derrompement dou ventre". It seems to refer to an injury or trauma to the stomach that results in it being torn or ruptured.
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	 The ruptures of the belly are great, medium, and small; sometimes the intestines or the nerves of the intestines come out from a large wound, and the suturing is more difficult, and often a small wound is worse than a large one, because the intestines are harder to put back in place, if they are not put back in hot after hot; for the intestines swell immediately when they feel the cold, so they return to their place more easily. Therefore, it is better to leave medium wounds open, so that the intestines can be more easily returned to their place. And know that the ruptures of the belly are according to four manners: the two common sutures occur in the suture of the belly, and the suturing of other wounds of the body and two other common sutures are specific to other wounds; but they are more particular with the suturing of the belly, and I will name each one and explain.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	 I say that when the wound is small, and some part of the intestines protrudes, and it is difficult to put back, this can be done in two ways: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen due to the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	 And when it is cold, warm it in the following way: moisten a sponge or a piece of cloth in warm water only, or cook it in a decoction of wormwood, cypress, and pepper, and sprinkle the intestines until the swelling is gone; and sometimes use this vinegar compress, and it is often effective for reducing swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	 And when you see the swelling subside, moisten the intestines with water or broth of lettuce and chicory, for this eases the insertion of instruments; and if it cannot be inserted, make an incision in the wound with the instrument used to cut piles; and the first treatment is to make a small incision, one should not cut more than necessary; and this is the instrument for cutting: it has a curved shape, and see the illustration.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	 And when the wound is enlarged and the intestines come out, put them back in their natural shape and proper place, if you are able to, for it is better to put them back in than to leave them out.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	 When the wound is large and it is in the area beneath the belly, you should make the patient lie on their back and place their legs higher than their head. And if it is in the area beneath the belly, then place the head and chest higher than the lower parts. And also, if the rupture of the belly is in either one of the two sides, then make sure that the injured part is higher than the other. And you should manage what I am saying in both large and medium-sized wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	 Small wounds, prepare what you have at hand,
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	 I set the intestines back in place after they had been outside for XXIV hours, and the wound was healed by the fifteenth day, and I treated it, and it was cured.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	 And the physicians had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not cure him with a salve, for I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicine; and I placed clean old cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until it was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	 I will tell you of the two proper methods of stitching: take the needle and insert it from the outside to the inside; when it has pierced straight through, leave the tip of the suture or thread on that side, and make it come out on the other side from the inside to the outside; and the technique of this stitch is such that you sew like a pelterer does with furs, leaving a loop of the suture on one side and taking it up on the other, until the stitching is fully complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	 The second manner of suturing, which Galen speaks of specifically, is as follows: some bring the two parts together naturally and apply one chief part of the suture to the other chief part in such a way: insert a needle or chief part of the suture close by, and only pierce that spot, and leave the two sides of the wound; then turn the needle and make it pierce from the outside to the inside, to the two sides of the wound; then make both pierce from the outside to the inside, in two other holes of the suture that are on the other side; and this is the stronger manner of suturing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	 Galen says this word, and some testify to it, that one should sew the belly with two needles, each having thread; and one should insert one needle from one side, and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew leather; and know that when the rupture is inside the belly, the sewing is more difficult than at other places on the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	 The judgment of the wound is as follows, just like the judgments of other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh, with all its blood, so that the flesh has been moved by the injury, then replace the intestines and stitch the cut; then put on powder drawing charcoal, and if the flesh has been moved by the fire, then put on some remedy that is at hand, until the wound closes; and moisten the threads and bind up the sutures and the ointment; then cure the wound as with others, until it heals; and if you have no medicines, then put on, as soon as it begins to close, old cotton, and move it two times a day until it heals.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	 For you do not need any other medicine in many cases when the wounds are simple; and if you suspect that the wound may communicate with the principal members, then you should moisten light linen in oil of temperate heat, or in rose oil, and place it around the edges, and beneath the buttocks; and if he feels pain or putrefaction in the belly, and this happens often, then you should enemize him with cold red wine, and similarly if the putrefaction reaches the intestines; and pierce inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	 The intestine that is called "jeun" cannot be healed when it is wounded, and this is due to the density of the veins that are there, and the delicacy of the whole body, and its similarity in nature to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	 And if the worm exits the wound, put it back in place like the intestine while it is still fresh; and if it is old and turned black or blue, tie off the blackened area to prevent bleeding, as there are veins and arteries there; then cut out the portion that is between the ligature and let the two ends hang down from the part below the wound to facilitate extraction when the worm comes out, and to help the wound heal.
de la routure dou boueil	of the cavity of the abscess
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	 When the intestine is swollen and the wound is small, it can be restored in some people, because I have seen that a man was wounded in the abdomen by a lance; and the wound was to the right of the stomach, and became inflamed and developed into a fistula, and there was an evacuation of waste and gas; I treated it as well as I could, and did not stop working on it until it had healed and the edges were fused together.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	 And when I saw it soldered, I feared that the patient would have pain in his belly; and he had no pain, but rather improved in condition, eating and drinking; and some experienced persons said that when there is a small wound in the intestines, it should be bound in such a manner: take strips with large heads, then bring together the edges of the wound, and when the strip has opened its mouth, place it upon the two edges so that it pulls the edges together; and then cut off the head, and this holds so that it cannot come undone, then put another strip in the same manner as before, until the wound is completely covered; and stitch the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	 The head of this instrument is heated in the interior, and it brings no harm to the patient, and one can bind the interior with a thin thread cut from the intestine of an animal, in such a manner: take the head of this thread of intestine that is very de-haired, and then bind the head of this thread to a thin twisted thread of linen, then put the thread on the needle and sew the intestine, and pull it together at the opening; and this method of stitching is not outside the path of belief and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, even when it is in one of the delicate intestines, there is no help nor cure, except for delicacy.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or where it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	 Know that every wound or abscess, when it matures, is commonly called a "fistula," and likewise when it breaks open and becomes hollow.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	 And a fistula is, according to its true nature, a hard and white nodulation, which is not painful, and is also hollow like the feather of a bird; sometimes clear and hollow, and other times thick; sometimes shallow, and other times quite deep; and I have spoken in the classification of wounds, that any wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh, it is not without one of the Nine causes: namely, due to the small amount of blood or flesh; or due to its malice; or because there is hard tissue inside, and on the lips, which does not allow flesh to grow; or there is too much hollow space; or the place is rotten, and the material is of poor quality; or the medicine is not good in the cure; or due to corruption being a kind of pestilence; or because digestion is slow in that region, and healing is delayed, and it swells naturally; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and their signs, and the cures with medicines in the classification.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now it is necessary for me to let you know the cure for a fistula, which is done by handiwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	 Know that a fistula can happen in all members of the body; for there are fistulas that come from the great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or at the syphilis, or at the intestines, or at the bladder, or at some of the ribs, or at the spine of the back, or at some joint of the hands or feet; and there are some that come to affect the very nature of the principal member, and similar areas.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	 And all fistulas of this kind are difficult to heal, and there is only labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not reach the place I mentioned, but you trust in the cure, and you recognize it, then take a probe of iron or of steel, if the fistula is straight, then seek it out; and if the fistula is curved, then search for it with a delicate probe of lead, for lead bends around curves; and if the fistula has many holes and you cannot easily seek it out with probes, then irrigate it through one of the holes, for moisture quickly travels from one hole to another, and cleanses it; then seek it carefully to know if there is bone or nerve in its path, and if it is embedded deep within, and ask the patient diligently about the pain they feel when you press with your hand, and where they feel it; and when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery or vein, or any of the places I mentioned to you, then cut according to what I have told you, and remove the abscess and rotten flesh that is inside; and then cure it until it is healed, and if the fistula is deeply embedded in a straight place, then cut as deep as you can, then apply moist bandages with medicine on them, and push them up to the opening of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the remaining excess that is at the bottom; and then apply healing ointments until healthy flesh has grown; and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize as we have said, and if the bone is decayed from the fistula, then cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 If vein or nerve does not trouble you, nor the principal members, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and blackness, let the king (surgeon) cut away the corrupt matter until it is all removed, then cure the injured flesh until it is healed; and if it is not healed, and returns bent as before, know that you have not yet reached the bottom: uncover and dig until you reach the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore the place; and if it is healed in this way, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	 If not, know that the corruption is too deep, and you cannot reach it; then there is no other means but to leave it to nature; and if there is a small bone corrupt, and you can pull it out with pincers, then extract it with an appropriate instrument for this, and if there are many bones, pull them all out, not leaving even one; and if moisture makes it difficult, and there is no mistake or fear, cut through the moisture and flesh, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	 And if you cannot remove them within an hour, place something foul-smelling on the wound to promote putrefaction, and leave it until the area around the bones has putrefied, then the bones will come apart more easily; and if it is a large bone, such as a leg or thigh bone, then ease up on the corruption until all the blackness is gone, then restore the wound; and if there is a lot of damage to the corrupted area, and it reaches the marrow of the bone, then it must be covered and bandaged until the corruption is healed, and then cure it until it is healed; and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you can take example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	 A young man of around thirty years old had pain in his leg due to an internal cause, which caused materials to come to the leg, and his leg became swollen with a large abscess. And there was no apparent reason to open it; but the physicians, out of their foolishness, operated on the abscess so much that it opened, and a lot of materials came out, and it became a fistula, and a great deal of pus flowed out which all came from the body. And many physicians applied treatment to it for two years, and there was no wise man in the art of healing until I was called, and I saw his leg and the medications with which he was being treated, and the matter that was flowing out through the openings in great quantities. And the young man's skin became red, and he had a citrine color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	 I set up a tent in one of these openings, and then examined all the openings, and found that one came toward the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	 I hurried then, and cut into one of the openings until I discovered a part of the bone, and found it rotten and pierced, and the rot extended to the bone inside; I thought that what appeared to me of the rotten bone was all of it, and I believed there was no other corruption except for what I removed; and I began to treat the wound with soaking medicines for a long time, and it could not heal; and then I tried again, and discovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continuing in the bone, and I removed it, and then I tried to heal the place; but I could not do so until I cut around a palm's width of the bone, and extracted all its marrow, then I treated it with medicines; and it healed and joined quickly, and there was no need to begin the work again except for the weakness of the patient, who could not bear it, and out of fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	 For through the evacuation of blood, it often hurt, but it was completely healed, and there grew in place of the bone a hard flesh, and it had a good disposition and caused no harm or contrary effect at all, neither in going nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	 And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be treated in this way: take a bandage and strain it at the tip of the bone that is visible, and command someone to pull it up; and place another larger linen bandage over the skin that is above the bone, and stretch it so as to draw the corrupt flesh underneath, and uncover the skin above the place where you want to operate, so that the scalpel does not harm the skin; and place a firebrand or a board beneath the bone to cover the corrupt flesh; and one must operate until the corruption is visible and felt, and operate again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	 And if the bone is corrupt and not visible, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part, reveal all the flesh; then place a piece of ember underneath, and then apply silk from one side to the other side of the corruption, and let the silk be one inch away from the corruption as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, cut the corrupt joint and cover the bone or what it contains on the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, there is no other option but to cut; and if the corruption is in the wrist of the hand, or in the ankle of the foot, this is a very strong thing, but nevertheless you must examine the corruption, how it appears to you; and clean it in all ways that you can, but not against the vein or nerve; and know that there are many incisors and silks for cutting these bones, according to the position of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and delicacy, and their size; and therefore one must prepare an instrument for each type of work; and know that the task will show you the instrument you need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of diseases; so consider the instrument you need accordingly.
dou feu	of fire[ dressing or cautery tool for use with fire]
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	 The shoulders rotten either from within or from without; and when you have treated this corruption with the cure of medicines, and it does not improve, then one must cover that member until the place where the corruption reaches, so that the patient escapes from death, or from the greater harm, which is the defect of the member; and the sign is that the member becomes black, so that it seems burned by fire, and after the blackness, the corruption spreads from member to member, and takes hold throughout the body; so one hurries to cover it, and if it is due to the sting of any venomous beasts, such as sea scorpions and vipers and the like, if the corruption is in the joint of the finger, one covers it and does not give it space to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	 And if it reaches the hand, cut it at the joint, so that the corruption does not reach the arm; and if it reaches the arm, cut with a knife; and if it surpasses the knife, it is death, and no ointment is of any use except for the quantity of its virtue; and do thus whenever the corruption comes to a point: if it comes to the first joint, cut after the other joint; and if it comes to the foot, cut all of the foot; and if it climbs up the leg, cut at the joint of the knee; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other means but to let the patient die; and the manner of cutting or sewing the member is that you tie it above and below, and extend one minister one of the ties downward, and another minister the other tie upward, and you separate the flesh which is between the two ties to the width of one span, so that the bone is exposed; then cut or sew, and place a linen cloth on each side, so that the suture does not touch the healthy place, and come to the patient another lesion and abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	 And if bleeding occurs while you are working, cauterize the area quickly, or apply tightening powders; then return to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the injured limb with a suitable bandage and cure it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man once: he had a burn that looked like a fire scar, and this corrosion first appeared on his foot's toe, until it spread throughout the foot; and when the man saw the corrosion, he quickly covered his foot and was healed; and long afterwards, the corrosion returned to the finger of his hand, and he came to me, and I applied healing substances after cleansing the body, but the corrosion could not be stopped; and he wanted me to cut off his hand, but I did not, because I had hope of pushing out the material; and I also feared that if I cut off his hand, he would die, because his vitality was weak; and he gave up all hope and returned to his land, and covered his hand himself, and was healed; and I have only told this story so that one might do likewise, if necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	 Sometimes a abscess comes in the groin area, and stays for so long that it forms a large collection of pus; and then it breaks and pierces, and the pus drains out, leaving the wound open, like an empty vessel; and the skin on top is as thin as delicate fabric, and does not extend all the way to the bone or nerve. Such a condition is called «boil», and is not called «fistula»; but if it is so elongated that it reaches the bone deeply, it is then called «fistula»; and the skin is such that you can cut it all around, even when it is thin, like delicate fabric; and it does not heal easily due to its corruption.
