Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	 And if you think that the skin has become hard, and corruption is not deep, and the skin is thick with flesh, then cure it with an enema as follows: check if the breasts are large, and if the swelling that is in it has a foul smell, then enema the patient with medicinal Egyptian concoction made as follows: take alum, oil, and galls, equally, and put it in a vase over fire, until the medicine becomes red and has the consistency of honey; and then take as much of this as required, and make a mixture of it with water and honey, and give an enema to the breast, and constrict the opening; and let the medicine stay inside for 2 hours, then extract it by straining; do this many times, until the breast is cleansed, and the pus is removed; and sometimes enema with ashes' water, when this medicine is not available, and it is made by taking vine branches' ashes, and pouring water over it, then filter it, and give an enema with it, until you are sure that the breast is well cleansed; and if the patient cannot bear this, or the Egyptian medicine or ashes' water, then give an enema of water and honey with a little galls, or give an enema of honey and wine mixed together, where honey has the property of cleansing and washing, and the wine makes the skin shrink; and when you have done this, and you think that the breast is well cleansed, then give an enema of that which forms flesh in it, and it is made by taking diaphoretic emplaster, and mixing it with rose oil and wine; or give an enema of some medicines and remedies, whose properties I have mentioned in the treatment section; and if the breast's opening is small, and the size of the enema nozzle cannot enter, then widen it slightly with iron, and put a piece of Egyptian or basilicon ointment inside, until it is widened; and if the wound is too wide, then sew it up, leaving enough space for the enema nozzle to enter, and if the opening that emits pus is above, then place the piece or lower down where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	 For when the bowel is deep within, it does not allow flesh to protrude; and if you are unable to cover the wound beneath as you would like, then make sure that the bowel falls to the lowest point that is possible, for when the bowel is deep within, it does not allow flesh to protrude and if you are unable to cover the wound beneath as you would like, then make sure that the bowel easily falls downward, and let nothing of the bowel remain; and take consolidative medicines to place on the wound, and stretch a linen cloth over it that covers the entire wound; then bind strongly around the wound where the hole in the breast is larger than the first one, then spread soft ointment on another cloth according to the size of the hole, and place it on the wound to lighten the bowel, and do not remove the large cloth outside until after many days once; and the one who is over the wound, frequently remove it to remove the bowel, and know what comes out of the bowel, whether it is venom or pus or enough, or digested, or undigested; and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has spread in such a way and you see the nature arise on the wound of the breast, know that the breast is already healing and approach the bandages; and then unbind it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you unbind the wound, change another cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast (udder) discharges curdled milk after many days, know that the breast is not healthy.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	 And if subtle poisons linger for a long time, do not lose hope for their cure, as health approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	 For there are men in whom the healing of flesh in their wounds is slow, and for those who do the opposite; and if pus does not digest from the breast after many days, know that the breast is not healthy; and if the breast is slow to dry, and is distant, then apply drying medicines in substance and dry in virtue, such as diaphoretic ointment, for there is a great part of vitriol in it, and this is the last medicine. Take diaphoretic ointment, and mix it with rose oil, and moisten it with old wine equal in substance; then cook it and use it; and do the same with boiled honey thickened when diaphoretic ointment is not present, or take myrrh and aloe and incense, and grind them, and powder them on the honey when it is over the fire; and then wrap it in glue and apply a cloth, and stretch it over the breast, and sometimes administer longwort and lily roots, which are also like vetch flour and centaury; and use simple or compound remedies: grind them and make powder, and put it on the honey that I mentioned, and use it; and if the cure is prolonged and not cured by this cure, then know that corruption has gone deep, and pressure is on the bone, or in the hard members, or in the sinews; then proceed to the cure of fistula as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of an abscess on the fingernail[SR1] .
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	 Panarix is a abscess that arises under the nail of the hand, or of the foot, or perhaps in other fingers; and when it has matured, and one does not pay attention, then a bad abscess comes, and they run and spread so much that they corrupt the root of the nail, and perhaps corrupt it all; and the corruption reaches the bone, so that there is painful, smelly pain, and the finger becomes wide, and its color is black.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	 When you cure it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help at all, then you should cut away with a knife all the remaining overabundance from under the nail, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The cautery is a great help if the bone is sound and the nail healthy; and if the nail approaches the flesh, and begins to prick, and wound it, then you should place a lancet under the nail to keep it from pressing on the flesh, and lift it up, and carefully and lightly cut away that portion of flesh, and apply heated and corrosive medicaments to remove all of it; then cure the wound with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	 And if the corruption is in the bone, then cut it out and remove it, for as long as the corrupt bone remains, it cannot heal; and if you see that the finger will become gangrenous, then cut it in two at the joint as has been previously mentioned, then cure it until it is healed; and if it is wounded, swollen, and causes great pain, then you must first treat the wound; then cut the nail of the spatula shape by cutting diagonally across above, but be careful not to cut all the way to the flesh beneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if this should happen, then apply something soothing.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain in the swelling of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	 The two types of dislocations that can occur in the hands of some men by chance are entirely fleshy, and by chance there are some where there are bones, and sometimes there is a nail, and some are born at the root of the joint, or the birth is in one of the knuckles of the fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	 The one that is born in any knuckle of the finger does not move, and the one that is born at the joint of the finger, by chance moves; the size of the one that is fleshy is small, in such a way: cut it at its root with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	A child born in the root of the joint is difficult to cure: so be careful while treating it.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 In the one that is born in the back of the last knuckle, you should first cut the flesh roundly until you reach the bone, then cut the bone to a size suitable for it, and then cure it until it heals.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The swellings that come to the joints come by birth, or by wound closure, or by fire cautery, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	 It is necessary that you cut that suture, so that the parts may heal according to their natural shape; then place between two tents or wet cloths in oil, so that they do not join; or you place between two thin pieces of wood, until the place is healed, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If swelling comes to one of his two hands with the palm, cut that swelling as it is appropriate to do.
des vils	 of the common people
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	 Veins are large, swollen vessels full of melancholic superfluities, which come to many members of the body; and this happens more often in the legs of those who walk, work, and carry loads, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Then you should administer to them a purging of bile, and then apply a treatment of basilicum.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	 The treatment with iron is of two kinds: one is to cut and let out the black blood; and the other kind is that you lift the vein and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	 The incision is done in this way: first, apply very hot water to the leg until the thick blood is thinned, then squeeze the leg of the patient from above the thigh down to below the knee; then cut the vein in one place or two or three places with a wide incision, then raise and drain out the black blood with your hand from one end to the other until as much blood comes out as the strength of the patient can bear; then bind it up and tell them to eat foods that cause black bile; and begin evacuation and bleeding again when the veins are full, and this harms the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The elevation of it is done in the following way: raise the leg of the patient, if there is a lot of hair, then place them in the bath, and soak the leg in hot water until it turns red and the veins swell; and if you do not have a bath, heat it by the fire, and then make an incision along the long vein above the head of the knee, or below at the ankle; then lift the skin with a scalpel, and flay the vein from both sides, until it appears when touched; and one sees it red and black, and when it enters the skin it looks like a white cord; then insert the stylet underneath, so that it is raised above the skin, and then gently pull it, then cut in another place three fingers away; then flay the skin above the vein until it appears, then lift it with a needle as you did before, and pull it with a needle as you did first; then make another incision, or several if necessary, then lift it, and pull it to the toe of the foot, then extract and lift it up to the second incision; then extract it vein after vein, until it is all removed, then extract; and if you cannot pull it out and lift it, insert a strong doubled threaded needle, and tie and pull it, and insert it underneath; and turn your hand back and forth, so that it comes out; and make sure it does not cut, for if it cuts, it cannot be pulled out or lifted, and it will harm the patient; and when you have extracted it all, place wool soaked in wine and rose oil on the wound; and cure it until it heals.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	 And if the eye sight is constricted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you should split it crookedly, but do not cut it; and pull it as we have previously said.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	 The shape of the iron with which you cut the eye should be curved and not straight, so as not to cut the vein; and it should be thickly curved, because if it were fine, it would cut the vein. But let it be thick as we have said, and here is its shape:
de la voinne civile	 of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	 This vein runs in the legs, in warm parts where no herbs or trees grow, and in soil where there is no moisture; and it may possibly arise elsewhere than in legs, and this happens due to decay that comes from under the skin, as a snake or worm crawls between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	 And if the signs of the beginning of this ailment are that there comes a very large inflammation in the leg, then the location changes and the vein begins to protrude, just like a plant's root.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	 When the incision has been made, you should wrap a piece of linen around it that is one and a half to two ells long, tie it, and leave it hanging from the leg. And every time it protrudes too much, wrap it again around the linen and tie it; and if it is too long, cut off part of it and wrap the rest, but do not cut it at its root until it has fully emerged. For if you cut it, it will go back into the flesh and cause an abscess and putrefaction at the site, causing a serious illness. Therefore, it should be treated little by little, never leaving anything in the body; sometimes this vein, when treated, is five palms long or even ten. And a man once came to me whose was ten palms long. When you cut it, insert one wick or hole and pierce it down to the bottom so that everything comes out. Let the contents inside be drained, and apply medicinal ointments for several days to prevent putrefaction, then treat it like abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	 And sometimes at this vein (there) are many flows, and likewise when it appears in the joint of the foot or in the foot, and there comes very large wounds, and from which it bleeds greatly; then cure it as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	 worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	 This disease is called in our land "maladie de buef" (disease of the ox), because it often happens to oxen, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and it moves throughout the body up and down, and one can feel it well when it moves from member to member, so much that it tears the skin where it goes and bleeds; and it comes from the putrefaction of certain humors, like worms and snakes and lampreys and ascarides in the belly; and one doubts its malice, because when it moves through the body and rises to the head, and if it reaches the eye, perhaps it enters and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	 When you see it being cured and pulled, it cannot be otherwise than when it goes: therefore, you must then tie the place above and below with a strong ligament very tightly, then cut on it and pull it out, and if the wound reaches deep into the flesh, and you do not find it, cauterize it with fire until it dies; and the greatest harm it does is that it runs the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming near the head towards the eye, strongly constrict the brow beneath it, then cut on it and pull it out; and you must have the patient use a cleansing of the body with solvent medicines for bad humors, and beware of putrefactive foods, so that they do not cause putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	 of the pain coming from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	 This disease is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that appears in certain limbs, and then moves from limb to limb; and I saw what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	 I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and soon after, I saw it rise up to the shoulder, more quickly than any other thing, like quicksilver when it flows from place to place; the pain left that spot and settled in the shoulder, and then soon after it spread throughout her body, until it reached the other arm; then she told me that it kept returning around her body, as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed at how it moved in this way from limb to limb, for I had never seen this disease behave in such a manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	 Nonetheless, I have often seen that
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	 And when you see this disease being treated, and the patient feels the pain, if they reveal it to you as we have said, then bind it above and below quickly, and then apply pressure until the constrained flatulence comes out; and cauterize the area; and if you do not see it with your own eyes, then have it treated by someone who can release flatulence, such as with fetid pills, and polecat pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	 of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their likenesses and according to the parts of the body where they land.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	 The varieties of them (arrows) are such that there are some with large points, and small ones, and feathered, and barbed; and some that have two edges, and some that have tongues, and some that have pieces; and an arrow that falls in any member falls in two ways: either in a principal member, such as the head, heart, liver, lung, spleen, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	 When it (the arrow) falls in any place of these members, and the signs of death, which I will tell you later, appear to you: then you must be cautious in extracting this arrow, for death comes after in many dispositions; and when these bad signs do not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then draw it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	 And the sign of the brain when the arrow falls and pierces the bone, and the dura mater that is above the brain jumps, is when there is scotoma (a visual field defect), stupor, dizziness, and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps there is discharge of fluid from the nose or ears; and perhaps speech and voice are lost; and there is a flow of moisture from the wound, appearing white like lumps of flesh; and if these signs appear to you, then refrain from treating it, and pull out the arrow if it is not in.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	 The signs of an arrow wound when it hits the heart are: it is close to the left breast, and it feels as if it is stuck in a hard object, not hollow; and perhaps the arrow moves like a beating heart, with blackish blood flowing out, and coming cold sweats and chills, and fainting: know without doubt that death is imminent.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the signs of the arrow that never miss their target are that without foam it jumps out of the wound, and the throat swells up, and the patient changes color, and breathes heavily and seeks cold air.[References to the signs or symptoms of wounds in medieval medical texts often include descriptions of physical manifestations of injury, such as swelling, discoloration, or altered breathing patterns. The idea that an arrow would jump out of a wound without foam may be related to observations of how arrows can sometimes exit cleanly, or with minimal blood loss, depending on the angle and force of the impact.][References to seeking cold air in medieval medical texts may reflect beliefs about the therapeutic value of fresh or cool air for promoting healing and recovery. However, they could also simply be a reflection of the patient's natural response to difficulty breathing or discomfort.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrows fall on the coverings of the chest, it is near the small ribs; and it causes great pain and great sorrow and sighing; and all the limbs of the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrows fall on the stomach, perhaps some matter of undigested food will exit the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow falls on the belly, and some feces comes out through the intestines, there is no hope for a cure or for extracting the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow falls in the bladder, and urine comes out and exits outside, and the patient feels strong pain, know that the wound is deadly.[NOTE: I am not a doctor, but I believe this wound would be fatal because of the risk of infection from the escaped urine.]
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the arms and neck and throat and shoulders and armpits and spine of the back and ribs and hips and legs, and similar members, are safe according to various conditions.[NOTE: "Dispositions" here means "conditions". This sentence is saying that these parts of the body are generally safe from harm, unless there are certain conditions or circumstances that put them at risk.]
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When an arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, so that you can do the same.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	 It happened to a man that an arrow hit him in the corner of the eye: I extracted it, and pulled it out from the other side under the ear fat, and it healed without difficulty.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	 And I extracted an arrow that hit him in the fat of the eye under the eyelid, and it was barbed, and I could not reach the tip, and it was a large arrow from a Turkish bow, all iron without ears; the eye healed, and no harm came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	 And pull an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with barbs: I sawed off the barbs, and skillfully pulled it out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	 And I pulled an arrow from a man, who had it fall in his belly, and I thought he would die; and after thirty days had passed, his condition did not change. I cut into the arrow and extracted it, and he had no adverse reaction.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	 And if you see a man who has an arrow stuck in his back, and the wound has healed over; and the arrow remains inside him, and does not affect his natural disposition or cause harm in any of his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	 And see another man, to whom an arrow fell in his face, and the wound was healed; and he remained without suffering great pain; and many other similar ones.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	 And I pulled an arrow from a man of the prince's, which had fallen into his nose, and it was slanting towards the right side; and the arrowhead was completely buried. I was called to the cure after it had been there for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	 I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	 I searched it with a thin probe and felt nothing; and he felt pricking and pain under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	 I thought it was the arrowpoint. I applied a plaster of atratum and digestive on the place because the place did not swell; and the place of the arrow appeared.[Notes: Atratum is an antiseptic and absorbent powder, used as a styptic. It can be bought today in pharmacies, it's still produced. The term "atrative" is related to its capacity to attract humors in order to reduce swelling, inflammation or pain.]
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	 I applied the poultice for many days, and the wound healed again, and the patient remained in this state for a long time, until he felt the arrow one day inside his nose; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	 I placed corrosive medicine on the wound for many days, until it was open, and I probed it and felt the tip of the arrowhead lodged in place; then I introduced the corrosive medicine into the opening of the wound, until the head of the arrow became visible to me; and more than four months had passed when the wound began to heal, so I inserted forceps, on one side and the other, but they could not exit; therefore, I did not stop trying and devising various methods of instruments, until I took it out with well-made forceps on one day, as its shape will come at the end of this chapter, so that I pulled it out and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	 And the surgeons judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: I then restored it, and the wound was healed, and the patient was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	 I have told you the nature of the extraction of certain arrows, so that you may apply your care to what I do not say, for a book cannot grasp everything; but a wise master compares even a little thing well, and in what is present and lacking, finds new work and nine instruments for the removal of strange things that occur in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	 I say that arrows do not exit the members in which they are lodged in two ways: either by the way they enter, or from another part; and the one that exits at the same place it entered is an arrow entering fleshy parts, and exits sometimes.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	 And if it does not jump now, let it be until the flesh is rotted around it, and the abscess is eased; and similarly, if it is embedded in the bone, and it cannot come out, let it be like that for several days, and move it every day; and then it will jump, and if it does not jump, carefully cut around until the entire wound is enlarged, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	 And if the arrow is stuck in the skull bone and reaches one of the cerebral ventricles, and any of the symptoms that I have mentioned appear in the patient: then do not pull it out, but leave it alone until it is even after several days, for if the arrowhead reaches the brain, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	 And if the arrow is not stuck only in the bone, and does not reach the marrow, and the patient remains without any bad accidents for several days, then extract it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply embedded and cannot come out, administer tree resin around it, as I have told you; then cure the wound until it heals.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	 And if the arrow is lodged inside the body so that it cannot be seen, search for it throughout the wound; and if you feel it, then extract it with a suitable instrument; and if you cannot because of the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone, nerve, or vein in the way, then enlarge the wound until it is large enough; and pull out the arrow if you can, and if there are ears or anything else that keeps it from being extracted, remove the flesh stuck to it on both sides as much as you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow so that you can extract it; and take care not to break the arrow, for you will extract it more easily.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, leave it until the place is thoroughly rotted, then pull it out, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	 And if the flow of blood is unfavorable, moderate what we have said about the treatment in its chapter; and be cautious of the incision of the nerve and vein, and use trickery as you can carefully pull out the arrow without danger, soon or later, firmly or gently; and place the patient in the same condition he was in when the arrow struck him, for this is the greatest help there is, and if you cannot, then place him according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	 The arrow that comes from another direction, where something is visible of it, or the skin is swollen in that spot if it can be seen or felt evidently: then cut there, as much as the pliers can grasp, and then pull it out; if it jumps out on its own.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is lodged in the bone, then turn your hand around repeatedly until it enters into the bone and widens the bone, then extract (the arrow).
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	 And if it cannot come out, leave it still, and then resume the extraction until it comes out; and if the arrowhead is stuck in there, push the whole shaft in; and if it is broken, and you see that the patient needs a wound treatment, administer the instrument with a small head, so that the point of the arrow enters the instrument's head; and then pull it out, and if the arrowhead is stuck, push the instrument with the entering point in, to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	 And if the arrow is embedded, it is necessary to cut all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, then treat the wound as is required.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And if the arrow falls in the flesh or belly or bladder or ribs, and it is close by, and you can cover it, do so; and take care not to cover the vein and nerve, then extract it, and stitch the wound if necessary; and cure it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to treat arrows resembles a bird's beak, and see below for the shape (illustration likely not included in text):
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many kinds of them: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	 The shape of the arrowhead is similar to the feather of a bird, in order to pierce with the tip of the arrow, as shown in the following form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of pliers for driving in and pulling out (an arrow) is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the common veins of the body.
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	 Of the veins from which one bleeds are XXXI, of which there are XVI at the head, namely: II veins that are behind the ears, called "herbech"; and the II arteries that are in the temples; and II veins that are in the eyelids of the two eyes, called "aspires"; and the vein that is between the eyebrows; and the vein that is at the tip of the nose; and the II tendons that are in the neck; and the II veins that are on the upper lip, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich"; and II veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	 The veins that are commonly bled are five in number, one for each arm: the first one is the cephalic and it is located on the left side, called by laypeople "vein of the head"; the middle one is called "faste" and is made up of the cephalic and basilic veins, and is called by laypeople "vein of the heart"; and the basilic one is on the right side, and is called by laypeople "vein of the belly", and it is located above the fascia, and is the one that is clearly visible at the cubit.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	 And the salvatelle is the vein that is between the ring finger and the little finger, and it has two branches; and in the leg and foot there are three veins: one of them is located under the cubital fossa of the left side, and the second saphenous vein that is at the ankle of the right side; and the vein that is called "nesse", which is in the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg there are three veins below these.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	 The dripping of blood from veins that are behind the ears helps against old catarrh and headache; and the quality of the dripping, as I tell you, is to raise the patient's head, and rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth; then tighten the patient's neck with a cord until two veins appear behind the ears in two places hanging from the head: then search for them with your finger, and where you feel the pulse under your finger, stop there; then take the lancet, and insert it beneath the vein until it reaches the bone, then lift your hand along the entire length of the vein, and cut the skin and the vein well two fingers' width across, and let the blood flow until you see; then bind and tie it up, until it is healed; and I have already mentioned incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	 The bleeding of the two arteries that are in the two temples is worthwhile for old and solid headache, customary ophthalmia, and watery eyes in the body; and the quality of the bleeding is as I say: and that is that the patient strains their neck, so that the two veins appear openly; and feel the pulse below your finger, and then bind above with a bandage; then lift the heart up on the vein to your index finger, and insert the lancet beneath, and lift the vein up, and let it flow, as you have done with the other veins, and make the blood flow according to your need; then untie the patient, and place your hand on the vein for an hour, then place cotton on top; and then bind it firmly, and leave it until it is healed; and we have already spoken of their binding and extraction, at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	 The bleeding of the frontal vein is worth as much as the bleeding of the cephalic in diseases of the face, and for migraines, and for rheum; and its quality is such that the patient wrenches their neck while twisting, until the vein appears; then take the instrument called "fosseur", whose form is as follows:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	 And place the tip on the vein, and strike it with your hand or another object, and let the blood flow according to the quantity that you see; then loosen the patient's neck, and bind the vein until it is healed and sometimes the work is done with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Nevertheless, it is not at all appropriate for the flame to be too sharp or oblique, for the bone is near and there is a risk that the flame may break when it is fine.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	 The bleeding of the two veins that are in the inner corners of the eyes helps with the eyes, and with itching, and with rheum, and with inflammation in the eye, and with diseases of the face; and the quality of their bleeding is such that the patient wrenches their neck while twisting with some ligature, as before; then bleed, and let the bleeding be a little long and wide with the flame, because there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is fine, it may break; then apply coagulated blood as needed, and then bind it with cotton, and bind it securely.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	 The sap of the vein in the nose is worthwhile for headache, and for sudden madness, and for diseases of the face, such as migraine and redness that comes to the face, and similarly when it is old; and the qualities of the sap are such that the patient constricts his neck, then constricts his nose with your left hand, and takes a slender flame, and sticks it between the upper lip in the space that is between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open widely, and the blood will begin to flow; and do not go too deep, and make the blood flow according to your need, then bind it up for one night, for it is quickly restored; and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	 The liquid from two leeches helps with the narrowing of the groin, and the beginning of emaciation, and with many diseases, and imposthume, and corrosion, and herpes, and abscesses; and the quality of the liquid is such that the patient constricts his neck below one and the other, as we have said; and let the master be standing over the patient's head, and the patient sit on a seat, then carefully open the vein lengthwise a little, then draw moderate blood, or as much as necessary; then do the same thing in the other vein, then untie the ligature, and moderately constrict both veins, so that the patient does not strangle; and leave it until morning, so that the wound heals.
de la sainie des leivres	 of the flow of blood/wound drainage from the lungs
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	Bloodletting from the veins in the lips above assists with cholera in the mouth, and decay of gums, cracks in the lips, and nasal congestion and swelling.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	 And the qualities of the wound drainage are as follows: make the patient sit in front of you and constrict his neck as I have said; then turn the lip and look at the two veins, one of which is on the right lip and the other on the left, and they are recognized by being black, and by having small black veins around them: then stop both of them, and if you do not recognize them and are in doubt, then stop the largest one from each side, and similarly do the same for the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	 of the wound drainage beneath the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	 The draining of veins that are under the tongue helps after the draining of the cephalic vein, and this is at the narrowing of the throat, and for eye ailments, and for mouth diseases; and the quality of draining is such that the patient lies between your hands in front of the sun, and raises the tongue, and looks down on either side, one black vein: then drain both, and do not go too deep, for arteries are beneath.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	 The veins of the arm that are commonly drained are drained in two ways: either by pricking with a large, moderate flame or with an olive-thin lancet as cutting tools are called, and it is called "anesil"; and they are wide and thin according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the mercurial flame is very famous, and is as wide as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	 And it is necessary, for opening veins full of clotted blood visible and containing thick and turbid blood, to use the form of an olive-colored flame;
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more finely pointed, and is used for healing delicate veins that contain delicate yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	 The bleeding of the basilica vein, which is one of these veins, helps to heal diseases that are located beneath the throat, neck, chest, and abdomen; and it is necessary for the surgeon to bleed carefully and be cautious of the artery that is underneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	 And if the artery is cut and a flow of blood ensues, it must be stopped as I have said; and the flame should not be piercing but cutting like a needle.[EOF]
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	 And if the vein does not open manifestly, you should constrict it, and apply another one; or seek a remedy for it, or heal the vein in place of it along the arm: it opens manifestly; and cover it with a damp cloth, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	 And if you want to recognize the location of bleeding, you should do the following: constrict the arm and feel for the place until you sense the pulse; then mark the spot with a sign, and bind the arm, and cover the vein with a damp cloth; and be careful not to strike an artery when you see the swelling, for it is an artery - avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if you see it protrude upwards like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is from an artery: hasten then, and place your hand on it for a long time, then remove your hand if the bleeding stops, which often happens; if the arm is swollen, leave it so and do not move it, and let the patient also not move it while healing; and be without fear, and do not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not stopped and it overpowers you, and the medicine is not present, then cut the artery if it is visible, for its source will retreat, and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	 Take a piece of fennel root, split it and take one half of it and bind it tightly until the next day; if the bleeding stops, it is good; if not, treat it as we have said, with powders that stop bleeding; and stopping the bleeding is not difficult in many conditions due to the small size of the wound and the strength of the arm's binding.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	 The wound in the middle helps so that it draws blood from the head above, and from the body below, because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic vein, as we have said; and it is necessary for the surgeon to be careful about the nerve that is beneath, and if it pricks too deep, and he finds the nerve, and it swells and the wound becomes infected, and perhaps cannot heal; and this nerve often appears, and if it does not appear in some men due to its delicacy, then you must cure it with a silver instrument; and move the nerve aside as much as you can.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, then make an incision through its length.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	 The incision of the cephalic vein helps so that it draws blood from the head and benefits the eyes; and one must cure by pricking with the olive-colored flame or the myrtle-colored flame, because it is the safest of all veins, for there is no nerve or artery beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	 Nevertheless, one should try to find the easiest approach, and not worry if there is a mistake the first time, and one can start over; and perhaps the area swells for some men when they make a mistake the first time, but it's no matter.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the sanies (pus or other fluid draining from a wound) is according to your judgment.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	 The first thing you need to know about bloodletting is that bloodletting is not performed unless it is to maintain health and to avoid future illnesses; and the bloodletting should be done in one of the three veins which are: namely, cephalic, saphenous, and basilic; and one should perform bloodletting at the beginning of prayers, and in autumn and winter after eating, when signs of fullness appear; and one should perform bloodletting on the first or third day, after two or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	 The medicine that is administered for illnesses has no set time, but rather when needed during the day or night, at all hours and in every moment; and one should not bleed children until they are 14 years old, nor pregnant women until the third month up to the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	And one should not bleed elderly people who have passed 60 years of age.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	 And when anyone wishes to be bled, in whatever manner, they must first cleanse their intestines with a gentle enema if they have retained a great deal of feces, so that the veins do not draw out impurities from the intestines harming the principal members; and one should not bleed someone who is overly full of food, or intoxicated, until they are no longer, nor those who are dropsical; and if one wishes to be bled after a colic attack, vomiting, diarrhea, frequent menstruation in women, work, watching, fasting, and any other thing that weakens the strength, whether from injury of arms or body; then refine the humors, if the blood is thick, with foods and drinks and medicines if you have them; then enter the bath, if nothing prohibits it, to further refine the blood, and bleed from the vein in the arm near the elbow as we have said; and on that day avoid work, exertion, lust, and similar things; and be joyful and happy, and let the one doing the bleeding raise their sleeve higher than the arm of the person being bled, and rub the arm two or three times, then loosen the ligature in the middle, for when it is too tight or narrow, the blood cannot flow; and then rub the area with your hands until the veins swell and can be felt; then moisten the bandage with a little oil, then place your left hand on the vein below the area to be bled, so that the vein does not move and is not missed when striking.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	 For there are veins that run like strings in the leg, and some of them are full of airiness, such that when one applies fire, they contract and cannot be opened, and it is thus for these; and if one opens the vein, the wound is too narrow, therefore the surgeon must be cautious in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, it is good; if not, try again a little below or above that location quickly, if the place is not swollen.[STHAPHANUS: That's all for now, I'll continue later. Thank you!}
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	 And if the limb is swollen and the patient is frightened, let him rest for one or two days and do not bind his arm: perhaps abscesses will form; do not enter into a bath, then resume bleeding if it pleases him; and if the opening is small and you fear that too little blood will flow, then apply the flame directly to that same opening; and perform the procedure hurriedly so that the limb remains swollen; for this occurs frequently when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.
