If you see the place swollen, do not restart the bleeding, but put a little bit of vinegar of oil (oil mixed with vinegar) on it, for it clears the body of blood, and the vinegar is beneficial in this regard; and so administer the vinegar of oil in every bleeding that you bleed the veins, to stop the flow of blood; and do the same with a compress and bandage, when placed on the swollen area; the blood will become thin and spread out if it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	 And if a large abscess occurs, which often happens, even when it is only bled once, at the time when the opening of the vein is small, then hurry and put a sponge soaked in warm water and salt on it, and hold it there for an hour; and you should do this after the issuing of blood from the vein, and if some darkness or greenness remains at the place after several days, it does not harm; and if you wish, put something of aloes or myrrh dissolved in chamomile juice on it.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there is an abscess and discharge at the basis of the shinbone: place then your hand on it, and if you find a soft spot upon compression of the hand, it is a bad sign.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, beware that you do not apply any of the things we have mentioned, for perhaps it will cut through the artery; but make a dry poultice in order to harden the spot, then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw blood from each (patient) according to the quantity of their strength, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if you see it is thick, let it continue to flow until it thins; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	 And it is necessary for one who is stout and robust, and in need of bloodletting, to make a larger incision, and let the wound be wide; and for the weak, do the contrary, and it is better to bleed them little and often, and this type of bleeding is to be done crosswise, not by stabbing; and this method of bleeding is safe from loss of blood and nerve damage, and is worth more than long or wide bleeding.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	 And for one whose body needs bleeding, give them moist bread in pomegranate juice; if they are overheated, let blood three or four times; and if they have a cold complexion, feed them before the bleeding moist bread in muscatel syrup, or aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and zedoary, and fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	 And if he has a fever after the evacuation of much blood, then he should eat meat broth, and scentful subtle syrup, and use other things that we have mentioned in the division or chapter on fainting, for the evacuation of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to bleed from the arm and purge himself again, it is necessary, when he becomes weak due to excessive bleeding, that he bleeds drop by drop, according to the amount of his remaining strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wants to bleed from the arm after the first bleeding, and he has a strong body, let him bleed seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.[SThana Vannan, Medieval Translator](mailto:St.thanavan@gmail.com)
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wants to bleed from another location, should do so on the second day or the third.[SThana Vannan, Medieval Translator](mailto:St.thanavan@gmail.com)
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	 For there is much blood inside the body which is already heated and causes fever; thus, you must draw out a large amount and widen the opening until it ceases to bleed; then make sure all conditions of bleeding are met, and place your hand on the pulse when bleeding, so that death does not occur in its place, which happens many times due to negligent phlebotomists. And when you unbind the arm and cause the blood to flow again, and if the opening is closed, do not press strongly or quickly extend the arm, for this would be harmful; instead, let it bleed until the second evacuation; or apply the tip of a flame cauterization until the congealed blood at the vein's opening emerges, then place a piece of cloth soaked in water and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it alone without constricting it until the abscess subsides.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw blood again, let it heal in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is bled instead of the vein in the head because it is composed (i.e., larger or more accessible).
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	 And the manner of bleeding is as follows: the patient puts his hand in warm water until the vein becomes red; then it should be bound moderately tight, so that the vein is visible; then bleed him across (the width of) the vein, not too much or too little; and make the incision large, and let it bleed close to the joint of the hand, and if no blood comes out, put the hand back in warm water and let the blood run into the water until you have enough; and if this is done in the summer, do not put the hand back in warm water, for it is more necessary to do so in winter than in summer; and bleeding from this vein is safer than all other veins, as there are no artery or nerve there.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	 The salve of the right hand's wrist is worthwhile for all liver ailments, and this is how: straighten the hand and immerse it in hot water until the vein fills up, if one sees it; and if the wound is crooked or if you cut it all around, it does not matter; and do not go too deep, for the nerves are bare of flesh beneath; and then put the hand back in hot water if the blood is frozen in the wound and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn enough blood as is necessary, then place oil and wax on the vein to quickly seal it, do the same for each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The letting of blood from the left hand is beneficial to the disease of the spleen, and do similarly as I have told you for the right (hand).
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	 The salve of the shin is worthwhile for all ailments that are below the body, such as diseases of the legs, retention of fluids, disease of the kidneys, thighs and old legs, and similar ailments.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	 And the qualities of his discharge are such that the patient puts his foot in hot water and rubs it on the vein until it disappears, and binds above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and from there over the foot go many vaines; then bleed where the vein is largest, or at the ankle, whichever is easier.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you bleed on the foot, beware of the nerves that are underneath, and also bleed across (?), as when cutting; and let the flame be gentle.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, put the foot in water and let the vein empty completely.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	 And if the bleeding fails the first time, try again a little above, for the place is salty; and do not worry about nerves, as we have said, and similarly do the same with the shin of the other leg.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The location of the sciatic vein is at the ankle of the leg, and its bloodletting is worth as much for the pain of inflammation, when it is hot blood.[Note: I translated "hainche" (inflammation) as such because, given the context of a medical treatise, it seems to be the most appropriate word. However, depending on the actual text and its author, it might have other meanings.]
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	 And the qualities of his discharge are such that the patient enters into a bath and squeezes above the ankle four times by twisting; for otherwise the vein will not open; and if it opens, bleed in all ways that you can, crossing (the wound); and it is better to make many incisions, for the place is dry, and the vein is deeply embedded in most men.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	 And if you don't find it (the dislocation), seek a vein of it that is visible on the back of the leg, and toward the small toe, and beware of nerves; and make the blood flow until you see, and then loosen the ligament, and place cotton on it and bind it; it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	 cup suction wounds
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Leech jars are made of horns, or brass, or glass; and cupping is done in two ways: either by striking and drawing blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	 And this cupping which is done without striking is of two kinds: either it is done with heat or without heat; and the cupping that is done by striking and bloodletting is done in fourteen parts of the body, of which one is at the very top of the head; and another is at the neck; and two are on both sides of the collarbone; and a cupping glass under the chin; and cupping glasses on both shoulders; and cupping glasses on the hips; and cupping glasses between both arms; and cupping glasses on both legs; and cupping glasses on both ankles; and the cupping does not draw large amounts of blood, only small veins that are scattered throughout the flesh, and therefore it does not weaken a person as much as venesection (bloodletting); and it should not be administered, either with or without heat, in any disease caused by repletion (an excess of bodily humors) until the whole body is evacuated.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	 And if by necessity, due to illness, it is necessary to perform bloodletting, or for customary purposes, we administer it every hour at the beginning or end of the month, and in between and at every time; for there are some who, when they need to be bloodlet, have a heavy head; and there are some who find congestion and redness in their face, and in their head, and neck, and darkness in their eyes; and there are such ones who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen tongue, and secrete blood; and there are some who dream, and see in their mind blood and wounds and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and likewise when it is within three hours of the day, we order them to be bled after.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	 The letting of blood from the nose helps with a crack in the skull that comes to the eyes, and it should not be done after the evacuation of blood from the whole body; and this bloodletting is a substitute for the letting of blood from the head, and it is not suitable for those of a cold constitution to use, or who have catarrh, because it does them great harm; and for this reason, the elderly should not use it, nor those who have cold diseases in their head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who are often healed by it (cupping) frequently become forgetful, and therefore the cup should be placed a little lower out of doubt for forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	 The ventilation to the neck is located near the bloodletting of the head and the basilic vein, and this is why it is useful for constriction of the nipple, and fissure of the channel of the foreskin, and for all [other purposes of] tightening; and one should not push it too hard, because if it stays in place too firmly, it can cause oblivion or stomach and heart ailments.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	 Ventilation between the two ribs of the neck is useful for headaches, eye diseases and migraines, and strangulation, and pain in the roots of the teeth, and it is located near the basilic vein's bloodletting; and you should instruct the physician to apply pressure gently when placing, so as not to cut the artery and cause a bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	Wind accumulation under the chin equates to diseases of the mouth and gum decay, as well as similar conditions in the mouth; it is located near the veins of the two lips.[Source](https://books.google.com/books?id=y0QZAAAAYAAJ&pg=PA62#v=onepage&q&f=false)
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Wind accumulation in the shoulders equates to a disease caused by heat and overfilling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	 Wind escape from the sides is equivalent to that of three veins in the arm, for it draws blood from these large veins; and it advises the surgeon not to strike too deep, for the place is bare of flesh, and there are nerves and arteries beneath.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping glass that is on the rump is as valuable for hemorrhoids of the rectum and other illnesses in the area below, and it must be large and made of iron, because it needs to pull strongly; and by chance, if it were too fine, it might break, and cause great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	Leg cupping is done openly, for it draws blood from the whole body, and is beneficial for old pains in the shins, legs, bladder, and loosens blockages. It is applied to the area around the two shin bones and the ankles. However, even though it strengthens the body after prolonged use, it can also cause fainting in certain situations.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of applying the cup is as follows: place it on the skin when it is empty and warm it up slightly, then apply it quickly and move it around evenly, without stopping until you see the area becoming red and swollen, and notice the appearance of blood. Then, puncture it once with a lancet, remove the cup, and pay attention to the condition of the body, as some have tender flesh and visible pores: in such cases, puncture only once, making the wound large and deep, and suction gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to puncture twice: the first time to thin out the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to puncture a third time; and when we want to draw out only a little bit of blood, once is sufficient.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	 And if we want much blood, let us repeat frequently; and if the blood is thick, strike deep; and the limit is that the heart should be pierced suddenly; and it is necessary for those who have thick and hard skin, and who have narrow pores, that you anoint the places of the cups with oil that opens and dissolves: if it is in summer, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or oil of cucurbit seed; and if it is in winter, with oil of cresson, or lily, or chamomile, or similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluidities are large and cold, take oil of marjoram, or of costmary, or oil of dill, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	 And if one treats someone with tender flesh and large pores, no oil should be put there, but it should be washed after ventosation with rose water, or cold water, or maidenhair fern water, or cucurbit water, or porcelain water, or any similar thing.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And the one who has too much moisture should rise from easel, or water of myrtle, and sumac, and similar things.[Translation Note: "Aisil" is not a common term in Old French and its meaning is unclear without additional context. However, based on the surrounding text about washing with different types of liquids, I have translated it as "easel," assuming that it may refer to some type of liquid or herbal mixture used for bathing or soaking.]
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	 And those who have excessive moisture rise from old wine, or water from a dry place, or decoction of dill or chamomile, or other similar things; and one should not be bled with cupping glasses before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath one hour or two; and one should not sleep after being cupped, and it is necessary that they are washed when they are about to be cupped and when they have been cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	 And beware if the one who is healing is choleric, and if the blood is too thick and inflamed; so they must take cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuces at ease, and similar things; and eat little, and meat of goat, and moist foods.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	 And he who has a cold complexion should take syrup of honey, and middle-aged scented wine, which is between old and new, and eat little, and eat pigeons and small birds and squabs; and on the day that they will be bled, they should drink more than they eat; and it is appropriate to give some people triacle or muscatel before or after the bleeding, to comfort the main members; and let the blood be thinned, but it is not appropriate for those who are hot to drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	 Cups that are placed without striking are those that are placed on the liver, and on the spleen, and gout, and on the stomach and groin and legs, for these members do not tolerate being struck, and one does not place them there except to draw blood from member to member, as we place them on the breasts when the milk is flowing; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we place cups on the stomach and on the groin to reduce swelling; and to alleviate pain when there is an obstruction or stone, as it possibly draws out the obstruction with its attractive virtue, or dislodges the stone from its place; and it does this when placed on the liver and spleen when there is trapped wind, and these cups are administered empty to only suction; and sometimes they are administered assembled with fire, and sometimes full of warm water, as in diseases of pleurisy, and in such a way that one fills the cup with hot water, or with water in which healing herbs have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the cup used with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	 And it should be two fingers in width and half a palm in depth, and have on the side near the middle a small hole, as big as to put a needle through, and be made of brass, smooth before so that it does not prick the patient when placed on the member; and have in the middle a cross bar of brass or iron, to hold a candle in place, and let there be both large and small [blisters/suction cups], according to the illnesses and age of those who use them; for the blisters/suction cups of children are different than those of the elderly, and of the thin than those of the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	 And one should place this blister/suction cup on the member in this way: dip the wick of wax or linen in it, and put it across the bar which is inside the blister/suction cup, so that the flame is at the bottom of the blister/suction cup, but not burning the patient; then place it on the member, with your fingers over the hole that we mentioned, so that when you want, the vapor comes out and remove the blister/suction cup; then reapply the linen as before, and repeat often if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	 In the cupping glass then, which is administered in cases of pleurisy, it has no tube or opening, and is not administered except when it is full of water, and is placed only on the body part; and this is the method:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	 Sweat vessels are not administered except in body parts where cupping glasses cannot be placed due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar places; and on bare areas of flesh, such as the inside of fingers or nostrils, and other similar places. And the quality of the sweating is such that when you find sweat vessels that are in clear, sweet water without putrefaction, then take them; and place one of them in clean, fresh water until they become familiar (acclimated), and have nothing left in their bellies; and then let them be bled from a vein and cupping glass, then rub the body part until it becomes red, and place the sweat vessels (leeches) on it; and when they are full and fall off, if it is a place where a cupping glass can be applied, then apply one, for this is very beneficial.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	 If not, lift the armpit and then the shoulder, very gently, and then wrap it; and if the wound takes too long to heal on the body of the swellings, wet a linen cloth in cold water and place it on until the swelling subsides; and if the swelling is multiplied, put crushed vitriol, or alum, and similar things on it until it subsides; or you put half of peeled beans on the affected area and leave them until they dry on the affected area, and this will stop the bleeding immediately; and if you need more, take other swellings.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	 And if the swellings do not want to form, rub the area with fresh blood, or insert a needle until blood comes out, and then put it on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will dry; and when you see that they are full, sprinkle some crushed aloe and salt, or ash, on them, and they will drain immediately.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it concerns the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	 Know, dear son, that foolish doctors throw themselves away from this chapter, as they never saw any of the ancient books, nor did they read letters; and for this reason, knowledge is estranged in our land, for I never found any good one; and I know nothing, except through the science of ancient books, where I have studied so much that I have extracted knowledge from it, and by experience, and by the custom of my life; and I have described to you in this chapter what it contains, and summarized it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are prepared, as I did in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Then it is necessary that we say in the prologue of this book the summaries of the words and the chapters where the wise man directs his attention, and remains on the truth, so that those who are proven may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	 I say that when fracture or dislocation or torsion or contusion happens to anyone, you should hurry to heal the patient from one side and another, if no obstacle prevents it, such as weakness of the body, children, old people; or if the weather is not extremely hot or too cold; and eat only lean meats, that is, cold game, and bird and hare meat, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not fill yourself with food that fills the veins with blood, until you are certain that there will be no hot abscess or spreading of matter to the limb; so that the patient returns to their usual regimen.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary to nourish the patient with foods that make for thick nutrition, or have a viscous quality, such as wheat cooked in water, and rice, and heads, and feet, and tripe of cattle, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For at times, during the setting, movement and healing are sped up and the fracture occurs more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	 And know that broken bones of the old and frail cannot heal or join together well according to their nature due to the weakness of their limbs, nor can those who are too young, such as the bones of small children; but it doesn't matter, reset the broken bone and use large, sturdy bandages that tighten and bring the limb back together, until it heals as it was before; and don't move it at all, and for this reason, they must be fed nourishing foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse and varied in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the break of the head is different than that of the hip or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all the types of fractures.[Read More](https://medium.com/@healinglanguagehq/old-french-medical-text-translation-5-e81b65904a7)
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a break that tends to go towards the groin, and another one sharpening, like the split of a pen's nib for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a break with a wound, and a break that is a small fissure.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	 And each condition has its own tool and proper instrument in healing, according to what is needed in its place; and a fracture of the bone is known by the limb being twisted, and it is clear to touch and sounds when pressed with the hand; and when there is no twisting or sound upon touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no fracture; but there may be twisting, or a crack, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	It is not at all appropriate to move it with your hand, but instead apply the following mentioned medicines and then bind it gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	 And know that fractures that are in a tree, and are the two parts disjointed, they must now be aligned equally, so that abscesses do not come there; and if abscesses do come there, let it stay for some days, until the abscess is calmed down; then align it evenly as you can easily and skillfully, and know that the restoration of this one is easier than the restoration of the one where pieces are missing; then bind it, as will be necessary next.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	 And if in the bone there are broken pieces, if it is in the leg or foot, or in your hand if it is one of the small members, or with two strings, or with one string and your hand; and place the member according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken member are separated, you align all the additions in their places as well as you can, and make sure that through your work the patient does not suffer injury or pain; and fit the two edges of the bone together according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it with your hand to make sure that it seems not quite right; then align it nicely and do not stretch it too much or press on it as those do who cause a hot abscess and constriction in the member through their work, as we have often seen.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	 And when the limb is healed, chastise the patient well so that they do not move it, whether awake or asleep, during turns, or in any other way; and make sure that the limb is secured in such a way that they feel no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	 For when they feel any pain, it is not yet healed, and it must be put in such a position that they feel no pain; and make sure that it is set straight, so that there are no deformities when it is restored; and the qualities of the broken limb are as I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken members (bones) vary in smallness and largeness and in shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	 For there are small limbs, such as arms and fingers and similar ones: these should be wrapped in soft and fine linen cloths; and those that are large, such as hips and legs: these should be wrapped in a wide and hard bandage, for the wide bandages embrace the entire large limb and constrain it equally on all sides, so that there is no bruising; then wrap light stuffing around it three or four times according to the limb, and tighten your hand slightly on the entire bandage, then go above the break and tighten less, so that the break moves away slightly; and loosen the bandage little by little, until you have captured a large part of the healthy limb, then take another bandage and wrap around again above the broken limb; then return to the part below the break, and tighten moderately, neither too tightly nor too loosely, as we have said in the first place above; then place linen or cloth stuffing between the bandages, so that it is all even, then bind it on top with a bandage, and then place your well-made splints on it, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	 And if there is swelling or abscess, place something warm and soothing for the abscess on it, and that reduces swelling, and leave it on for several days; then apply pressure with your fingers, with bandages half as wide as a reed, or made of wood used for roofing shingles, or from palm leaves, and arrange them like this:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	 but it is necessary that the splint put on the fracture be slightly larger and wider than the others; and also be as long as required for the size or length of the limb; then apply pressure with your fingers like you did at the first location, then bind it with a suitable thread like in the first location on the fracture; tighter is better, less so; and the thread should be of medium thickness, not too thick or thin, and made of soft linen; for if the threads are thick, as I have seen done by foolish people who bind their fractures with twisted rope, it is a great error, because the binding cannot be equal if it is too fine, and it should not have less than two finger-widths of space between each splint.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is wounded by the shards of arrows after being tightened in a healthy place, place under them plugs of linen, or wool padding, so that they do not wound themselves.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is accompanied by a break and the flesh is torn, I will tell you the cure after this.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not appropriate to bind all broken limbs with arrows on the first day.[_](id:r86v2o3aokvp)
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	 For when the limb is large, splints should not be applied unless after 5 or 7 days, or more depending on your certainty of a developing abscess; and here is the method of ancient emplasters for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists: it consists of taking flour that clings to the walls of the mill, and mixing it abundantly with egg, and applying this concoction, not too clear nor too thick, and use it; and this is the common method of the restorative emplaster for many fracture situations, and likewise for women and small children, because it is not too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another manner of plaster restores the fracture and dislocation and twisted limb: take three ounces each of alabaster, ladanum, enula campana, asafetida, and gum arabic, and myrrh and aloes, five ounces each; aloe juice, eight ounces; and reduce to a powder, and mix with egg white; if the complexion of the person is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and quickly restores broken bones, and is beneficial for many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	 Another emplaster method for twisting: take marsh mallow and great burnet, in equal parts 10 units; myrrh and aloe, in equal parts 9 units; gum arabic 6 units, and grind well, and mix with water or abundant egg, and apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	 Another way of plaster for joints and separated bones in their place, and to calm the resulting pain, and for the surgeon to use on the bone, and the fracture: take new wool, and soak it in vinegar and cooked oil, and put it on the place.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	 This plaster does not restore, but it is good for soothing hot abscesses, and properly removing pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another plaster that restores broken bones: take dried fig leaves and crushed clover, grind together, and make a plaster. (Note: spelling, measurements, and some plant names have been modernized)
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	 Another way of plaster for the restoration of bone fractures and to lessen the remaining abscess.[1](https://www.definitions.net/definition/remainder)
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	 Take root of mallow, chamomile, flowers of violets, flour of peas, of each one part; and grind, and mix with wine, and if the limbs are heated, mix it with moist coriander water, or with water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	 Another manner of emplaster, stronger than the first, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	 Take root of mallow, and seeds of linseed, valerian, melilot, and elderflower, and flowers of violets and chamomile, all in equal parts; and grind, and infuse with salt water, or fresh water, or with wine, according to the heat of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates states in his book that one should not place any plaster on a broken limb to restore it but only a cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says that it should be moderately warm and not too hard or too soft.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen also recommends that one should apply to a broken limb, for the purpose of restoring it, mildly warm dry substances such as myrrh, aloe and incense, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another manner of plaster that is useful for wound and pain: take a beetle and chopped off human hair or bird feathers, and red lead, and boil evenly, and grind, and make it into a plaster and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And then loosen it a little afterwards, and take care if the patient feels no pain, nor have the bones moved from their place; if not, do not loosen it for many days. And if pain comes to the area, or itching, without rest or swelling, then hurry and loosen it, and remove the plaster immediately; and take a light cloth and sea sponge, and dip in water, and raise the area, until the itching ceases and the pain is calmed; then let the member rest for an hour, then put dry wool, dampened in water or rose oil, and bind it on a bandage, as long as you are sure of the heated abscess; and relieve the inflammation of the member, and remove the pain, then carefully redress it and apply a little plaster, and do not tighten it as before; and carefully until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that an abscess is red, swollen, painful and has drained completely, and you need a poultice and bandage, then reapply it as you did the first time.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	 And if no improvement comes to the member from what we have said, do not unlock it until after three days, or four or five or seven; and sometimes leave it for twenty days, according to what one sees, so that the breaker becomes cautious and approaches the adjustment of the flesh upon it; then hold it back more than before, and the flesh swells, as I said before; and if you see the joint drying out more than necessary, know that no numbness can come there; therefore, anoint it with warm water each time you unlock it, and this should be every third day, and loosen the ligature a little; by this work, numbness is cut off from the member, and heals quickly what foolish doctors do, who restore the member incorrectly: that is bad, and such work is to be feared, and I see no other option but to leave it alone and work on it correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	on various types of fractures.
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	 Many kinds of fractures exist, with various shapes, and different causes; for there are fractures that are made by the striking of a sword, and the neck takes out all the bone down to the syphax which is beneath the bone, as done by a hatchet or stick; and this kind of fracture is called "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Where the sword cuts the bone without piercing it, and this type of fracture is called "absolute"; and the wound of these two fractures is large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a hidden impact, or a crack from a stone, or from falling on a stone, or from similar causes.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a penetrating fracture that approaches the membrane beneath the bone or is on top of it, and this wound is either large or small.[Note: "toile" in Old French can mean "membrane", "fabric", or "canopy". In this context, it likely refers to the membrane (periosteum) that covers the surface of bones. The translator had to make a judgement call on this one.]
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	 And if there is a wound that is sunken into the bone as thin as a hair, and the fracture is small, it is therefore called "capillary" fracture; and if the wound is made by striking with a stone, or by falling, or by some similar thing, and drives a piece of the bone inward, and the location is hairline, as blacksmiths make when they strike anvils; then it enters among the stones inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	 And this happens more to those who have moist bones in their head, such as children's heads; and it happens in all these types of fractures where small pieces are separated, like so; and I will speak about it later.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we recognize all kinds of fractures by the swelling on them, and through inquiry by touch, and by the corrupt flesh that is on top.[NOTE: I translated "char" as flesh since it can refer to any tissue in medical texts from this time period.]
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of the fracture is recognized by this: when one has uncovered the bone and rubbed over it, the fracture appears black.[NOTES: I translated "li brisure" as "the fracture," assuming that "brisure" is being used as a noun here. Also, I translated "capillaire" as "appearance" since this word can mean several things including hair-like or relating to the head.]
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, beware of any adverse symptoms in the patient, such as vomiting bile, loss of consciousness, convulsions, pallor, fever, and redness and protrusion of the eyes, among other things in various conditions; for without doubt, it cannot heal if these are present.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a frightening accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the cure.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wounded person comes to you first, and it is winter, you should remove the bone before the fourteenth day at the latest that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in the summer, you should quickly remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the cloth underneath the bone does not become rotten, and the accidents that we have mentioned come.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	 And if the fracture of the bone comes as far as the skin covering the brain, then you should split open the injured part like this: take hold of the patient's wounded head and expose the bone in every way that you can, and gently along the wound's shape; and if bleeding occurs when exposing the bone, or an abscess arises, provide what is necessary for it; and it is done by filling the space with cloths soaked in rose oil; let the wound rest until the abscess subsides and you are certain that there is no more bleeding; then begin to remove the bone, which can be done in two ways: one way is to make a narrow incision in front, and this is the method:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make another incision, larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is to have several different cuts, some narrow and others wide, and they should be pointed and made of iron; and work lightly, so as not to wound the flesh.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and tough, then you must drill around it so that you provide cuts with terraces (ledges), not going through the bone but stopping at the outer layer of the bone, leaving a margin or circle on the tip that does not allow the tip to go beyond the bone; and you will need several of these, so that each one comes into place according to the thickness of the bone, so that you have terraces for all parts of the bone; and this is the method of the three types of terracing:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for drilling around the broken bone are: place a awl on the bone, and turn to your hands until you know that the bone is pierced; then move the awl a little further, and do so all around, then cut the space of the bone that is between the holes, and do this as delicately as you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you draw the bone to your hand, or to any of the tools that you have such as tongs, pliers; and make sure that you do not touch the brain or the sutures.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	 And when you have pierced and treated the bone, you must remove the splinters that remain from the bone on all other similar instruments like a lancet, but it should be more slender and finer than the other lancets; and if any small bones or fragments remain, gently remove them with the instruments; then cure the wound with bandages and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of work is as described by Galen, which is safer, and he highly recommends it; here is what he says:
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary, firstly, that you uncover a part of the bone, where the break is clearly visible. Once you have uncovered this area, place beneath the tip of this lunate knife, of which the shape is as follows:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	 And do not cut from one side, but rather leave it attached on two edges so that the cut is toward the bone; then strike lightly with a small mallet so that you chop the entire bone all around, taking great care not to damage the cloth beneath; if it is torn at the bone, remove it gently, for it can be removed without harm or fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the break in the bone does not penetrate through to the periosteum (the membrane covering the bone), but rather is only cut from above with fragments remaining, then you must smooth over this roughness and remove the small flakes using a sharp razor, which you should have in various sizes, so that you can choose the most suitable one for each situation depending on the work and shape of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If the king before large razors, and afterward with more fine ones, and do not stop until it is fully done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each other case of hair trimming and fine bone breaking, it is necessary to arrange the direction accordingly; and this is not an easy task even for those who have devoted their studies to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	 And if the abscess is uncovered, take a linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, and soak it in rose oil, and place it on the wound; then take another double cloth, and soak it in wine and rose oil, and place it on top of the first cloth; and do this as lightly as you can, so as not to harm the abscess, then apply another bandage, but do not strain it too tight, just enough to hold the wound; and leave it like that for a day or two, until the abscess has calmed down; then unbind it, and apply medicine such as lily roots, vetch flour, incense powder, aristologue, and similar things; make a powder from these things and place it on the wound, and apply medicine that is not harsh; and make sure the wound stays clean, do not let any pus accumulate, for when pus collects under the cloth on the brain, it will rot and cause great harm to the patient; for when something harsh is placed on the abscess, it will burn from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take heed then, if any adverse event befalls the patient, as we have said, there is reason for doubt and fear.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if no improvement comes from the medicine that has been applied, unless it has such power, then you should take a part of honey and three parts of rose oil and glue a compress, and place it on the styptic; then cure it in various ways until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the nose above are broken, or one of them, because there are two bones; and the one below is cartilaginous, and does not break but only becomes swollen or twisted, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	 And if one of the two parts is broken, then you should insert your little finger or the tip of a probe into the break and push it back into its natural shape with your index finger on one side and your thumb on the other, taking care to cause no pain to the patient as you do this.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the nose, and your finger cannot reach it, you should use a small piece of wood to push it back into place.[*]
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	 And if the break is in two pieces, then do the same thing; and make haste to set it on the first day if you are able; if not, then after the seventh or tenth day, when the swelling has gone down, insert a linen compress into the wound if the break is in one piece.[
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or place one [bandage] on the other side if the fracture is there; and let the bandages be thick enough to fill the openings of the nose.[source_author](Guido of Arezzo)
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	 And some surgeons say that you should moisten the bandages with butter and change them every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	 It does not seem right to me, but it is necessary that they are moistened with a mixture of egg yolk and powdered gypsum; then leave the bandage on until the bone is healed and the cartilages harden.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes goose feathers are placed in the nose instead of bandages, with a soft cloth around it, and this holds the fracture together, and the patient blows through it; do what you will.[source\_author](Guido of Arezzo)
