Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if pustulent abscesses come to the nose while you are working, put either cerote or cotton soaked in rose oil, or in a piece of lily root.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if abscesses do not form, apply an emplaster over it, made of lily flour and incense powder, mixed with egg yolk; then place light cotton swabs on top, but do not bind them. If the fracture in the nasal bone is small and splintered into many pieces, extract them using appropriate instruments, then stitch the wound and cure any injuries to the flesh and cartilage, as well as with suitable emplasters and ointments. And if there is no wound inside the nasal bone, treat it with bandages and place wooden splints on it until it heals.[This translation is not perfect, but I did my best to provide a clear understanding of the text's meaning in English]
de la routure de la mandibule	about the fracture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the lower jaw is dislocated, and there is no wound above it, and the fracture is not present but only a protrusion inside, it can be easily recognized.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the fracture is on the right side, you should put your index finger in the patient's mouth; and if the fracture is on the left side of the jaw, insert your index finger of the right hand, and gently push the fracture back into place, and align it with the other hand from the outside.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the jaw fracture is separated into two parts, you must apply extension to both parts until they are aligned.[df-note] Note: I translated "desevree" as "separated" and "extension" as "applied force to stretch or extend a part of the body."
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if there is movement of the teeth or a fracture, then bind them with a golden or silver or silk thread, and apply a cerate on the broken jaw, and place a double bandage over it. Place a large well-made star-shaped object or a piece of leather of equal size, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it up high on the head as tightly as possible, and instruct the patient to rest and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see the figure changing, unbind it on the third day, and then realign what has become misaligned; and apply a plaster on top, with powder from the mill and plenty of egg or chickpea flour, after removing the wax; and place light linen on top of the plaster, and if the plasters dry out, and the patient's condition does not change, leave it on until it is healed; it is often healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses come, treat them as we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound at the same time, see if any piece of bone has been removed from it; then carefully remove it with suitable instruments.[Read More](https://raghavkansha.github.io/)
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with fire as necessary.[Read More](https://raghavkansha.github.io/)[ ](https://raghavkansha.github.io/)
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and none remain, then stitch the wound, if it is large, and apply one of appropriate plasters to it, to help heal the flesh, until it has healed.
de la forcele	The word "de la forcele" does not appear in the provided text. If you could provide more context or the full sentence, I would be happy to help translate it.
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The collarbone breaks in several places before the shoulder, and there are three types of fractures: one where it is broken and dislocated in two pieces, which is easier to reset; and another with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the operation is as follows when the fracture is without a wound: that you have two assistants, one holding the injured collarbone and the other extending the neck towards the side; then place the break between your hands so that it is in its proper shape and there is no appearance or deformity.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend it more, place a round sphere of cloth or wool under the patient's shoulder and make it thick as needed; then extend and lift the collarbone and hold the sphere with your hand, so that you can place the break in its proper position.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the humerus outward because it is deep within, an oversized pillow should be placed under the patient's shoulder blade, and the assistant should push the shoulder downwards until the bone of the humerus is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then realign the fracture with your hands, and if you find it shattered, you should cut open the wound further; gently pull out the fragments and, if the bones cannot join due to any obstruction, saw one of the ends of the bone that is causing the obstruction. But make sure to place the instrument called a "syfac" under the humerus to protect it.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	 and seems like a spoon, and is not curved, and should be as wide as it should be, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and have two edges, as you see, and one should be wide, and the other narrow, similar to the opening of the wound that you made when treating the bones; and when you are certain of a hot abscess, burn the wound, and if the opening is small, or if you doubt a hot abscess, bandage the wound with strips and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if abscesses appear, wet a dressing in rose oil, vinegar, and assyl (a type of resin), and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	 The straightening of the bone, when it is without wounds and without cutting, is done by placing poultice made from molin powder and egg white on the bone, and then putting light cotton on top. Place a sponge underneath if necessary; then take a large bandage one palm wide, put a double cloth on top of the cotton and poultice. Then take a thin stick three fingers wide and long, wrap it around the bandage so that the end hangs loose; place the stick over the fracture, turn the bandage around the neck and under the healthy shoulder, and under the fractured shoulder; adjust the fracture from each side, and when you see that the ligament is holding the fracture properly and the stick does not move on the bone, rewrap it every day and tighten it when the binding loosens. Have the patient lie on their back and place a small pillow under the healthy shoulder to raise the affected shoulder; this will align the force of the shoulder with the fracture, or bind the arm to the neck and do not unbind unless there is an accident, for up to 20 days. Reapply the poultice if necessary and leave it on until healed, which should take no more than 28 days, and less for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of a shoulder fracture
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	 Not often does the shoulder break or dislocate in such a way that it is noticeable from the outside, only perceptible through touch; prepare it according to the shape of the fracture, and reset it following its natural form, in every way possible; then place powder of flour with plenty of egg, and light bandages, and place a double cloth above; then place a wide and thin board, slightly larger than the shoulder, and if there are any hairs underneath the board in any part of the shoulder, fill those hairs with linen bandages, so that the board lies evenly; and then bind it firmly with a large bandage, making sure the board does not move from its place, and check the binding each day; and every time it loosens, rebind it, and realign the board if it has moved, and have the patient lie on their side; and the shoulder will be restored in 20 or 25 days. And when this number is accomplished, unbind it, and be careful, for it is not an easy matter if the bone comes out of place.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a part of the bone juts out in front, but not underneath the skin, then make an incision, and cut it as we have said in the break of the forearm to soothe a hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	In the break of the hip.
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	 The bone is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; however, it often breaks at the ends.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	 And when it is broken in the middle, it tilts downwards, and the patient feels great pain, and there is a risk of infection, and they may vomit blood, and the fracture is visible in the broken bone, which can be felt.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	The restoration process is as follows: the patient lies down on their back, and a cushion is placed between their shoulders. Then, the shoulders are pressed together, and the ribcage is pulled inward with both hands, gently and carefully equalizing the alignment of the broken bone as much as possible, until the shape of the bone is correct. After that, ointments and compresses are applied on top of a thin layer of salt or other light wood, then wrapped in a bandage and tied over the broken bone so that it does not move. The bandage is wrapped around the back and tightened appropriately, and re-tightened every hour if it loosens. If it becomes necessary to loosen the bandages due to corrosion, itching, pain, or abscess, then do so immediately, remove the ointment, treat the affected area, reapply the ointment, and rewrap the bandage tightly until healed.[
de la brisure des costes	of the breaking of ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breaking of ribs does not come about except in heavy blows to the back, and at the chest within, and they do not bend except because they are slippery; and one can feel it well upon examination of the sides.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	 And the restoration is to align the break evenly, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	 Then apply the poultice and bind it with a splint if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the break of the rib is angled inward, then the patient feels great pain and a stitching sensation, just like with pleurisy, because the bone pierces the flesh; and the lung has prickly points, and soon vomits up large quantities of blood, and this is a serious condition, and the ancients have applied much skill to it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And there are some who say that one must administer foods which cause the belly to swell, in order to push the break outward.[Note: This suggests that the recommended diet is intended to increase gastric distension and thereby help realign the broken ribs.]
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make it so that abscesses come to a boil, if they have not already come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have come to a boil, then lance them.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some of you have said that cupping glasses should be placed over the place to draw out strongly, and this seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that the cups may attract impurities to the weakened area.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some of you have said that the place should be covered with a cloth soaked in warm oil and then bandages should be placed between the ribs to evenly distribute pressure around it, and then treated with the treatment for pleurisy, food and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot bear due to the broken bone pressing against the cloth, and there is doubt, then a cut must be made above the broken rib, and an instrument placed underneath to protect the lung; and then the bone must be cut and carefully removed, and the edges of the wound sewn up if it is large, and treated with poultices until healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if boils are about to come, put wet cloths steeped in rose oil on it, and place it on the affected area; and care for the boil as necessary, lying on one's side next to where it is, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the breaking/fracture of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes there occurs a breaking/fracture of the bones of the neck, and it rarely happens that it bends; and also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	 And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if it will heal or not, observe if you see their hands becoming softened, swollen, and lifeless, and they cannot move or stretch them, and when you poke them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	 Know that it is mortally afflicted in many ways, and if they move and feel when they are pressed and poked, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient can be cured if treated.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	 And if a similar thing comes to the spine of the back, and you wish to know if it will be healed or not, look to see if the feet are weak, and if there are symptoms in the hands, and on the back an overabundance of wind and unwanted discharge; and when it has been warmed on its belly, unwanted discharge occurs.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	 And when it has been warmed on its back and it wishes to relieve itself, it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	 Know that it is mortal: it does not labor at all in its care.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if these symptoms do not occur, then the condition is less severe.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you should treat it if there is a hot abscess, put rosin oil or egg yolk oil on it until it calms down; then apply one of the strengthening and drying plasters, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and let them not sleep on the part where they feel pain, until it is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone becomes dislocated, it is necessary to cover the wound; remove the bone and align the two edges of the wound, sew it up with a stitch if it is large; then apply a wound healing ointment until it heals; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called "the cow's head", insert your left hand pocket, and place it evenly with your other hand to your ability; then apply the plaster and bandage if needed; then bind it, and if there is a dislocated bone, adjust it and remove it, and treat the wound until it heals.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the shin bone.
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It rarely happens that the shin bone is broken, and if it does happen, it is usually only a slight reduction in size at the end; it becomes long, deviates to the side, and causes pain to the patient at the site, as well as bruising and swelling where it is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is as follows: you extend your hand upon it, until you are above the break; and know what the break and its shape is; and if the break is at the top only, then align that break equally, so that it is in its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is long or it slants inward, then have the patient lie on their stomach, until the restoration of that break is clear to you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have aligned it equally, then apply the poultice and place a stick or bone splint on top of it, holding the break in place so that it does not move; and fill the space beneath with a pad, until the area is even
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the patient to sleep on their healthy side or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if abscesses come there, do not touch them until the abscesses have calmed down, and use what we mentioned before; then return to the restoration, holding it in place as is necessary, unless there is an adverse event; this is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder.
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder joint is the part between the neck and the top of the shoulder, and if it is dislocated, it should be restored in one of two ways: the first way is to take a stick of medium size, shaped as follows:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two arms with two bandages and pull them upwards, and seat the patient on a chair; then lay his dislocated arm over the stick so that it rests in the middle of the stick, forming an arch; then hang a heavy weight or have the assistant stretch it downward; then place the healer's hands around the fracture, bringing the ends of the fracture together until the broken bone returns to its proper position.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other way is to lay the patient on his back with his dislocated arm raised upwards and tie his hand to his neck; then command two assistants, one takes hold of what is above the fracture with both hands, and the other holds it below with a bandage, extending each one in their direction.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	 And if you wish the extraction to be stronger, tighten the ligament below the fracture and above the fracture, and extend each of the assistants to their side.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	 And if the break is near the shoulder joint, you should place a middle splint beneath the joint, and another one toward the groove, under the break; and also if the break is toward the groove, you should gently place a splint there, without strain, so that the break is even on the surface, and on the groove; then align the fracture as it should be, and bind it, if no abscess comes.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if abscesses appear, do not bind it until 7 days have passed, and put a damp linen cloth on it, soaked in oil of roses, until the abscess has calmed down; then bind it, and the method for binding is to put the poultice on the armpit, then place the arm on the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or chest; and put the cloth, and bind on the armpit, and on the arm, so that the arm stays in place, if nothing prevents it, or if the bones are not broken.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you are unsure whether the bone is broken, use splints, and place a wider and stronger splint on the break than the others, and have one finger space between each splint, and let each splint be so big that it extends beyond the break by three fingers on each side; then bind on the splints, as I said at the beginning of this chapter, more tightly and less loosely, on the break.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	 And if you see the positioning and binding, as we have said, at the time you restore the broken member, and you are uncertain whether a hot abscess will develop, then leave it to be bound until the seventh day, as we have said; then examine the bandage every three days, to see if there is itching, swelling, or discharge in the area, or if circulation cannot reach the member because the binding is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	 If the procedure, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	 And if no such accidents occur, do not unbind it until after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on their back with their hands on their stomach; place a cushion filled evenly with wool underneath the shoulder, and check every hour during the day or night to ensure that the position of the broken limb does not change or that the bindings have not loosened; then perform the procedure with the power of medicine, and give them the food as we have previously mentioned, making it light at first; and when they begin to recover, make it richer.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	 And it is customary for the shoulder and leg to be bound for forty days in total; and then they should be unbound and a bath and ointment medicine should be administered to help heal the injury.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	 And if the ligature is tight and embedded, it should remain to be untied for 3 days or 2 months.
de la brisure du bras	of the break of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is made up of 2 bones, which are called the "humerus", one of which is small, and it is this one that follows the armpit; and the other is large, and it is the one that is below, towards the little finger; perhaps the large humerus breaks alone, or the small one, and perhaps both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	 When the small bones are broken, restoration is easy, and healing occurs quickly; but when large bones are broken, healing is difficult and more severe than when both are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	 If only the small ribs are broken, then they should be slightly extended and aligned properly.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	 And if it is the large ribs that are broken, then they must be strained more forcefully and stretched out on a cushion, with the pouchet (a medical term) of the hand raised higher than the others, and the little fingers lower than the other fingers. The patient should be lying crosswise on themselves, with the cushion elevated higher than the patient can tolerate. Then the minister should extend the patient's arm below at the side of their hand or to the suture, and another minister at the top.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	 And then the doctor places it evenly, in the best shape.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	If the break is in pieces, then each piece should be put in its place. And if there is any fragment that pierces the heart and cannot be restored to its place, then a hole must be made through the ribs and the fragment removed, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, which I have spoken of in a previous chapter, then attend to the treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	 And if during the beginning of the treatment a boil arises, apply a plaster of rose oil and white wax, neither too hard nor too soft; and gently bind the plaster over it until the boil subsides.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	 And then remove the plaster and apply the poultice made of flour milled with plenty of egg; place the splints, and let the splint of the fracture be stronger and slightly larger than the others; and know that it should have six splints or branches in multiple arrangements: whether the fracture is in one of the bones or two; and bind more above the fracture than elsewhere, and always less as you move away, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the bandages over the fracture be soft and moist, and not hard or rough; and let the thread used for binding be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	 And wrap the limb and the ligature after several days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	 And if any harm comes to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, then you should apply warm water to the limb until the itching subsides; and do not let the limb rest too tightly.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	 Then resume tightening, and if the ligaments have softened and the bones have separated, address that.[Reformulated for better clarity: And then, if you notice that the ligatures have weakened or the bones have become disjointed, take appropriate action.]
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you notice that the swelling cannot reach the member because it is too tightly bound, then loosen it slightly and leave it like that for several days until the swelling returns, and then rebind it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	 And if none of the things we've mentioned happen to the patient, do not release them for 20 days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	 or after that time, bind their hands to their neck, and make sure their collars are even, be vigilant of movement and sweating, and sleep on their backs; and know that this break will be healed in 30 days or 35, perhaps even in 20, depending on the constitution and complexion of one's virtues.
de la brisure de la main	Here is the translation of the given Old French sentence into modern English:
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that breaks in the back of the hand and at the knuckles of the fingers are rare, and only swelling comes there often.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or sprained, then the patient should sit cross-legged and face straight ahead evenly; then place his hand on a spread-out cloth, and have the assistant extend the broken bones, and align them properly so that they are well joined; and apply a dressing and bandages, unless pus forms, then place a splint according to the size of the area; and wrap it in a linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the breaker is around the belly of the sole, make a sphere of cloth, and instruct the patient to press it against their broken sole; and then bind it with a long strip of cloth, and let the stick be as wide as the palm of the hand, and bind it as it should be.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is above, then you must place a stick on top of it, and another below in the sole, so that the hand is open and straight, then bind it all around the hand, and make the binding tight between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture comes to any of our fingers, if it is the thumb, then set it straight as it should be; and bind it with the sole, and if you see fit, place a small straight stick on top to raise the fracture and keep it from moving; and if the fracture is in one of the other fingers, such as the index or another, then set it straight and bind it with the good finger that follows it; or bind them all together, which is easier, or place a stick on top, like with the thumb; and take care in the restoration and arrangement of hot abscesses, and help those who come to it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	Here is the translation of the text you provided: "of the broken thigh" or "of the thigh that has been fractured."
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The thigh bone is often broken, and this is easily seen when it turns forward and backward; and the restoration is such that one bandage is placed above the break, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then each minister extends their bandage to their equal part; and this is when the break is between the bones.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	 And if the fracture is near the root of the thigh, let one of the ligaments be towards the wrist, and the other ligament below the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	 And similarly if it is near the knee, then let the ligament be near the knee, and let there be extension downwards; then place the surgeon's hands equally on both sides of the bone and adjust it to its natural shape, then apply the poultice and bind it, if no abscess forms.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, let it subside and then return to your work and treatment; the binding is done in such a way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	 You should wrap around the fracture 1 bandage doubled in 2 or 3 layers, and let the excess remain; then bend the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the thigh, and place a long thread between the thigh and the leg, near the knee below, and bring the ends of the thread to the top; then wrap around the leg and thigh the bandage, then place a splint on the fracture, and a splint on the bone of the leg; then fill the space between the leg and the thigh with soft cloths to apply equal tension, then begin to tie tightly 3 or 4 turns on the fracture; and when it goes above the fracture, tighten less; then pay attention to the two ends of the thread that you placed between the leg and the thigh, and tie three splints that are above, then go down to the bottom of the thread, so that you come near the foot; and tighten it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it like this, as long as no abscess, swelling or other similar thing comes.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, loosen it, and realign what is out of place, as we have said many times; and if there are fragments of bone that prick, they must be gouged out if possible; and if not, the place must be split open and drawn forth; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the hip is broken so that splints are placed in it, as in the shoulder and arm; nevertheless, in this type of restoration, the patient does not fare well.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the hip is restored in 3 days, or less or more, depending on the differences in constitutions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the groin of the knee

de la brisure de la jambe	about the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. And if the two bones break together, the leg becomes deformed in all directions.

And when you have completed your work, take two rods of stripped wood that extend along the leg on both sides and are as long as the leg from the knee downwards; then wrap it in two layers, one above and one below, and bind it in the middle so that the leg cannot bend to the right or left, and this is good. And some administer a splint as long as the leg, made of wood, and place the leg on it to prevent movement, and this is done properly in fractures where there is a wound; and move the leg every day to see if there is any inflammation or other accident; and care for it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the fracture of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no fracture, but sometimes there is a fracture in the bones of the foot and the toes, and it only results in a crush injury in multiple ways.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a fracture in the bones of the foot and you see the bones sticking out over each other, place the patient's foot on the ground as if they were going to walk, then place your foot on top of theirs where the bones are protruding, press it firmly until they return to their place, then apply a plaster and bandages, and place a small board with two flat pieces under the affected foot, then bind it to the foot with bandages and any other necessary materials.

And if some of the toes are fractured, then set them as we have said for the fingers of the hand; then place a splint on the broken toe according to the length of the toe, and make it slightly wider, then place under the foot the board that I mentioned earlier, and bind it appropriately; and if there are two or three, or more, fractured toes, then place a splint on each one according to its size, wrapped in a linen cloth, and bind the board under the foot; and let it be placed on top of the chief (top surface) of the board outside the belly of the foot, so that it touches it well.
