And it is necessary that you do not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, just as we have mentioned; and treat each incident as it should be.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	Here is a line-by-line translation of the provided Old French text:
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When the bone of a woman's nature (vagina) is broken, have her sit with her legs spread apart, then lean her back and support her from behind. Fill the vagina with cotton, making it as thick as a finger, then stand the woman up and lift her pelvis, allowing the cotton to come out of the vaginal opening until the bone returns to its place with the finger. When she needs to urinate, remove the cotton and replace it once she is done for seven days or so. This will help heal the fracture. If desired, take a bladder from an animal, attach a cane to the opening, insert the entire bladder into the vagina, and blow strongly into the cane until the bladder expands inside. This will pull the broken bones back together, then fill the area with cotton and leave it for several days until it heals.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	 And when the bone of the wrist in a man or woman is broken, it should be reset in the same way as we have said for the shin bone; and such fractures are not hidden from one who applies close attention and skill, and pays heed to my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	 For the fracture indicates in several ways the correct path of restoration: pay attention then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the penis, when it is broken, take a goose gullet and insert the penis in it; then wrap bandages around it, and leave it for three days or until it heals quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a fracture with wound, even if it is large, such as the bone of the thigh or shoulder or similar, that it be healed now, just as the drainages that we have mentioned testify to.[note]Here, "sainies" refers to the drainage or discharge from the wound, indicating its healing progress. The translator has chosen to use the word "testify" to convey the idea that these drainages provide evidence of the healing process. However, this is a somewhat loose interpretation and other possible translations include "show", "indicate", or simply "are".[/note]
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, then cauterize it with vitriol if you have nothing else, then begin to heal the fracture in that same hour or on that day, unless abscesses come there.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if abscesses arise there, then leave the healing until the ninth day, until the abscess is calmed down, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, because you would cause a harmful incident to occur.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone appears under the skin, it is necessary to put it back in place gently with your hands, with slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not suitable for you to put it equal with your hands, then use this instrument which is of iron, with 7 or 8 holes that are long, and the width is according to the size of the wound; and it is necessary for the surgeon to prepare 3 or 4 (finger) rings, depending on what is needed in each bone-breaking cure; and let them be round and a little thick, so that they do not bend during compression on the member while you are working, and let it be sharp at the front, and thick from the middle to the end, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	 And it is called "palainche," which means that the curved head should be placed on the visible end of the bone; and push it once until it aligns, so that they are even with each other.[6](https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Disjonction_ouverte)
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	 And if the fracture is subtle and the instrument cannot grasp the bone well, then you must cut the end of the bone so that the instrument has enough power.[6](https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Disjonction_ouverte)
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot set the bone as we have described, then cut it with an appropriate instrument, such as a knife or scalpel, to your best ability; then smooth down any roughness and small shards left in the bone.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	 And when the bone is set back in place, and the patient feels great pain afterward, know that it is not in its natural position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	 Make sure it is back in its proper position, then wet a cloth in black styptic wine, if possible in the summertime; and do not apply any salve or other oily substance to the wound, as it may cause putrefaction and corruption; then administer a cautery after setting the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, cutting away the coverings according to the size of the wound; and take great care that the wound is not constricted by the broken bones; for many foolish surgeons have caused harm to the patient by either killing them or causing their wounds to fester; and let the constriction be lighter and softer than other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	 And if the wound is large or severe, and you fear that harm may come (to it), as we have said, and you find pain in the place, then you should not put caustics on it; but instead, wrap hard bandages around it, in place of caustics, and bind it.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	 And when you see after 1 or 2 days that pus is developing in the wound, remove what you have placed on it, and apply a wound-healing ointment, such as tetrapharmacon ointment and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary to loosen the limb twice a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it has healed and become clean.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be arranged in such a way that pus drains away easily.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if for many days they are beyond repair, and it can no longer join but keeps bowing back, know that there are small fragments of bone, therefore you need to stitch the wound with sutures, and remove all the separated pieces causing the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	 And if a fistula comes to the place, or any other form of corruption, then you should treat it according to what is described in the previous chapter.[In this context, "fistula" likely refers to an abnormal tube-like passage from a hollow organ to the body surface, often caused by infection or inflammation. The author suggests that such a condition should be treated as described earlier in the text.]
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	 And when the bone is broken and visible on the limb, such as the bone of the thigh or the shoulder, do not pull it out, for many times this leads to death; but leave it until it rots. Perhaps it will come out by itself after twenty or thirty days, then cure the wound if you can; and if you cannot, then leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	bruises that come upon sutures
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often come across this after the healing of a fracture, even when it is close to the joint, and it is an unpleasant sight to see the appearance of the member; and perhaps the limb cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take great care then if it is fresh to us: and administer styptic medicines to him, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocollex, acacia, and similar others, so that you take some of these things, or all together, and cook them with astringent wine or with egg yolk or with vinegar; and put it on the wound in wicks, and bind it well, and do not loosen it for several days; and then loosen, and begin another, until the knots are removed; or you strain on a piece of wood well made; for the property of wood is that it removes all swelling above the members; and if the nodulation has already turned into hardness just like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, then cut it off and let the excess appear; or you have it scraped by a skilled barber, until it is removed, and cure it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the weak member after healing.
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is healed, but the member remains weak and fragile afterwards, it happens for many reasons: one of which is that it was bound too tightly and not bound as it should have been; or because there were too many bandages and the nourishment could not reach the member; or due to an excess of moisture; or due to excessive movement, not at the appropriate time; or because there is little blood in its body, so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and make the body supple, so that the blood is multiplied in him; and administer baths for him, and give him joy and pleasure; then put poultices on the member, so that the poultice attracts great nourishment to it, and often moisten it with warm water, until the nourishment reaches the member; and it returns to its natural form.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	of the twisted limb after health
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the bone is broken open, and the shape of the limb is unsightly, it does not lose its natural function; do not believe the foolish ones who say that the limb should be broken again; many foolish surgeons have done this in our land; and these works are blamed, and cause great harm, and perhaps even death; nevertheless, if the knots and tension are fresh, they should be soaked in hot water, or softening herbs should be cooked, such as vismalve leaves and roots, melilot, and similar things; and make a softening poultice, such as a well-made diaclytic, and take the mucilage of vismalve and thicken it with chicken fat or oil of Saint John's wort, and make a poultice; or take greasy figs, and crush them with dung from a horse, and similar medicines that reduce swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	 And sometimes nodes are removed through continuous and lengthy rubbing with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	 And bring about gentle movement to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisting is old and hardened, like stone, and it is necessary to remove it with a iron, then it should be covered down to the bone with a sharp incision made with a delicate lancet; and cotton and a bandage should be used in the care.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When a dislocation occurs to someone, it must be corrected immediately.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	 For if one waits, the place swells, and perhaps it cannot be reset; therefore, it should not be moved when it is swollen: many times it causes spasms and other pains; nonetheless, when this happens, make the patient vomit, then leave him, until the abscess has subsided; then apply warm water and oil to the limb, then gently reset it, and treat each limb as it comes into place.[Answer in English]
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have arranged the chapters on dislocations of the limbs from head to feet.
des mandibules	of the jaw(s)
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It rarely happens that the jaws are dislocated on both sides, and there are two ways in which dislocation of both occurs: either they are slightly out of place and somewhat loose; or they are completely dislocated and hang toward the back, and saliva flows from the mouth that he cannot hold in, nor can he close his mouth, and his tongue becomes entangled as he speaks.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns to its place through several positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	 And if it is whole and complete, you must quickly reset it and not delay; and in such a way that the assistant holds the head of the patient, and places his small pillow (or mirepoix) of one of his hands into the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is two-sided; and let the other hand be free to align (it); and command the patient to relax, his jaws, and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the physician adjusts it evenly until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if the returning is difficult, even if it's both jaws together, soak them with warm water and oil, until you can easily adjust them; do not delay in readjusting, as we have said.[Notes:
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	 And when they are evenly reset, and the mouth of the patient closes well without difficulty, then place wet bandages (or cloths) dipped in a cerate made of rose oil and wax on it, then bind it lightly with soft ligaments; and let the patient sleep on his back, and his head should be placed between two cushions so that he does not move it to the right or left, nor make any effort to chew, but eat light food until the pains are gone, and the jaws are healed; and then eat what you want lightly, and do not struggle to open your mouth to eat and drink, until the jaw is well healed and cured.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jawbones cannot be restored to their place in an hour and are not returned to their proper position, then fevers and habitual swelling may follow, and possibly abdominal distension, and perhaps vomiting of bile.[ ](https://fr.wiktionary.org/wiki/pur)
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, know that it is a lost cause; and many times, those to whom it happens die within nine days.
de la forcelle	of the fork/fracture/dislocation
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The dislocation cannot be removed from the side towards the back and the hip, and it is dislocated at times to the outside, which can be felt.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	 And the restoration is as follows: let the patient lie flat on their back, and stretch out their arms; and then press firmly with your palm on the joint, and it will return; then apply the poultice and bandage, and bind it; and the hip that is dislocated towards the leg cannot come out; if not, and if it dislocates at any time, reset it to its place, as we have said; then apply the poultice and bandage, and bind it, and instruct the patient to rest until they are healed; and similarly, the hip joint is put back in place when it is dislocated from its position.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	 Know that the shoulder does not dislocate in any other way than in three manners: of which one is when it dislocates at the part of the shoulder blade beneath; and the second is at the part of the hip; and perhaps it dislocates at the upper part, but this happens rarely; and it never dislocates backwards at the shoulder blade, nor does it dislocate inwards towards the nerves; and often it dislocates downwards towards the shoulder blade, especially in those who have little flesh, for it slips easily in them; in those who have enough flesh, it dislocates with difficulty, and returns to its place with difficulty.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And it may happen to some men that they receive a blow or fracture, causing the shoulder to swell from a hot abscess, and they mistakenly believe that it is dislocated because of this.[5][1](Ch. 23)
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore, you should examine it until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.[5][1](Ch. 23)
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	 And it is known that the dislocation is when it moves down toward the shoulder blade, and creates a distinction between the sick and the healthy shoulder, and you will find a clear difference between them; and you will find at the top of the shoulder a pit, and below the shoulder blade where you touch the top of the shoulder, as if it were an egg; and the patient cannot bring his hand to his neck, nor move at all; and likewise, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you will find it manifestly when you touch it; and this type of dislocation is not difficult to set back in place, when it is new, or if the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the manner is that the servant raises the patient's hand up high, then puts your fingers underneath the joint, and forcefully lifts the joint up to its place; and the servant lifts the hand, stretches it up, then puts it down; and it will come quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	 And if it does not come back as we have said in many days, then the patient should be bathed in hot water; and given soothing and relaxing remedies, such as a decoction of althea, fenugreek, and melilot in water, and let them drink it; then the patient should be propped up on their back, and place a soft woolen support below the shoulder blade, neither too soft nor too hard, then have the attendant put their heel on the support and lift the top of the shoulder forcefully, and pull the arm of the sick person; and another attendant hold the head of the patient so that it does not move downwards; this shoulder will come back immediately, and if you see it coming back in this manner: and it is that you make sure a person who is larger than the patient is present; and stand next to their side, and put their shoulder under the patient's shoulder blade, and lift the shoulder blade upwards, so that the patient hangs in the air; and another attendant pulls the arm of the patient down towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	 And if the patient is too lightweight, have them hold something heavy, and the dislocation will return now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	 And the dislocation can also be reset in another way: by inserting a long stake into the ground, so that the patient's head rests on it like a pillow, and it should not be too thick or too thin. The patient should then lie down with soft blankets underneath, with their body aligned along the length of the stake. Then extend their arm away from the body and straight out, and the joint will quickly return to its place. If it still does not want to return despite all these things that we have mentioned, then perform this treatment: take a stake that is two arms' lengths long and four fingers wide, with a pointed end that can be inserted deep beneath the shoulder blade, according to this shape: [The text includes an image/diagram of the stake positioning]
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	place a soft cloth over the patient's head, so that the stick does not hurt or wound them, then place it beneath the dislocation of the patient; stretch the arm along the length of the stick, and tie the shoulder to the stick, and the arm to the head of the hand, then place the arm on a step of a ladder of appropriate width, and let the hand hang down, leaving the body suspended on the other side: now the joint will return to its place.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is back in place, no matter how, you should put a pad of wool of equal size under the dislocation, then apply a poultice made with powdered flour, incense and egg white all over the shoulder and around it, then tie it in place beneath the dislocation, and turn the bandage over the poultice, and hold the hand to the neck, leaving the hand remaining in this position.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that they eat only soft food until the limb is healed, as this will promote faster healing; and then eat normally after 5 or 7 days, and move the limb; and if it feels firm and not swollen, then it has healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	 And if the joint is out of place due to moisture that has come there, or for another reason, you should apply cautery to it at three points, as is set out in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all of this and it becomes dislocated again after seven days, and the joint cannot hold and the arm cannot be raised, then know that the nerves at the head of the shoulder have been cut or stretched or weakened; and know that the joint will never return to its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	A dislocation that is towards the side of the buttocks or the back is made by a thrust and extension of the hands, and another joint is used as a substitute; and care should be taken until it has healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing comes cracking in the limb and slow movement, then the patient should use baths many times until that cracking is eased and returns to its original state.[Machine translation](Note: The following translations were generated by machine translation services and may contain errors. de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the rib(s)
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the rib is dislocated at the tips, and it returns to the tips; and it is dislocated all around, both in front and back, and the dislocation has not been reset, for it is clearly visible and can be felt; and it is dislocated according to each shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	 And when you join the cut patient with the flesh, you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	 Because the joint is dislocated and cannot bend the arm or touch the shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it must be reset in such a way that abscesses do not come there, for if abscesses come there, it would be difficult to reset; and perhaps it cannot be completely reset, especially when it is at the back; and this type of dislocation is worse than others, and causes greater pain, and may even result in death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration, when it is of such a kind that it can be reset, is as follows: you extend the patient's hand with your two hands; and his arms should be spread out, and the surgeon's hands should be placed around the rib, both above and below, and push the joint back to its place, either at its tips or at the root of the palm, until it returns to its original position.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it comes back when he doubles his hand to his hand, and strikes with the root of the palm the dislocated bone.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	 Because it does not want to return to its place, apply strong traction; have two people extend the arm and hold it with two people so that it does not move during the extension; then bend the arm in each direction after you have wrapped a long and wide bandage around it; and when the physician has put the joint in its place by hand, anoint it with some oil to soften the joint, then press firmly on the joint until it returns; and once it is in place, apply dry poultice with egg white, and bind it tightly, and hold the arm up against the patient's neck, and leave it for several days, then loosen it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, release the bandage and leave it alone; and if you see that the joint does not align properly, repeat the ointment and bandage, and leave it in this way for several days until it is firmly set; then release it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	 And if he feels great pain after the resetting of the joint, and it moves, bathe and gently rub him, and press until he is eased; or put warm sheep's fat on the joint, then leave it for one day and one night, then remove it, and make him enter the bath; and when he sweats, gently rub the joint, then replace the fat, and then enter the bath; and do this two or three times, until he is healed; and if you wish, put moist cow dung, heated with butter, and bind it on; it will return to its normal state.
li dislocation de la main	hand dislocation
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand is dislocated, and the return is easy, more so than for other joints; nevertheless, it must be quickly returned to its place at once when it becomes dislocated, so that the place is swollen or there arises a hot abscess.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	 And the resetting is as follows: place the sick hand on a table, extend the assistant's hand, and the doctor aligns it so that he places his palm on the appearance of the joint, and pushes until it returns to its place. Nevertheless, you must look to see if it is properly aligned; then have the patient place the back of his hand on a table for the extension and resetting.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	 And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, let the patient place the back of his hand on the table, and let the physician put his hand on the appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	 If it (the dislocation) goes back now, that is good. If not, apply a plaster of soothing emollient for abscesses and let it stay without further manipulation.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	 And if he cannot bear it and you cannot set it right after several days, then the joint remains dislocated; and it does not harm the patient as long as his hand remains numb and cannot grasp anything. At that point, know that the nerves or arteries are severed, and there is no other remedy but to cauterize near the wound, which may be the only thing that works.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is healed, place the ointment that we mentioned on it, then bind and leave it for five days, then loosen it and leave it like that.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is any cracking sound, moisten it with warm water and rub it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	on the dislocation of the fingers of the hand.
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	 Sometimes the fingers of the hand dislocate on each side, sometimes at the back of the palm or the belly; then stretch out the finger, and push the dislocation towards its knuckles until it goes back in place, then hold the finger's head and bend it towards the side where it is disjoined; and leave it for 2 days, and then straighten it that day; and tie it up at night and untie it during the day, and make it move, and rebind it at night; and do this frequently until it becomes tight, and do the same if it is dislocated on the belly of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it heals; and do the same when it is dislocated from the other side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Here comes a new sentence to translate: "of the dislocation of the loin of the back" or "of the dislocation in the small of the back".
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the shininess (swelling) of the back or neck is dislocated, or if there are multiple dislocations, there is no cure, for death is near for the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	 And the signs are that stools leave suddenly without voluntary control, and cannot be held back, and often certain limbs become weak, or both thighs or both arms or one of them, and often the hips move in four ways; the one that moves at the back is called "hunched back"; the cure is to check if the hunchback has come from childhood: if it has, there is no cure or healing at all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	 And the one that comes from falling or being struck or similar things, ancient methods of cures say that there is no great benefit in all cases; but I have shortened it according to my intention and created various instruments for it.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	 I say that in the gout that comes to the front of the foot, there is no device nor health; and also that which comes directly on two sides, and cannot be cured except by the one who comes specifically to the back, as I say; and it is that the patient is stretched out on his face evenly, and has support beneath, so that he does not injure himself; then stick one stake in the ground deeply at the head, and another at the feet, and tie a rope underneath the patient's ankles, and another around the calves, and the knees, and the ankles; and two assistants know the ropes, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two stakes; and they are well tightened, the stakes as we have said, and the assistant places his palms on the spine forcefully, until it realigns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	 And if it does not return to its place with this treatment, take a board of three arms' length, and prop it up under the patient, and have the patient lie on his side, and put the head of the board under the affected area, then place the middle of the board on the spine; and have the physician place his feet on the other end of the board and press firmly until it returns to its place; and if you see it is necessary, do so with a device that turns by hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	 And have two stakes driven into the patient's head, one at arm's length and the other towards the feet, with a hand-span of space between each stake; and let there be a hole in each stake for the device to pass through, and have them firmly planted in the ground so that they do not move; and between each pair of stakes there should be one turning stake, on which the ropes turn, and have two small stakes of a hand-span in length for turning the device; and then tie the rope that is between the crossbars to the device towards the head, and the other rope towards the feet to the other device, and each assistant turns his device along the entire rope, and the master aligns the spine as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	 And when it is aligned, place a dessicative plaster with plenty of egg yolk on it, then the wool compresses, then an elongated stylet of a tablet three fingers long, which reaches the area of the gelatinous inflammation and the healthy part of the shoulder blade, then bind it with a ligature as we have said, and have the patient use gentle exercise until it is healed; and if any complication arises at the end of the healing process, one must administer softening and soothing medicines, with the stylet that I mentioned before; and sometimes a piece of wood is administered, and sometimes an appearance comes on the back spondylos of the spine, and one thinks it is a dislocation; but it is the bone that appears, for which one should not make any assumptions: perhaps it would lead to death.
des dislocations de la hainche	of hip dislocations.
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that the hip joints and the shoulder joints do not come out of place except by dislocations only, and not in the same way as other joints; and the hip joint comes out of place in four ways: inside and outside, and front and back; and more on the inside than elsewhere, and little out of place in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	 And the recognition of its dislocation is as follows: when you join the sick leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and the sick knee appears higher than the healthy one, and the sick person cannot bend their knee by the fire; and the place next to it is swollen with a abscess, because the hip comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of this, when it occurs in someone, is that these symptoms are contrary to those mentioned before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the sign of this when it occurs at the onset is that they extend their leg properly according to completion; nevertheless, they do not bend the knee without pain, and if they want to make it move, it cannot advance, and they retain their urine, and their ankles swell, and when they walk, they step on their heels.[translated by me]
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the sign of this when it occurs afterward is that they cannot stretch out or bend their knee, and that leg is more crooked than the other, and the ankle is swollen, and the head of the hip is located under the ribs.[translated by me]
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The reduction of this similar type of dislocation is that you should observe whether the dislocation is old and if it remains in its position, then there is no need for treatment, and one should not be overconfident.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in the case where the dislocation is fresh, and it is of the four types of dislocations, hurry to turn the joint, and stretch it inward and outward, and move it to the right and left; perhaps it will return, and no other treatment is needed.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	 And if it does not return in this manner, then you must prepare and strongly hold the leg with two hands, or with a ligament tied above the knee; and another assistant extends his hand above in such a way that he pushes his hands under the patient's arches, then gently tightens a soft ligament on the thigh; and another holds the end of the ligament; and they all pull up and down at once, so that the patient is lifted off the ground once and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of stretching is common to four similar things, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, that is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	 If not, then you must proceed with caution when the dislocation is on the outside, you must turn the patient onto their healthy side, then place the ligament on the root of the thigh and the groin area that is below the inguinal region, then pull the ligament up towards the inguinal region and the flank; then have another assistant grab hold of the patient's arms and strongly embrace the large thigh of the affected leg, extending it far outwards: in this way, it will return to its place now; and this method of dislocation is easier than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	 And if you cannot tighten it in this manner as we have said, then you should tie the patient's two feet together with a strong soft ligature at the heels and at the knees, and let the ailing leg be extended two digits more than the other; then let them hang from the head of a beam, and be above ground two arms' length; then command a minister to embrace the hip's head, and let there be another minister hanging with the patient, who firmly embraces the thigh, for the joints return quickly now.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	 And when the dislocation is outside, let the patient lie down as we have said in the one with gout, and tighten the ligature properly on the ailing leg, and on the foot as well; then place two splints, one at the head and one at the feet, then insert one splint between the patient's thighs in the shape; and have moist bandages placed around it so that it does not wound the patient, then each minister stretches out towards them, and let the doctor place his hand evenly on the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	 If it returns, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	 If not, place it on top, that is, a table, and press it as we have said in gout, and let the patient lie on the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, you must quickly stretch out the sick leg as I have said, and the surgeon should take care to be on the affected ankle, then press with one hand and pull down towards the knee with the other.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 And if the dislocation is on the outside, it should not be stretched downwards or lifted up from the ground. Instead, the patient should be positioned as if the hip was dislocated to the outside, as we have said in the lying position for two hips. Let them lie on their back and stretch out the limbs as we have said before, and press on the joint against the table. It is done correctly when the patient extends their legs and they are even. Then adjust the thighs and apply the poultice and bandage so that the hip does not move. Leave it like this for three or four days, then loosen the bandage and reapply the poultice. If you see that the legs are even, adjust the bandage as before and leave it for three days. Then loosen the bandage and let them walk gently until the limb is strengthened.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee dislocates in three ways: namely, inward and outward, and backward; it does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 And the signs are that you instruct the patient to bend his leg at his thigh, and if it does not reach his thigh, know that it is dislocated. And the restoration of all such cases is that you make the patient sit upright, and stretch out his leg if he can, and place your back against his face, and put his feet upon your feet; then take his knee with your palms, and pull it between your hands, then strongly bend the two sides of the knee; and another minister extends his foot, so that the knee comes back to its place, and the sign is that he easily bends his leg at his thigh; and apply the bandage, and bind the leg to the thigh, and keep them together strongly for three or four days, then unbind it; and let the patient not exert himself to go, until the limb is strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	 And if the limb is not in alignment, stretch it out strongly, as we have said in the treatment of contusions, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	for a dislocated ankle.
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The ankle can be partially dislocated, or fully dislocated both internally and externally.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	 And the sign is that the ankle is swollen, and it protrudes at the part where it is dislocated: the reduction is easy, and one should gently stretch it with their hands when it is moved slightly.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	 And when it is dislocated completely, you should make the patient sit upright, and hold their leg with your hands above the ankle; then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then with your left hand twice, then stretch it upwards, and place the foot nicely upward; and do this two times, as we have said, by pulling and stretching the foot; if it returns, it is good; if not, then begin the work again, for it will return; and if it cannot return in this way, then make the patient lie on their back on the ground, and firmly plant a stick in the ground between their thighs, and tie bandages around so that it does not hurt the patient; then hold the thigh with one hand, and another minister stretches the healthy leg with hands or a strap, which is tied to the neck of the foot; then each minister pulls evenly, and the stick should be firmly between the patient's thighs to hold the patient down when they are stretched; then place the dislocation between your hands, and another minister holds the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	 And when it is ready, put the poultice and wadding on, and bind it firmly, and tie the foot to the leg, and watch the nerves that are above the heel, so that the bandage is not too tight; then leave it for 2 or 3 days, and if the bandage loosens, bind it again; then untie it on the third or fourth day, and forbid the patient to walk for 4 days; and if he goes before this term, it is not certain that he will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses come, you should soothe them, as we have said elsewhere, until they are healed.
des dois	of the shoulders
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the shoulders are dislocated, they should be stretched out nicely without force, and this is an easy thing to do.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the dislocation is in any joint of the leg, you should make the patient sit upright on a flat surface or table, and place your foot on what is visible of the joints, then press firmly on your foot until it returns to its place; and when it is aligned, and nothing is apparent, place a two-chambered plate under the sole of the foot, then bind it firmly, and leave it for 3 days, then untie it; and let the patient rest until he is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together.
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	 When a wound comes with the dislocation, and one wants to restore it, often times the patient dies; so do not be presumptuous in the cure, if you are not wise in the art and have not practiced it long, and if you are not pitying and merciful and slow, not hasty; and use at the beginning soothing remedies for the swollen abscess, and leave the patient in God's hand, if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope, then reset the limb to its place, so that the swelling comes to it; and when the limb is in place, administer soothing remedies for the swollen abscess, and cure the wound as appropriate, with drying ointments; and if with the dislocation there is a fracture, and small bones are separated, then remove them, and do what we have said in simple illnesses; and beware of entering the path of fear, as I have said, for it will lead you astray according to your Creator, and for the safety of your art and body.
Amen	 Amen
